Returning to the Black Stone for Istilam after Tawaf Prayer
Ruling on touching the Black Stone after completing the two rak'ahs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on returning to the Black Stone after the two rak'ahs and explain the evidence from the hadith.

Core Idea
After tawaf prayer, returning to kiss the Black Stone is a sunnah, not wajib.

After completing the two rak'ahs of tawaf at Maqam Ibrahim, the pilgrim faces a choice: depart immediately or return to the Black Stone for a final touch. This lesson clarifies the Hanafi position on this act, drawing on the practice of the Prophet ﷺ and his companions. Understanding its status as a recommended sunnah helps avoid over- or under-commitment in hajj rites.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its timing
Locate the specific recommended action: after performing the two rak'ahs of tawaf, the pilgrim should return to the Black Stone and touch or kiss it.
This is a separate act from the initial istilam at the start of tawaf.
2
Examine the dalil
Read the hadith from Abd al-Rahman ibn Safwan: the Prophet and his companions touched the Kaaba from the door to al-Hatim after exiting. This indicates the act was performed after tawaf.
The hadith is ahad and zanni in both transmission and meaning.
3
Classify the hukm
From the hadith, the Hanafi school derives a sunnah (recommended) ruling, not wajib. The Prophet's action establishes desirability, not obligation.
No contrary evidence makes this wajib; the act is mustahabb.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۳۲۱) پھر لوٹ کر حجر اسود کا استلام کرے۔
تشریح : مقام ابراہیم پر نماز پڑھنے کے بعد اگر ہو سکے تو دوبارہ حجر اسود کو چومے۔
وجه : (۱) عن عبد الرحمن بن صفوان ... فرايت النبى الا الله قد خرج من الكعبة هو واصحابه قد استلموا البيت من الباب الى الحطيم وقد وضعوا خدودهم على البيت ورسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وسطهم. (ابوداودشریف، باب الملتزم، ص ۲۷۶، نمبر ۱۸۹۸ سفن سیتی ، باب الملتزم، ج خامس ،ص۱۵۰، نمبر ۹۳۳۱) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ آخر میں بھی بیت اللہ کو چومنا چاہئے۔
Translation: (1321) Then he returns and touches the Black Stone. Explanation: After praying at the Station of Ibrahim, if possible, he kisses the Black Stone again. Evidence: (1) From Abd al-Rahman ibn Safwan: '... I saw the Prophet come out of the Kaaba, he and his companions, they touched the House from the door to al-Hatim, and they placed their cheeks on the House, and the Messenger of Allah was in their midst.' (Sunan Abi Dawud, Chapter of al-Multazam, p. 276, no. 1898; Sunan al-Bayhaqi? Chapter of al-Multazam, Vol. 5, p. 150, no. 9331). From this hadith it is understood that at the end one should also kiss the House.
Source pages p. 359

Commentary
This passage covers a secondary act after the two rak'ahs. The matn instructs: 'Then he returns and touches the Black Stone.' The commentary explains that after the two rak'ahs at Maqam Ibrahim, the pilgrim should go back to the Black Stone and kiss it if possible, or touch it. The proof is a hadith describing the Prophet and his companions touching the Kaaba from the door to al-Hatim and placing their cheeks on it. This act, known as iltizam (embracing the Kaaba), is recommended after tawaf. The Hanafi school considers this as mustahabb (recommended), not obligatory.

Key Terms
التزام (iltizam): Embracing the Kaaba between the door and al-Hatim, placing the chest and cheeks against it, as a form of devotion after tawaf.
حطيم (al-Hatim): The semicircular wall adjacent to the Kaaba; part of the original Kaaba structure.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
After performing the two rak'ahs of tawaf, what does the Hanafi text recommend doing?
A) Returning to the Black Stone and touching it.
B) Proceeding directly to Safa.
C) Performing an additional tawaf.
D) Leaving the mosque.

Key Takeaway
Returning to the Black Stone after the two rak'ahs is a recommended sunnah in the Hanafi school, based on the Prophet's practice.

Tawaf al-Qudum is Sunnah for the Afaqi
Ruling on the arrival tawaf for pilgrims coming from outside Mecca

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling of Tawaf al-Qudum for the afaqi and explain the proof from the hadith of Ibn Umar.

Core Idea
Tawaf al-Qudum is a sunnah for pilgrims from outside Mecca, like greeting the mosque upon arrival.

This lesson clarifies the Hanafi ruling on Tawaf al-Qudum, the arrival circumambulation performed by pilgrims entering Mecca. While many assume it must be obligatory, the Hanafi school classifies it as a confirmed sunnah for those coming from outside the Haram. The proof comes from a hadith where Ibn Umar references the Prophet's practice as the standard.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? Identify Tawaf al-Qudum and its hukm level for the afaqi.
The act is the arrival tawaf performed upon entering Mecca in ihram for Hajj.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite? The hadith of Ibn Umar in Sahih Muslim is the primary evidence.
The hadith is a single narration (ahad), so its thubut is zanni.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How exactly does this hadith prove that Tawaf al-Qudum is sunnah and not wajib? Ibn Umar uses the Prophet's action as a model, implying desirability, not obligation.
The Prophet performed it, but there is no command indicating wujub.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Is there any disagreement? Other schools also consider it sunnah, but the Hanafis emphasize the analogy to greeting the mosque (tahiyyat al-masjid).
The practical outcome is similar across schools, but the rationale differs.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi position
Why is the Hanafi position considered correct? The text compares it to tahiyyat al-masjid, which is sunnah, and the hadith supports this level.
The authority_weight is zahir al-riwayah, and all Hanafi imams agree.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۳۲۲) به طواف قدوم ہے، یہ آفاقی کے لئے سنت ہے۔
تشریح : مکہ مکرمہ سے باہر سے آنے والوں کو آفاقی ، کہتے ہیں، چونکہ وہ باہر سے آتے ہیں اس لئے تحیۃ المسجد کی طرح طواف قدوم سنت ہے۔
وجه : (۱) یہ طواف واجب نہیں ہے سنت ہے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ سأل رجـل ابـن عـمـر أطوف بالبيت و قد احرمت بالحج ؟ ..... ثم قال رأينا رسول الله الا الله أحرم بالحج و طاف بالبيت و سعی بین الصفا و المروة ، فسنة الله وسنة رسوله أحق أن يتبع من سنة فلان ان كنت صادقا ؟ . (مسلم شریف، باب استحباب طواف القدوم للحاج واسعى بعده ص ۴۰۵ نمبر ۲۹۹۸/۱۲۳۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ طواف قدوم سنت ہے، واجب نہیں۔
Translation: (1322) This is Tawaf al-Qudum, and it is sunnah for the afaqi. Explanation: Those who come from outside Mecca are called afaqi. Since they come from outside, tawaf al-qudum is sunnah like greeting the mosque. Evidence: (1) This tawaf is not wajib, it is sunnah. Its proof is this hadith: 'A man asked Ibn Umar: Should I perform tawaf around the House when I have entered ihram for Hajj? ... Then he said: We saw the Messenger of Allah enter ihram for Hajj, perform tawaf around the House, and do sa'i between Safa and Marwa. So the Sunnah of Allah and the Sunnah of His Messenger are more deserving to be followed than the practice of so-and-so, if you are truthful?' (Sahih Muslim, Chapter of Recommendation of Tawaf al-Qudum for the Pilgrim and Sa'i After It, p. 405, no. 2998/1233). In this hadith, tawaf al-qudum is sunnah, not wajib.
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This passage defines Tawaf al-Qudum (the arrival tawaf) as a sunnah for the afaqi — a pilgrim coming from outside the Miqat boundaries of Mecca. The Hanafi school compares it to greeting the mosque (tahiyyat al-masjid) upon entering; it is not obligatory but recommended. The proof is a hadith where Ibn Umar cites the Prophet's practice as the benchmark. The text explicitly states it is not wajib but sunnah, correcting any misconception that it might be obligatory for all pilgrims.

Key Terms
طواف القدوم (tawaf al-qudum): The tawaf performed immediately upon entering Mecca by a pilgrim coming from outside, before other rites.
آفاقي (afaqi): A person coming from outside the boundaries of the Haram, specifically from beyond the Miqat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling of Tawaf al-Qudum for a pilgrim coming from outside Mecca?
A) It is wajib.
B) It is sunnah.
C) It is fard.
D) It is mubah.

Key Takeaway
Tawaf al-Qudum is a confirmed sunnah for pilgrims from outside Mecca, not an obligation, based on the Prophet's practice.

intermediate

Proceeding to Safa and Supplications There
Ruling on recommended dhikr at Safa during Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah actions at Safa during sa'i and identify the proof from the hadith of Jabir and Quran 2:158.

Core Idea
At Safa, the pilgrim stands, faces the Kaaba, and recites prescribed dhikr as modelled by the Prophet.

This lesson covers the recommended acts at Safa hill, the starting point of sa'i. The Hanafi school details specific dhikr based on the Prophet's practice. Understanding these sunnah acts enriches the ritual and follows the Prophetic model.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being described? The pilgrim ascends Safa, faces the Kaaba, and recites takbir, tahlil, talbiyah, and supplications. The ruling is sunnah (recommended), not wajib.
Sa'i itself is wajib, but these details are sunnah.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The main proof is the hadith of Jabir (Sahih Muslim, Sunan Abi Dawud) describing the Prophet's actions at Safa. The Quranic verse (2:158) establishes Safa and Marwa as symbols.
The hadith provides specific wording and sequence.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove the ruling? The Prophet's action is taken as a model; the Hanafi school considers his practice as evidence for sunnah. The verse does not prescribe dhikr, but the hadith supplements.
Hanafi usul uses ahad hadith for sunnah, not fard.
4
Note cross-madhhab considerations
Other schools may have slightly different sequences or additional dhikr. The Hanafi position is well-supported and the ikhtilaf is legitimate.
Differences are minor and do not affect validity.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, a pilgrim should stand on Safa, face the Kaaba (or approximate direction), recite the phrases, and make personal supplication with raised hands.
Omitting these does not invalidate sa'i but loses reward.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۳۲۳) پھر صفا کی طرف نکلے اس پر چڑھ کر کھڑا ہو یہاں تک کہ بیت اللہ نظر آئے ہتکبیر تہلیل ، تلبیہ کہتے ہوئے ، درود شریف پڑھتے ہوئے ، ہاتھ اٹھا کر دعا کے ساتھ استقبال کرے۔
تشریح : پھر صفا پہاڑی کی طرف جائے ، اس پر اس طرح کھڑا ہو کہ بیت اللہ نظر آئے ، آج کل سامنے دیوار حائل ہے اس لئے بیت اللہ نظر نہیں آتا ، البتہ اس طرح کھڑا ہو کہ دیوار نہ ہو تو بیت اللہ نظر آجائے] بیت اللہ کا استقبال کرے، تکبیر پڑھے، لاالہ الا اللہ پڑھے، تلبیہ پڑھے، درود شریف پڑھے اور ہاتھ اٹھا کر دعا کرے۔
وجه : (۱) حدیث یہ ہے۔ قال دخلنا على جابر بن عبد الله ... ثم خرج من الباب الى الصفا فلما دنى من الصفا قرء ( ان الصفا والمروة من شعائر (الله نبدأ بما بدء الله به فبدأ بالصفا فرقی علیه حتی رای البیت فاستقبل القبلة فوحد الله وكبره وقال لا اله الا الله وحده لا شريك له له الملك وله الحمد وهو على كل شيء قدير لا اله الا الله وحده انجز وعده ونصر عبده وهزم الاحزاب وحده ثم دعا بين ذلك قال مثل هذا ثلاث مرات ثم نزل الى المروة . (مسلم شریف ، باب حجتہ النبی الله ص ۵۱۳، نمبر ۲۹۵۰/۱۲۱۸ / ابو داؤد شریف ، باب صفته حجتہ النبی ص ۲۷۷، نمبر ۱۹۰۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ صفا پہاڑی پر آکر تکبیر و تجلیل کرے اور دعائیں کرے (۲) اس کی تائید اس آیت سے بھی ہوتی ہے۔ ان الصفا والمروة من شعائر الله فمن حج البيت او اعتمر فلا جناح عليه ان
Translation: (1323) Then he goes out towards Safa, ascends it and stands until he sees the House, saying takbir, tahlil, talbiyah, reciting salawat on the Prophet, raising his hands in supplication, facing it. Explanation: Then he goes to the hill of Safa, and stands on it in such a way that the House is visible. Nowadays there is a wall in front, so the House is not visible; however, he stands so that if there were no wall, the House would be visible. He faces the House, says takbir, says La ilaha illa Allah, says talbiyah, recites salawat, raises his hands and makes supplication. Evidence: (1) The hadith is: He said: 'We entered upon Jabir ibn Abdullah... then he came out of the door to Safa, and when he approached Safa he recited: 'Indeed, Safa and Marwa are among the symbols of Allah.' (We begin with what Allah began with.) So he began with Safa, climbed it until he saw the House, faced the Qibla, declared the oneness of Allah and magnified Him, and said: 'La ilaha illa Allah, alone, no partner, His is the kingdom, His is the praise, and He is over all things competent. La ilaha illa Allah, He fulfilled His promise, gave victory to His servant, and alone defeated the confederates.' Then he supplicated between that. He said this three times, then descended to Marwa.' (Sahih Muslim, Chapter of the Prophet's Hajj, p. 513, no. 2950/1218; Sunan Abi Dawud, Chapter of the Description of the Prophet's Hajj, p. 277, no. 1905). From this hadith it is understood that upon coming to the hill of Safa, he should say takbir and tahmid and make supplications. (2) This is also supported by the verse: 'Indeed, Safa and Marwa are among the symbols of Allah. So whoever performs Hajj to the House or performs 'umrah, there is no blame upon him...' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:158).
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This passage describes the recommended actions upon reaching Safa hill to begin sa'i. The matn instructs: go to Safa, ascend, face the Kaaba, and recite specific dhikr. The commentary clarifies that the pilgrim should stand where they can see the Kaaba; if a wall obstructs, they imagine it. The dhikr includes takbir (Allahu Akbar), tahlil (La ilaha illa Allah), talbiyah (Labbayk...), salawat upon the Prophet, and personal supplication with raised hands. The proof is the detailed hadith of Jabir describing the Prophet's sa'i, where he recited specific phrases three times. Additionally, the Quranic verse (2:158) is cited, confirming that Safa and Marwa are among Allah's symbols. The Hanafi school derives that these acts at Safa are sunnah, part of the sa'i ritual.

Key Terms
صفا (Safa): One of the two hills near the Kaaba; the starting point of sa'i between Safa and Marwa.
تهليل (tahlil): The phrase 'La ilaha illa Allah' (There is no god but Allah).
تلبیة (talbiyah): The chant 'Labbayk Allahumma labbayk...' recited during ihram and at certain points in Hajj, including at Safa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi text, what should a pilgrim do upon reaching Safa hill before beginning sa'i?
A) Immediately begin walking towards Marwa.
B) Stand, face the Kaaba, recite takbir, tahlil, talbiyah, and make supplication.
C) Perform two rak'ahs of prayer.
D) Sacrifice an animal.

Key Takeaway
At Safa, the sunnah is to face the Kaaba and recite dhikr as the Prophet did, making sa'i more complete.

Tawaf al-Qudum is Sunnah for the Afaqi
Ruling with proof that Tawaf al-Qudum is sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Tawaf al-Qudum for the afaqi and explain the evidence from the hadith of Ibn Umar.

Core Idea
Tawaf al-Qudum is a recommended sunnah, not an obligation, for those entering Mecca from outside.

In this passage, the author clarifies the legal status of Tawaf al-Qudum, the tawaf performed upon arrival in Mecca by pilgrims coming from outside the city (afaqi). The Hanafi school holds it to be a sunnah mu'akkadah, analogous to the greeting of the mosque (tahiyyat al-masjid). We will examine the proof from the hadith of Ibn Umar that establishes this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Tawaf al-Qudum is the circumambulation performed upon arrival in Mecca by a pilgrim coming from outside the Haram (afaqi). The author states it is sunnah (recommended), not wajib (obligatory).
The ruling depends on the pilgrim's origin; it only applies to those outside Mecca.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith of Ibn Umar (narrated in Muslim) where a man asks about performing tawaf after assuming ihram. Ibn Umar replies by describing the Prophet's practice.
The hadith is quoted with the key phrase 'Sunnah of Allah and His Messenger is more deserving to be followed'.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith shows the Prophet performed Tawaf al-Qudum but does not command it with an imperative. The term 'sunnah' indicates a recommended practice, not an obligation.
In Hanafi usul, a mere action of the Prophet without a command indicates sunnah, not wajib.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
All schools generally agree Tawaf al-Qudum is sunnah. The Hanafi emphasis is on its non-obligatory nature, distinguishing it from wajib acts.
Some may think it is wajib because of its importance, but the text clarifies otherwise.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that Tawaf al-Qudum is sunnah mu'akkadah for the afaqi. This is the ruling from Zahir al-Riwayah.
No intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is recorded; the three imams agree.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل تركيب افعال الحج (۱۳۲۲) وهذا طواف القدوم وهو سنة للآفاقى وجه : (۱) عن عبد الرحمن بن صفوان ... فرايت النبى الا الله قد خرج من الكعبة هو واصحابه قد استلموا البيت من الباب الى الحطيم وقد وضعوا خدودهم على البيت ورسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وسطهم. (ابوداودشریف، باب الملتزم، ص ۲۷۶، نمبر ۱۸۹۸ سفن سیتی ، باب الملتزم، ج خامس ،ص۱۵۰، نمبر ۹۳۳۱) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ آخر میں بھی بیت اللہ کو چومنا چاہئے۔ ترجمه : (۱۳۲۲) به طواف قدوم ہے، یہ آفاقی کے لئے سنت ہے۔ تشریح : مکہ مکرمہ سے باہر سے آنے والوں کو آفاقی ، کہتے ہیں، چونکہ وہ باہر سے آتے ہیں اس لئے تحیۃ المسجد کی طرح طواف قدوم سنت ہے۔ وجه : (۱) یہ طواف واجب نہیں ہے سنت ہے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ سأل رجـل ابـن عـمـر أطوف بالبيت و قد احرمت بالحج ؟ ..... ثم قال رأينا رسول الله الا الله أحرم بالحج و طاف بالبيت و سعی بین الصفا و المروة ، فسنة الله وسنة رسوله أحق أن يتبع من سنة فلان ان كنت صادقا ؟ . (مسلم شریف، باب استحباب طواف القدوم للحاج واسعى بعده ص ۴۰۵ نمبر ۲۹۹۸/۱۲۳۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ طواف قدوم سنت ہے، واجب نہیں۔
Section on the composition of the actions of Hajj (1322) This is the Tawaf of arrival (Qudum), and it is sunnah for the Afaqi (one coming from outside Mecca). Evidence (1): From Abdur Rahman bin Safwan... I saw the Prophet (peace be upon him) come out of the Kaaba, he and his companions, they had touched the House from the door to al-Hatim, placing their cheeks on the House, with the Messenger of Allah in their midst. (Abu Dawud, Bab al-Multazam, p. 276, no. 1898) From this hadith it is known that at the end one should also kiss the House of Allah. Translation: (1322) This is Tawaf al-Qudum; it is sunnah for the Afaqi. Explanation: Those coming from outside Mecca are called Afaqi. Since they come from outside, Tawaf al-Qudum is sunnah like Tahiyyat al-Masjid. Evidence (1): This tawaf is not wajib but sunnah; its proof is this hadith: A man asked Ibn Umar: Should I perform tawaf around the House when I have assumed ihram for Hajj? ... Then he said: We saw the Messenger of Allah assume ihram for Hajj, perform tawaf around the House, and perform sa'i between Safa and Marwah. The sunnah of Allah and His Messenger is more deserving to be followed than the sunnah of so-and-so if you are truthful. (Muslim, Bab Istihbab Tawaf al-Qudum...) This hadith states that Tawaf al-Qudum is sunnah, not wajib.
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on Tawaf al-Qudum, which is the tawaf performed upon arrival in Mecca by those coming from outside the city (afaqi). The author begins by stating that it is sunnah (recommended), not wajib (obligatory). He then provides two pieces of evidence. The first evidence is a hadith about the Prophet and his companions kissing the Kaaba at the Multazam, which seems to support the practice of kissing the Kaaba at the end of tawaf, but the author uses it to emphasize the importance of the House. The second evidence is a stronger hadith from Muslim: a man asked Ibn Umar about performing tawaf after assuming ihram, and Ibn Umar replied that the Prophet did so, and that the Sunnah is more worthy of being followed. This directly proves that Tawaf al-Qudum is a recommended practice, not an obligation. The commentary further explains that the ruling depends on whether the pilgrim is from outside Mecca (afaqi) or from within. It is likened to the greeting of the mosque (tahiyyat al-masjid), which is also sunnah. The Hanafi school holds that Tawaf al-Qudum is sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah) for the afaqi, and it is not wajib.

Key Terms
طواف القدوم (Tawaf al-Qudum): The circumambulation performed upon arrival in Mecca by a pilgrim coming from outside the city.
آفاقی (Afaqi): A person who comes from outside the boundaries of the Haram (Mecca) for Hajj or Umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Sunnah Actions on Safa: Climbing and Supplication
Ruling with proof on sunnah actions at Safa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah actions on Safa and identify the proofs that establish them.

Core Idea
Climbing Safa to see the Kaaba and reciting prescribed remembrances is sunnah muakkadah, rooted in the Prophet's practice.

This lesson details the recommended actions when reaching Safa during Hajj or Umrah. The author provides four pieces of evidence—the hadith of Jabir, a Quranic verse, another hadith, and a companion statement—to demonstrate that these actions are sunnah, not obligatory. Understanding these proofs helps the pilgrim follow the Prophet's example with confidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the set of actions upon reaching Safa: climbing until the Kaaba is visible, facing it, and reciting takbir, tahlil, talbiyah, blessings on the Prophet, and supplication with raised hands. The ruling is sunnah muakkadah (confirmed sunnah).
The term 'sunnah' here indicates a recommended practice that the Prophet consistently performed.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The main proof is the hadith of Jabir (narrated by Muslim and Abu Dawud) describing the Prophet's actions on Safa. It shows he climbed until he saw the House, faced the qiblah, said takbir and tahlil, and made supplication three times.
This hadith is ahad (single-narrator) but accepted as evidence for sunnah acts.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith directly reports the Prophet's practice (fi'l). In Hanafi usul, the Prophet's action (fi'l) indicates istihbab (recommendation) unless there is evidence of obligation. Therefore, these actions are sunnah.
The repetition three times emphasizes that the supplication is a distinct sunnah, not a one-time act.
4
Consider supporting evidence
The Quranic verse (2:158) establishes the legitimacy of sa'i. Another hadith from Nasa'i specifies climbing until seeing the House then saying takbir. The statement of Ibn Abbas lists Safa as one of seven places to raise hands. These reinforce the sunnah status.
The companion statement (qawl sahabi) is a source of evidence in Hanafi fiqh.
5
Evaluate common misunderstandings
Some may think seeing the Kaaba on Safa is a condition (shart) for sa'i validity. However, it is merely sunnah; if the view is obstructed (e.g., by a wall), the pilgrim still performs sa'i validly without the elevation.
The commentary clarifies that the sunnah is to climb until one would see the Kaaba if no obstruction existed.

Then you go out to as-Safa, climb it, and stand upon it until you see the House (Kaaba), then you face it, saying takbir, tahlil, talbiyah, sending blessings, supplicating, and you raise your hands outstretched. Evidence (1): The hadith: We entered upon Jabir ibn Abdullah... Then he went out from the door to as-Safa, and when he approached as-Safa he recited: 'Indeed as-Safa and al-Marwah are among the symbols of Allah. We begin with what Allah began with.' So he began with as-Safa, climbed it until he saw the House, faced the qiblah, pronounced the oneness of Allah, said takbir, and said: 'There is no god but Allah alone, no partner, His is the dominion, His is the praise, and He is over all things competent. There is no god but Allah alone, He fulfilled His promise, aided His servant, and defeated the confederates alone.' Then he supplicated during that. He said: He did this three times, then descended to al-Marwah. (Muslim, Bab Hajjat al-Nabi, p. 513, no. 2950/1218; Abu Dawud, Bab sifat Hajjat al-Nabi, p. 277, no. 1905) From this hadith it is known that upon reaching as-Safa, one should say takbir and glorification and make supplications. (2) This is also supported by the verse: 'Indeed as-Safa and al-Marwah are among the symbols of Allah. So whoever makes Hajj to the House or performs Umrah, there is no blame upon him for making tawaf (sa'i) around them.' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:158) From this verse it is known that sa'i between Safa and Marwah should be performed. (3) Climb as-Safa enough to see the House, then face the House and recite supplications. There is a hadith: We were told by Jabir that the Messenger of Allah climbed as-Safa until, when he looked at the House, he said takbir. (Nasa'i, Bab mawdu' al-qiyam 'ala al-Safa, p. 409, no. 2974) From this hadith it is known that one should climb as-Safa until the House becomes visible, then say takbir etc. (4) Raising the hands: for this there is the statement of a companion: From Ibn Abbas, he said: 'Hands are not raised except in seven places: when standing for prayer, when seeing the House, on as-Safa, on al-Marwah, at Arafat, at Muzdalifah, and at the Jamarat.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, Man kana yarfa' yadayhi fi awwal takbira thumma la ya'ud, vol. 1, p. 214, no. 2450; Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab raf' al-yadayn idha ra'a al-bayt, vol. 5, p. 117, no. 921) From this effect it is known that when climbing as-Safa and al-Marwah, one should raise hands and supplicate. Translation: (1323) Then go out to as-Safa, climb it, stand upon it until you see the House, then face it saying takbir, tahlil, talbiyah, sending blessings, supplicating with hands raised. Explanation: Then go towards the mountain of as-Safa, stand in such a way that the House is visible. Nowadays, there is a wall in front preventing sight, so if one stands such that there is no wall, the House would become visible. Face the House, say takbir, recite la ilaha illallah, recite talbiyah, send blessings, and raise hands in supplication.
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This passage details the prescribed actions upon reaching the hill of Safa during Hajj or Umrah. The author begins by instructing the pilgrim to go to Safa, climb it, stand until the Kaaba is visible, face it, and then engage in various remembrances: saying Allahu Akbar (takbir), La ilaha illallah (tahlil), the talbiyah (Labbayk...), sending blessings upon the Prophet, and making supplication with raised hands. Four pieces of evidence support these actions. First, the detailed hadith of Jabir, which describes the Prophet's own actions on Safa: he climbed until he saw the Kaaba, faced the qiblah, declared Allah's oneness, praised Him, and made supplication, repeating this three times. Second, the Qur'anic verse (2:158) establishes the legitimacy of sa'i between Safa and Marwah. Third, another hadith from Jabir (via Nasa'i) specifies that the Prophet climbed until he could see the Kaaba, then said takbir. Fourth, the saying of Ibn Abbas lists seven places where raising hands is sunnah, including on Safa and Marwah. The commentary in Urdu clarifies that if a wall obstructs the view of the Kaaba (as in the current construction), one should stand as if the wall were not there. All these actions are sunnah, and the Hanafi school follows this practice.

Key Terms
الصفا (as-Safa): A small hill near the Kaaba in Mecca, one of the two points between which sa'i is performed.
تہلیل (tahlil): The utterance of 'La ilaha illallah' (There is no god but Allah).
تلبیہ (talbiyah): The recitation of 'Labbayk Allahumma labbayk...' during Hajj and Umrah.

Key Takeaway

Method of Sa'i: Walking and Hastening
Ruling on walking normally and hastening between the green markers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two modes of walking during sa'i and identify the specific section where hastening is sunnah, citing the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Hasten only between the green markers; walk calmly elsewhere during sa'i.

During sa'i between Safa and Marwah, the pilgrim alternates between two paces: calm walking and brisk hastening. This lesson clarifies exactly where each is prescribed, based on the practice of the Prophet ﷺ and the example of Lady Hajar. Understanding this distinction ensures your sa'i follows the sunnah correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the method of walking during sa'i. The ruling is that walking calmly on the open stretches is sunnah, and hastening between the two green markers is also sunnah (muakkadah).
The ruling applies specifically to the male pilgrim; women do not hasten.
2
Locate the dalil
The evidence is the hadith of Jabir ibn Abdullah (Muslim, Abu Dawud) describing the Prophet's sa'i.
The hadith is ahad but accepted as sound (sahih).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's action of hastening in the valley (batan al-wadi) and walking normally elsewhere demonstrates the sunnah. The word 'sa'a' (hastened) indicates a brisk pace, not running.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
This practice is agreed upon (muttafaq alayh) among the madhahib; there is no significant dispute.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is the mufta bihi: hastening between the green markers is sunnah, and the rest of sa'i is normal walking.
This is based on zahir al-riwayah.

(مسلم شريف ، باب حجتہ النبی ، ص ۵۱۳، نمبر ۲۹۵۰/۱۲۱۸ رابوداؤد شریف، باب صفته حجته النبي ص ۲۷۷، نمبر ۱۹۰۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ بطن وادی میں تیز قدم چلے اور باقی مقامات پر اپنی حالت پر چلے ۔ اور تکبیر تہلیل اور دعا ایسا ہی کرے جیسا کہ صفا پر کی تھی۔ لغت : تحبط بحبط سے مشتق ہے، نیچے اترنا۔ ھدیہ : وقار کے ساتھ چلنا، اپنی ہیئت پر چلنا بطن الوادی وادی کہتے ہیں نشیبی زمین کو بطن الوادی کا ترجمہ ہے وادی کا پیٹ ، یہاں مراد ہے وادی کے درمیان کا حصہ ، صفا اور مروہ پہاڑی کے درمیان وادی تھی ، اور اس وادی کے درمیان میں دو ہرے رنگ کے کھمبے لگے ہوئے ہیں جسکو میلین اخضرین ، کہتے ہیں ان میلین اخضرین کے درمیان تھوڑی تیزی سے چلے یہ سنت ہے۔ حیا: تیز دوڑنا۔
Then you descend towards al-Marwah in a calm manner. When you reach the bottom of the valley (Batan al-Wadi), you hasten between the two green markers with brisk walking. When you have passed it, you walk calmly until you reach Marwah and climb it. Translation: (1324) Then walk towards Marwah calmly. When you reach the bottom of the valley, hasten between the two green markers. When you pass the bottom of the valley, then walk calmly until you reach Marwah and climb it. Explanation: After finishing the supplications on Safa, proceed towards the mountain of Marwah walking normally. However, when you reach the two green markers, hasten (run) briskly because Lady Hajar (peace be upon her) ran here. Then after passing the two green markers, walk calmly until you climb Marwah. Evidence: (1) In this hadith: We entered upon Jabir ibn Abdullah... He said: He did this three times, then descended to Marwah. When his feet settled in the bottom of the valley, he hastened until his feet went up, then walked until he came to Marwah and did on Marwah as he did on Safa. (Muslim, Bab Hajjat al-Nabi, p. 513, no. 2950/1218; Abu Dawud, Bab sifat Hajjat al-Nabi, p. 277, no. 1905) From this hadith it is known that in the bottom of the valley one should walk quickly, and in the rest of the places walk at one's normal pace. And one should recite takbir, tahlil, and supplications as done on Safa. Glossary: 'Tahabbat' is derived from 'hubb' meaning descent. 'Hadyah' means walking with dignity, keeping one's normal gait. 'Batan al-Wadi' means the bottom of the valley; here it refers to the middle section between Safa and Marwah where there is a valley. In this valley, two green pillars are installed, called 'al-Milayn al-Akhdarayn'. Between these two green pillars, one should walk briskly; this is sunnah. 'Hiththa' means brisk running.
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This passage describes the method of walking during sa'i from Safa to Marwah. The pilgrim should walk calmly (on hay'ah) from Safa until reaching the bottom of the valley (batan al-wadi). In that valley, between two green markers (milayn akhdarayn), the pilgrim should hasten (sa'y hathith) — a brisk walk or light jog. After passing that section, he returns to normal walking until climbing Marwah. The evidence is the hadith of Jabir, which states that when the Prophet's feet settled in the valley, he hastened, and then walked normally again. The commentary explains that this is based on the action of Lady Hajar, who ran between the hills. The glossary clarifies terms: 'tahabbat' means to descend, 'hadyah' means dignified walking, 'batan al-wadi' is the valley floor, and 'hiththa' is rapid walking. This is an established sunnah in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
بطن الوادی (Batan al-Wadi): The middle part of the valley between Safa and Marwah where the two green markers are located.
میلین اخضرین (al-Milayn al-Akhdarayn): Two green pillars (or markers) placed in the valley area between Safa and Marwah, indicating the section where one should hasten.
سعی (sa'y): In this context, brisk walking or light jogging, especially in the designated part of the valley.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The sunnah of sa'i is to walk calmly except between the two green markers in the valley, where men hasten briskly.

The Method of Sa'i Between Safa and Marwah
Describes the actions of sa'i with proof from hadith and lexical notes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the Hanafi method of sa'i between Safa and Marwah and explain the proof for running between the two green markers and the counting of rounds.

Core Idea
Sa'i is wajib; its specific actions are proven by the Prophet's practice, especially running between the two green markers.

The ritual of sa'i commemorates the actions of Lady Hagar. This lesson examines the precise manner of performing sa'i as established by the Hanafi school from the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him). The passage from Thamaratun Najah details the actions on Safa and Marwah, the running between the green markers, and the counting of rounds. We will work through the legal proofs and the intra-madhhab dispute regarding the completion point of a round.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the legal status of sa'i? It is wajib. The actions described (running, supplications) are sunnah or mustahabb.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith of Jabir (Muslim, Abu Dawud) describing the Prophet's actions during the Farewell Hajj.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's fi'l (action) indicates the recommended manner: he walked calmly except in the valley where he ran between the two green markers.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is a dispute about when a round (shawt) is completed. The Hanafi school counts each traverse as a round, while others count a complete back-and-forth as one round.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) in the school, based on the apparent meaning of the hadith.

Source Text

فصل تركيب افعال الحج
ثمرة النجاح جلد ٢ حتى ترى البيت فيستقبله مكبرا مهللا ملبيا مصليا داعيا وترفع یدیک مبسوطتين(۱۳۲۴) ثم تهبط نحو المروة على هيئة فاذا وصل بطن الوادى سعى بين الميلين الاخضرين سعيا حثيثا فاذا تجاوز يطوف بهما (آیت ۱۵۸ ، سورۃ البقرۃ ۲) اس آیت سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ صفا اور مروہ کے درمیان سعی کرنا چاہئے ۔ (۳) صفا پر اتنا چڑھے کہ بیت اللہ نظر آنے لگے، چنانچہ بیت اللہ کی طرف استقبال کر کے دعائیں پڑھے۔ حدیث میں ہے۔ حـدثـنــا جـابـر ان رسول الله رقى على الصفا حتى اذا نظر الى البيت كبر (نسائی شریف، باب موضع القیام علی الصفاج ثانی ص ۴۰۹، نمبر ۲۹۷۴) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ صفا پر اتنا چڑھے کہ بیت اللہ نظر آنے لگے پھر تکبیر وغیرہ کہے ۔ (۴) ہاتھ اٹھائے اس کے لئے یہ قول صحابی ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال : لا ترفع الأيدى الا في سبع مواطن : اذا قام الى الصلوة [۲] و اذا رأى البيت [۳] و على الصفا [۴] و المروة [۵] و في عرفات [۶] و في جمع [۷] و عند الجمار ۔ (مصنف ابن ابی شبيبة ، من كان يرفع يديه في اول تكبيرة ثم لا يعود، ج اول ، ص ۲۱۴، نمبر ۲۴۵۰ رسنن بیھقی ، باب رفع الیدین اذار کی البیت ، ج خامس، ص ۱۱۷، نمبر ۹۲۱) اس اثر میں ہے کہ صفا اور مروہ پر چڑھے تو ہاتھ اٹھائے ، اور دعا کرے۔ ترجمه : (۱۳۲۴) پھر مروہ کی طرف اطمینان سے چلے، جب بطن وادی کے پاس پہنچے تو میلین اخضرین کے درمیان میں تیزی سے دوڑے، جب بطن وادی سے گذر جائے تو پھر اطمینان سے چلے، یہاں تک کہ مروہ پر آئے ، اور اس پر چڑھے۔ تشریح : صفا پر دعا وغیرہ سے فارغ ہونے کے بعد مروہ پہاڑی کی طرف چلے اور اور جس طرح وہ عام حالت میں چلتا ہے اسی طرح اطمینان سے چلے لیکن جب میلین اخضرین کے پاس پہنچے تو تیزی سے دوڑے، کیونکہ حضرت ہاجرہ علیہ السلام یہاں دوڑیں تھیں، پھر جب میلین اخضرین سے گزر جائے تو اطمینان سے چلے، یہاں تک کہ مروہ پہاڑی پر چڑھ جائے۔
وجه : (۱) اس حدیث میں ہے ۔ قال دخلنا على جابر بن عبد الله ... قال مثل هذا ثلاث مرات ثم نزل الى المروة . حتى اذا انصبت قدماه في بطن الوادى سعى حتى اذا صعدتا مشى حتى أتى المروة ففعل على المروحة كما فعل على الصفا. (مسلم شريف ، باب حجتہ النبی ، ص ۵۱۳، نمبر ۲۹۵۰/۱۲۱۸ رابوداؤد شریف، باب صفته حجته النبي ص ۲۷۷، نمبر ۱۹۰۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ بطن وادی میں تیز قدم چلے اور باقی مقامات پر اپنی حالت پر چلے ۔ اور تکبیر تہلیل اور دعا ایسا ہی کرے جیسا کہ صفا پر کی تھی۔
لغت : تحبط بحبط سے مشتق ہے، نیچے اترنا۔ ھدیہ : وقار کے ساتھ چلنا، اپنی ہیئت پر چلنا بطن الوادی وادی کہتے ہیں نشیبی زمین کو بطن الوادی کا ترجمہ ہے وادی کا پیٹ ، یہاں مراد ہے وادی کے درمیان کا حصہ ، صفا اور مروہ پہاڑی کے درمیان وادی تھی ، اور اس وادی کے درمیان میں دو ہرے رنگ کے کھمبے لگے ہوئے ہیں جسکو میلین اخضرین ، کہتے ہیں ان میلین اخضرین کے درمیان تھوڑی تیزی سے چلے یہ سنت ہے۔ حیا: تیز دوڑنا۔
بطن الوادى مشى على هيئة حتى يأتى المروة فيصعد عليها (۱۳۲۵ ) ويفعل كما فعل على الصفا يستقبل البيت مكبّرا مهلّلا مُلبّيا مصليا داعيا باسطا يديه نحو السماء وهذا شوط (١٣٢٦ ) ثم يعود قاصدا الى الصفافاذا وصل الى الميلين الاخضرين سعى ثم مشى على هيئة حتى يأتى الصفا فيصعد ترجمه : (۱۳۲۵) اور وہی کام کرے جو صفا پر کیا، بیت اللہ کا استقبال کرے، تکبیر تہلیل ، تلبیہ، درود، ہاتھ آسمان کی طرف پھیلا کر دعا مانگے ، یہ ایک چکر ہوا۔
تشریح : مروہ پر چڑھنے کے بعد جو کام صفا پر کیا تھا وہی کام مروہ پر بھی کرے مثلا اس پر اس طرح کھڑا ہو کہ بیت اللہ نظر آئے ، 1 آج کل سامنے دیوار حائل ہے اس لئے بیت اللہ نظر نہیں آتا، البتہ اس طرح کھڑا ہو کہ دیوار نہ ہو تو بیت اللہ نظر آ جائے] بیت اللہ کا استقبال کرے، تکبیر پڑھے، لا الہ الا اللہ پڑھے، تلبیہ پڑھے، درود شریف پڑھے اور دونوں ہاتھوں کو اٹھا کر دعا کرے۔صفا سے مروہ پر آیا تو ایک شوط ہو گیا، اور پھر مروہ سے صفا پر جائے گا دوسرا شوط [ دوسرا چکر ہو جائے گا۔ وجه : (۱) اوپر یہ حدیث گزرگئی ۔ قال دخلنا على جابر بن عبد الله ... حتى أتى المروة ففعل على المروة كما فعل على الصفا. (مسلم شریف، باب حجتہ النبی ، ص ۵۱۳، نمبر ۲۹۵۰/۱۲۱۸ را ابوداؤد شریف ، باب صلته حجتہ النبی ص ۲۷۷، نمبر ۱۹۰۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ تکبیر تہلیل اور دعا ایسا ہی کرے جیسا کہ صفا پر کی تھی۔ ترجمه : (۱۳۲۶) پھر صفا کا قصد کرتے ہوئے لوٹے ، جب میلین اخضرین کے پاس آئے تو دوڑے پھر اطمینان سے چلے یہاں تک کہ صفا پر آجائے ، پھر اس پر چڑھے اور جیسا پہلے کیا تھا ایسا ہی کرے، یہ دوسرا چکر ہے۔ تشریح : مروہ سے فارغ ہونے کے بعد صفا کی طرف اطمینان سے چلے اور جب میلین اخضرین میں پہنچے تو دوڑے، اور اس سے پار ہو تو پھر اطمینان سے چلے اور صفا پر آ جائے، اور جس طرح پہلے صفا پر تکبیر تہلیل درود شریف اور دعا کی تھی اسی طرح کرے۔ یہ دوسرا چکر ہو گیا ۔ بعض حضرات کے یہاں صفا سے مروہ اور مروہ سے پھر صفا پر آئے تب ایک چکر پورا ہوتا ہے لیکن ہمارے یہاں مروہ پر ایک چکر پورا ہوا اور صفا پر دوسرا چکر پورا ہو گیا۔
وجه : (۱) قال سمعت عبد الله بن ابى أوفى بهذا الحديث زاد : ثم اتى الصفا والمروة فسعى بينهما سبعا ثم حلق رأسه . (ابوداؤد شریف، باب امر الصفا والمروۃ ص ۲۶۸ نمبر ۱۹۰۳ ) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ صفا مروہ کے درمیان سات شوط سعی کی۔(۲) فقال ابن عمر قدم رسول الله فطاف بالبيت سبعا وصلى خلف المقام ركعتين وطاف بين الصفا والمروة سبعا وقد كان لكم في رسول الله الا الله اسوة حسنة (سنن بیھقی ، باب وجوب الطواف بین الصفا والمروة وان غیرہ لا یجری عنہ ، ج خامس ص ۱۵۸، نمبر ۹۳۶۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ صفا اور مروہ کے درمیان سات شوط کئے ، اور
Chapter: Composition of the Actions of Hajj. Thamaratun Najah Volume 2. Until you see the House (Kaaba) and face it, saying takbir, tahlil, talbiyah, salawat, and supplications, raising your hands open. (1324) Then descend towards Marwah in a dignified manner. When you reach the bottom of the valley, run rapidly between the two green markers. When you pass them, walk normally. (Verse 158, Surah Al-Baqarah 2) This verse indicates that sa'i between Safa and Marwah is required. (3) Ascend Safa until you can see the Kaaba, then face the Kaaba and recite supplications. A hadith: Jabir narrated that the Messenger of Allah ascended Safa until he saw the Kaaba, then he said takbir. (Nasa'i) This shows that one should ascend Safa until seeing the Kaaba, then recite takbir etc. (4) Raising hands: This is based on the statement of a Companion: Ibn Abbas said: Do not raise hands except in seven places: when standing for prayer, when seeing the Kaaba, on Safa, on Marwah, at Arafat, at Muzdalifah, and at the Jamarat. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, Bayhaqi) This effect shows that when ascending Safa and Marwah, one should raise hands and supplicate. Translation of (1324): Then walk towards Marwah calmly. When you reach the bottom of the valley, run rapidly between the two green markers. When you pass the valley, walk calmly until you reach Marwah and ascend it. Commentary: After finishing supplications on Safa, walk towards Marwah mountain calmly. When you reach the two green markers, run rapidly because Lady Hagar ran there. Then when you pass the green markers, walk calmly until you ascend Marwah. Proof (1): In this hadith: We entered upon Jabir ibn Abdullah... He said similar three times, then descended to Marwah. When his feet sank in the bottom of the valley, he ran; when they ascended, he walked until he reached Marwah and did on Marwah as he did on Safa. (Muslim, Abu Dawud) This shows that one runs in the valley and walks elsewhere, and repeats the takbir, tahlil, and supplications as on Safa. Lexical notes: 'Tahbitu' is derived from 'habata', meaning to descend. 'Hadya' means walking with dignity. 'Batn al-wadi' means the bottom of the valley; here it refers to the area between Safa and Marwah, where there were two green pillars (milayn akhdarayn). It is sunnah to run between them. 'Hathitha' means fast running. Then, on Marwah, walk calmly until you ascend it. (1325) And do as you did on Safa: face the Kaaba, saying takbir, tahlil, talbiyah, salawat, and supplications, spreading your hands towards the sky. This is one round (shawt). (1326) Then return heading to Safa. When you reach the two green markers, run; then walk calmly until you reach Safa and ascend. Translation of (1325): And do the same as on Safa: face the Kaaba, recite takbir, tahlil, talbiyah, durud, stretch hands towards the sky and supplicate. This is one round. Commentary: After ascending Marwah, do as on Safa: stand so that the Kaaba is visible (today a wall blocks it), face the Kaaba, recite takbir, la ilaha illallah, talbiyah, durud, and raise both hands in supplication. Coming from Safa to Marwah completes one round; then going from Marwah to Safa completes the second round. Proof (1): The above hadith (Jabir) shows that the same takbir, tahlil, and supplication are done on Marwah as on Safa. Translation of (1326): Then return heading to Safa. When you reach the green markers, run; then walk calmly until you reach Safa, ascend, and do as before. This is the second round. Commentary: After finishing at Marwah, walk calmly towards Safa. When you reach the green markers, run; when you pass them, walk calmly until you reach Safa. Then do as before: takbir, tahlil, durud, and supplication. This is the second round. Some scholars hold that one round is completed only when you go from Safa to Marwah and back to Safa. But in our school, one round is completed at Marwah (first half) and the second at Safa (second half). Proof (1): Abdullah ibn Abi Awfa narrated: then he came to Safa and Marwah and performed sa'i between them seven times, then shaved his head. (Abu Dawud) This shows seven rounds of sa'i. (2) Ibn Umar said: The Messenger of Allah performed tawaf around the Kaaba seven times, prayed two rak'ahs behind the Maqam, and performed sa'i between Safa and Marwah seven times. Indeed, you have in the Messenger of Allah an excellent example. (Bayhaqi) This shows seven rounds of sa'i between Safa and Marwah.
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof lesson from Thamaratun Najah explaining the method of sa'i between Safa and Marwah during Hajj or Umrah. The text begins by describing the actions on Safa: the pilgrim ascends until they see the Kaaba, then faces it and recites takbir, tahlil, talbiyah, salawat, and supplications, raising their hands. This is supported by a hadith from Jabir and the statement of Ibn Abbas that the hands are raised in seven specific places, including Safa and Marwah. Then comes the core ruling: after descending from Safa, the pilgrim walks calmly towards Marwah, but when reaching the bottom of the valley (batn al-wadi) between the two green markers (milayn akhdarayn), they must run rapidly. This running is a sunnah, emulating Lady Hagar. Once past the green markers, they resume walking calmly until ascending Marwah. On Marwah, they repeat the same actions as on Safa. The text then explains that one round (shawt) is completed upon reaching Marwah from Safa. This is followed by the return trip: from Marwah back to Safa, again running between the green markers, and upon ascending Safa the second round is completed. A key intra-Hanafi point is mentioned: some scholars consider a round completed only after returning to the starting point (Safa to Safa via Marwah), but the Hanafi school counts the first round at Marwah and the second at Safa. The text provides two hadith proofs for the seven rounds of sa'i overall. The lexical notes clarify terms: 'tabata' (descend), 'hadya' (walk with dignity), 'batn al-wadi' (valley bed), 'milayn akhdarayn' (two green pillars), and 'hathitha' (rapid running). The commentary reinforces that the running is only between the green markers, not the entire distance, and that the same supplications are recited on both hills.

Key Terms
سعی (سعی) (sa'y): The ritual walking between Safa and Marwah, specifically the running between the green markers.
شوط (شوط) (shawt): One complete traverse from Safa to Marwah or from Marwah to Safa. In Hanafi school, each direction is a separate shawt.
میلین اخضرین (ميلان أخضران) (milayn akhdarayn): Two green pillars or markers located in the valley between Safa and Marwah. The pilgrim is to run between them.
بطن الوادی (بطن الوادي) (batn al-wadi): The bottom or middle of the valley between Safa and Marwah where the green markers are placed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is the first round (shawt) of sa'i completed?
A) Upon returning to Safa after going to Marwah
B) Upon reaching Marwah from Safa
C) After the seventh round
D) At the end of the entire sa'i

Key Takeaway
The sa'i between Safa and Marwah is performed by walking calmly except between the two green markers where running is sunnah; each traverse constitutes a round, with odd rounds ending at Marwah and even at Safa.

Hajj — Pilgrimage

The Rulings and Pattern of Sa'i Between Safa and Marwah
Describes the ritual actions for Sa'i, including running and number of laps.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on the number and definition of laps in Sa'i and apply them to calculate the correct ending point.

Core Idea
One lap of Sa'i is from one hill to the other; seven laps end at Marwah.

This lesson explains the ritual actions of Sa'i (running between Safa and Marwah) as prescribed in the Hanafi school. You will learn the correct sequence of actions, including the supplications and the running between the green pillars. The lesson also clarifies the Hanafi definition of a 'lap' (shawṭ) and contrasts it with other schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is Sa'i between Safa and Marwah. It is wajib for Hajj and Umrah according to the Hanafi school.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites hadith from Muslim, Abu Dawud, and Bayhaqi describing the Prophet's actions on Safa and Marwah and the number of laps.
The key hadith is from Ibn Umar: 'He performed Sa'i seven times between Safa and Marwah.'
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's actions on Marwah were identical to those on Safa. The phrase 'seven times' is interpreted as seven one-way traversals.
The Hanafi understanding counts each traversal from one hill to the other as one lap.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) consider a lap to be a round trip from Safa to Marwah and back to Safa. The Hanafi school rejects this.
This difference affects whether the seventh lap ends at Marwah or back at Safa.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is based on the zahir of the hadith and is the relied-upon view (mufta bihi) in the school.
The author of Thamaratun Najah follows the majority Hanafi view.

وجه : (۱) اوپر یہ حدیث گزرگئی ۔ قال دخلنا على جابر بن عبد الله ... حتى أتى المروة ففعل على المروة كما فعل على الصفا. (مسلم شریف، باب حجتہ النبی ، ص ۵۱۳، نمبر ۲۹۵۰/۱۲۱۸ را ابوداؤد شریف ، باب صلته حجتہ النبی ص ۲۷۷، نمبر ۱۹۰۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ تکبیر تہلیل اور دعا ایسا ہی کرے جیسا کہ صفا پر کی تھی۔

ترجمه : (۱۳۲۶) پھر صفا کا قصد کرتے ہوئے لوٹے ، جب میلین اخضرین کے پاس آئے تو دوڑے پھر اطمینان سے چلے یہاں تک کہ صفا پر آجائے ، پھر اس پر چڑھے اور جیسا پہلے کیا تھا ایسا ہی کرے، یہ دوسرا چکر ہے۔

تشریح : مروہ سے فارغ ہونے کے بعد صفا کی طرف اطمینان سے چلے اور جب میلین اخضرین میں پہنچے تو دوڑے، اور اس سے پار ہو تو پھر اطمینان سے چلے اور صفا پر آ جائے، اور جس طرح پہلے صفا پر تکبیر تہلیل درود شریف اور دعا کی تھی اسی طرح کرے۔ یہ دوسرا چکر ہو گیا ۔ بعض حضرات کے یہاں صفا سے مروہ اور مروہ سے پھر صفا پر آئے تب ایک چکر پورا ہوتا ہے لیکن ہمارے یہاں مروہ پر ایک چکر پورا ہوا اور صفا پر دوسرا چکر پورا ہو گیا۔

وجه : (۱) قال سمعت عبد الله بن ابى أوفى بهذا الحديث زاد : ثم اتى الصفا والمروة فسعى بينهما سبعا ثم حلق رأسه . (ابوداؤد شریف، باب امر الصفا والمروۃ ص ۲۶۸ نمبر ۱۹۰۳ ) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ صفا مروہ کے درمیان سات شوط سعی کی۔

(۲) فقال ابن عمر قدم رسول الله فطاف بالبيت سبعا وصلى خلف المقام ركعتين وطاف بين الصفا والمروة سبعا وقد كان لكم في رسول الله الا الله اسوة حسنة (سنن بیھقی ، باب وجوب الطواف بین الصفا والمروة وان غیرہ لا یجری عنہ ، ج خامس ص ۱۵۸، نمبر ۹۳۶۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ صفا اور مروہ کے درمیان سات شوط کئے ، اور

عليها ويفعل كما فعل اوّلا وهذا شوط ثان (۱۳٢٧) فيطوف سبعة اشواط يبدأ بالصفا ويختم بالمروة ويسعى في بطن الوادى فى كل شوط منها
Walk in the valley bottom in a composed manner until you reach Marwah, then ascend upon it (1325) and do as you did on Safa: face the House, saying takbir, tahlil, talbiyah, salawat, supplicating with your hands extended towards the sky. This is one lap. (1326) Then return heading towards Safa. When you reach the two green pillars, run, then walk in a composed manner until you reach Safa and ascend upon it, and do as you did first. This is the second lap. (1327) He performs seven laps, starting from Safa and ending at Marwah, and he runs in the valley bottom during each lap.
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This passage from the commentary explains the detailed actions of Sa'i (the ritual walking between Safa and Marwah). The author describes two key rulings: (1) The actions on Marwah are identical to those on Safa: facing the Kaaba, reciting takbir, tahlil, talbiyah, salawat, and raising hands in supplication. (2) The counting of laps: one lap is completed from Safa to Marwah, not from Safa back to Safa. The Hanafi position is that the seven laps of Sa'i begin at Safa and end at Marwah; each traversal from one hill to the other counts as one lap. The author cites hadith from Muslim, Abu Dawud, and Bayhaqi to support this, including the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and the narration of Ibn Umar. He also addresses a difference of opinion: some schools consider a lap as going from Safa to Marwah and back to Safa, but the Hanafi view is that one lap is from one hill to the other, so the seventh lap ends at Marwah.

Key Terms
شوط (shawṭ): One lap of Sa'i between Safa and Marwah. According to the Hanafi school, one shawṭ is from one hill to the other (e.g., Safa to Marwah), not a round trip.
صفا (Ṣafā): One of the two hills in Mecca between which Sa'i is performed. The Sa'i begins at Safa.
مروة (Marwah): The second hill. According to Hanafi opinion, the Sa'i ends at Marwah after seven laps.
ميل أخضر (mīl akhḍar): A green pillar or marker in the valley between Safa and Marwah. The area between the two green pillars is where the pilgrim runs (harwala) during Sa'i.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, where does the seventh lap of Sa'i end?
A) At the starting point, Safa
B) At Marwah
C) At the Kaaba
D) In the middle of the valley

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, Sa'i consists of seven one-way laps from Safa to Marwah, ending at Marwah.

Post-Sa'i: The Mufrid's Stay and Superiority of Tawaf
Ruling that a Mufrid should remain in ihram and perform Tawaf as much as possible.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a Mufrid regarding staying in ihram and performing voluntary Tawaf, and explain why Tawaf is better than nafl prayer for an Aafaqi, citing the textual proofs.

Core Idea
For a Mufrid, Tawaf in Makkah is better than nafl prayer; stay in ihram until the Day of Sacrifice.

After completing Tawaf al-Qudum and Sa'i, a Mufrid (one performing only Hajj) remains in ihram until the Day of Sacrifice. During this waiting period, the Hanafi school recommends performing as many voluntary Tawafs as possible. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its rationale, and the three proofs from the Sunnah and a Companion's saying that establish that Tawaf is superior to nafl prayer for those who cannot perform it in their homeland.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its context
State who the ruling applies to (Mufrid, Aafaqi) and what actions are prescribed: remain in ihram and perform Tawaf repeatedly.
The ruling is not about obligatory Tawaf but about voluntary acts during the stay.
2
Understand the rationale for preferring Tawaf
Recognize the key reasoning: Tawaf can only be done in Makkah, while nafl prayer can be done anywhere. Therefore, for a non-Meccan, Tawaf is more valuable.
This is a location-specific virtue.
3
Examine the first proof: Hadith of Aisha
Read the hadith showing that the Prophet and companions who intended Hajj alone or Qiran did not remove ihram until the Day of Sacrifice. This establishes the obligation to remain in ihram.
This proof directly supports staying in ihram.
4
Examine the second proof: Saying of Ata
Consider the statement of the tabi'i Ata that for strangers (non-Makkans), Tawaf is superior to prayer because they cannot perform Tawaf in their homeland.
This is a direct textual evidence for superiority.
5
Examine the third proof: Hadith of Ibn Abbas
Review the hadith promising immense reward for performing multiple Tawafs. This encourages maximizing Tawaf during the stay.
This underscores the merit of the act.

Source Text

ثم يقيم بمكة محرما ويطوف بالبيت كلّما بدا

ترجمه : (۱۳۲۸) پھر مکہ مکرمہ میں احرام کی حالت میں ٹھہرا رہے، اور جب جب ہو سکے بیت اللہ کا طواف کرتا رہے، یہ آفاقی کے لئے نفلی نماز سے افضل ہے۔

تشریح : چونکہ یہ مفرد بالج ہے اس لئے اس کا احرام باقی ہے، اس لئے احرام کی حالت میں مکہ مکرمہ میں ٹھہرا ر ہے۔ اور جتنا ہو سکے طواف کرتار ہے، کیونکہ اپنا ملک جانے کے بعد یہ طواف نہیں کر سکے گا اس لئے یہ نفلی نماز سے بہتر ہے۔

وجه : (۱) دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن عائشة انهـا قـالـت خرجنا مع رسول الله عام حجة الوداع فمنا من اهل بعمرة ومنا من اهل بحج وعمرة ومنا من اهل بالحج، واهل رسول الله له بالحج واما من اهل بالحج او جمع الحج والعمرة لم يحلوا حتى كان يوم النحر (بخاری شریف، باب التمتع والقران والافراد بالج و نسخ المح لمن لم يكن معه هدی ، ص ۲۵۴، نمبر ۱۵۶۲ را بود اود شریف ، باب القرآن، ص ۲۶۵، نمبر ۱۸۰۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ جس نے حج کا احرام باندھا یا قران کا احرام باندھا وہ طواف قدوم کے بعد احرام نہیں کھولے گا۔ بلکہ مکہ مکرمہ میں محرم ہو کر ٹھہرے گا۔

(۲) طواف زیادہ افضل ہے اس کے لئے یہ قول تابعی ہے۔ كنت اسمع عطاء يسأله الغرباء ، الطواف افضل لنا ام الصلاة ؟ فيقول
امـا لـكـم فالطواف افضل ، انكم لا تقدرون على الطواف بارضكم ، و انتم تقدرون هناك على الصلاة ( مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الطواف افضل ام الصلاة ، ج خامس ، ص ۵۳، نمبر ۹۹۰) اس قول تابعی میں ہے کہ آفاقی کے لئے طواف افضل ہے، کیونکہ اپنے ملکوں میں نہیں ہوسکتا۔

(۳) اس حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال قال رسول الله من طاف بالبيت خمسين مرة خرج من ذنوبه كيوم ولدته امه. ( ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فی فضل الطواف ،ص ۱۷۵ نمبر ۸۶۶) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ طواف کا ثواب بہت ہے اس لئے زیادہ سے زیادہ طواف کرتار ہے۔
Then he stays in Makkah as a muhrim and circumambulates the House whenever he can. Translation: (1328) He remains in Makkah in the state of ihram, and performs Tawaf of the Kaaba as often as possible. For a person coming from outside the miqat (Aafaqi), this is superior to non-obligatory prayer. Explanation: Since he is performing only Hajj (Mufrid), his ihram remains; so he stays in Makkah in ihram and performs Tawaf as much as he can, because after returning to his country he will not be able to perform Tawaf; therefore Tawaf is better than nafl prayer. Evidence: (1) Hadith of Aisha: 'We went out with the Messenger of Allah in the Farewell Hajj... those who intended Hajj or Qiran did not remove ihram until the Day of Sacrifice.' This indicates that a person in ihram for Hajj or Qiran should not open ihram after Tawaf al-Qudum, but remain in Makkah as muhrim. (2) Saying of Ata: 'For you (strangers), Tawaf is superior because you are not able to perform Tawaf in your own lands, while you can pray there.' (3) Hadith of Ibn Abbas: 'Whoever circumambulates the House fifty times, his sins will be forgiven like the day his mother bore him.' This shows the great reward of Tawaf, so one should perform as much Tawaf as possible.
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling for a Mufrid (one performing Hajj only, without Umrah) after completing the initial Tawaf al-Qudum and Sa'i. According to the Hanafi school, such a person remains in ihram until the Day of Sacrifice (10th Dhul Hijjah). During this waiting period, it is recommended (mustahabb) to engage in Tawaf as much as possible because it is not available in one's homeland, whereas nafl prayer can be done anywhere. The author provides three proofs: the hadith of Aisha showing the Prophet and his companions did not remove ihram until the Day of Sacrifice; the saying of Ata that for those who are not from Mecca, Tawaf is better than nafl prayer because it is location-specific; and the hadith of Ibn Abbas on the immense reward of Tawaf. The practical takeaway: a Mufrid should maximize Tawaf during his stay in Makkah while in ihram.

Key Terms
آفاقي (āfāqī): A person who comes from outside the miqat (appointed boundary) for Hajj or Umrah. For such a person, Tawaf is considered superior to nafl prayer because they cannot perform Tawaf in their homeland.
مفرد بالحج (mufrad bil-ḥajj): One who performs Hajj only (Ifrad), without combining it with Umrah. Such a person remains in ihram after Tawaf al-Qudum until the Day of Sacrifice.
طواف (ṭawāf): Circumambulation of the Kaaba. In this context, it refers to the voluntary Tawaf performed by the Mufrid while waiting in Makkah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A Mufrid should remain in ihram and prioritize voluntary Tawaf over nafl prayer during his stay in Makkah, as Tawaf is a location-specific act of worship.

The Ruling on Sa'i: Seven Circuits from Safa to Marwa
Ruling on Sa'i with seven circuits

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the correct method of performing Sa'i (seven circuits, each from Safa to Marwa, ending at Marwa) and explain the sunnah of running in Batan al-Wadi.

Core Idea
Sa'i consists of seven circuits, each from Safa to Marwa, ending on Marwa — not a round trip.

In this passage, the author clarifies the precise method of performing Sa'i between Safa and Marwa. Many pilgrims confuse the definition of a single circuit. The author emphasizes that each circuit begins at Safa and ends at Marwa, and the seventh circuit concludes at Marwa. Additionally, the sunnah of running between the two green markers is explained.

Guided Path
1
Define one circuit (shawt) in Sa'i
Understand that in the Hanafi school, one shawt is from Safa to Marwa, not a round trip. This is the fundamental unit.
The source explicitly says: 'each circuit starts at Safa and ends at Marwa'.
2
Count the seven circuits correctly
The Sa'i consists of exactly seven circuits. After completing the seventh, you end at Marwa, not Safa.
The author warns against the mistaken notion that the seventh circuit ends at Safa.
3
Identify the start and end points
The start is the hill of Safa, and the end is the hill of Marwa. The seventh circuit finishes at Marwa.
This means you do not return to Safa after the seventh.
4
Recognize the sunnah of running
In each circuit, between the two green markers (Batan al-Wadi), it is sunnah to run quickly. This is an established practice.
Proof for this running is referenced as having passed earlier in the text.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل تركيب افعال الحج
ثمرة النجاح جلد ٢ عليها ويفعل كما فعل اوّلا وهذا شوط ثان (۱۳۲۷) فيطوف سبعة اشواط يبدأ بالصفا ويختم بالمروة ويسعى في بطن الوادى فى كل شوط منها (۱۳۲۸) يہ بھی معلوم ہوا کہ صفا سے مروہ تک میں ایک شوط پورا ہو جاتا ہے۔ ترجمه : (۱۳۲۷) سات چکر پورے کرے کہ صفا سے شروع کرے اور مروہ پر ختم کرے اور ہر چکر میں بطن وادی کے درمیان تشریح : صفا سے شروع کرے اور مروہ پر ایک چکر پورا ہو جائے تو سات چکر میں مروہ پر جا کر پورے ہو جاتے ہیں، واپس صفا نہیں آنا پڑتا، اس لئے مصنف فرماتے ہیں کہ مروہ پر سا تواں چکر پورا کرے۔ اور اگر صفا سے چلکر واپس صفا پر ایک چکر مانتے ہیں تو سات چکر صفا پر آکر پورے ہوں گے، مصنف فرماتے ہیں یہ نہ کریں۔ اور دوسری بات یہ ہے کہ ہر چکر میں میلین اخضرین میں تیزی سے دوڑے، یہ سنت ہے۔ دلیل او پر گزرگئی۔
Chapter: Composition of the Actions of Hajj. The fruit of success volume 2. Upon it, he does as he did first, and this is the second circuit. (1327) He performs seven circuits, starting from Safa and ending at Marwa, and he runs in the bottom of the valley in each circuit (1328). It is also known that from Safa to Marwa one complete circuit is completed. Translation: (1327) He completes seven circuits, beginning from Safa and ending at Marwa, and in each circuit he runs in the middle of the valley. Explanation: He starts from Safa and completes one circuit at Marwa, so in seven circuits he ends at Marwa, he does not need to return to Safa. Therefore the author says that he should complete the seventh circuit at Marwa. And if one considers going from Safa and returning to Safa as one circuit, then seven circuits would end at Safa; the author says do not do this. And the second matter is that in every circuit he should run quickly between the two green markers; this is sunnah. The proof for it has passed.
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on the performance of Sa'i between Safa and Marwa. The author clarifies that Sa'i consists of seven complete circuits. Each circuit begins at Safa and ends at Marwa; the seventh circuit ends at Marwa, not at Safa. Some mistakenly consider a round trip from Safa to Safa as one circuit, but the correct method is to end at Marwa. Additionally, it is Sunnah to run between the two green markers (the area known as Batan al-Wadi) during each circuit. The proof for this running is already mentioned earlier in the book.

Key Terms
سعی (sa'y): Walking between Safa and Marwa seven times as a ritual of Hajj and Umrah.
شوط (shawt): One circuit from Safa to Marwa (in Sa'i).
بطن الوادی (Batan al-Wadi): The valley between Safa and Marwa where the two green markers are; running is prescribed here.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Staying in Makkah in Ihram and Virtue of Tawaf for the Afaqi
Ruling on staying in ihram in Makkah and preference of tawaf over nafl prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that for a mufrid or qarin, staying in Makkah in ihram is required and that tawaf is more virtuous than nafl prayer for an afaqi, and cite the proofs from hadith and the saying of Ata.

Core Idea
For the afaqi, tawaf in Makkah is more virtuous than nafl prayer because it cannot be performed elsewhere, while prayer can be performed anywhere.

After performing the initial tawaf and sa'i, a pilgrim performing Hajj ifrad or qiran remains in ihram and stays in Makkah, performing as many tawafs as possible. This passage explains that for someone from outside Makkah (afaqi), tawaf is superior to voluntary prayer due to the limited opportunity. Three proofs are provided: the hadith of Aisha on staying in ihram, the saying of Ata on the virtue of tawaf for strangers, and the hadith on the immense reward of tawaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its context
The passage addresses a person performing Hajj ifrad (mufrad) or qiran. After entering Makkah, what must he do? He must stay in Makkah in ihram and perform tawaf whenever possible.
2
Distinguish the ruling for afaqi vs Makkan
Why is tawaf better than nafl prayer specifically for the afaqi? Because he can pray anywhere but can only do tawaf in Makkah. For a Makkan, nafl prayer may be equal or better.
This distinction is crucial.
3
Examine the first proof
Hadith of Aisha: those who entered Hajj or Qiran did not remove ihram until the Day of Nahr. This implies they remained in Makkah as muhrimun.
The hadith is from Bukhari and Abu Dawud.
4
Examine the second proof
Saying of Ata ibn Abi Rabah: for strangers (afaqi), tawaf is better because they cannot perform it at home, but can pray there.
This is a direct statement from a prominent Tabi'i.
5
Examine the third proof
Hadith of Ibn Abbas: fifty tawafs erase sins like the day of birth. This shows great reward, encouraging frequent tawaf.
The hadith is from Tirmidhi.

ثم يقيم بمكة محرما ويطوف بالبيت كلّما بدا له وهو افضل من الصلوة نفلا للآفاقى (۱۳۲۹) ترجمه : (۱۳۲۸) پھر مکہ مکرمہ میں احرام کی حالت میں ٹھہرا رہے، اور جب جب ہو سکے بیت اللہ کا طواف کرتا رہے، یہ آفاقی کے لئے نفلی نماز سے افضل ہے۔ تشریح : چونکہ یہ مفرد بالج ہے اس لئے اس کا احرام باقی ہے، اس لئے احرام کی حالت میں مکہ مکرمہ میں ٹھہرا ر ہے۔ اور جتنا ہو سکے طواف کرتار ہے، کیونکہ اپنا ملک جانے کے بعد یہ طواف نہیں کر سکے گا اس لئے یہ نفلی نماز سے بہتر ہے۔ وجه : (۱) دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن عائشة انهـا قـالـت خرجنا مع رسول الله عام حجة الوداع فمنا من اهل بعمرة ومنا من اهل بحج وعمرة ومنا من اهل بالحج، واهل رسول الله له بالحج واما من اهل بالج او جمع الحج والعمرة لم يحلوا حتى كان يوم النحر (بخاری شریف، باب التمتع والقران والافراد بالج و نسخ المح لمن لم يكن معه هدی ، ص ۲۵۴، نمبر ۱۵۶۲ را بود اود شریف ، باب القرآن، ص ۲۶۵، نمبر ۱۸۰۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ جس نے حج کا احرام باندھا یا قران کا احرام باندھا وہ طواف قدوم کے بعد احرام نہیں کھولے گا۔ بلکہ مکہ مکرمہ میں محرم ہو کر ٹھہرے گا۔ (۲) طواف زیادہ افضل ہے اس کے لئے یہ قول تابعی ہے۔ كنت اسمع عطاء يسأله الغرباء ، الطواف افضل لنا ام الصلاة ؟ فيقول اما لـكـم فالطواف افضل ، انكم لا تقدرون على الطواف بارضكم ، و انتم تقدرون هناك على الصلاة ( مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الطواف افضل ام الصلاة ، ج خامس ، ص ۵۳، نمبر ۹۹۰) اس قول تابعی میں ہے کہ آفاقی کے لئے طواف افضل ہے، کیونکہ اپنے ملکوں میں نہیں ہوسکتا۔ (۳) اس حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال قال رسول الله من طاف بالبيت خمسين مرة خرج من ذنوبه كيوم ولدته امه. ( ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فی فضل الطواف ،ص ۱۷۵ نمبر ۸۶۶) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ طواف کا ثواب بہت ہے اس لئے زیادہ سے زیادہ طواف کرتار ہے۔
Then he stays in Makkah as a muhrim, and performs tawaf of the House whenever he desires, and it is more virtuous than nafl prayer for the afaqi (one from outside the Haram). Translation: (1328) Then he stays in Makkah al-Mukarramah in the state of ihram, and performs tawaf of the House of Allah whenever possible; this is more virtuous than nafl prayer for the afaqi. Explanation: Since he is performing ifrad Hajj, his ihram remains, so he stays in Makkah in ihram. He performs tawaf as much as possible, because after returning to his homeland he will not be able to perform tawaf, so this is better than nafl prayer. Proofs: (1) The hadith of Aisha: 'We went out with the Messenger of Allah in the year of the Farewell Hajj. Some of us assumed ihram for Umrah, some for Hajj and Umrah, and some for Hajj. The Messenger of Allah assumed ihram for Hajj. As for those who assumed ihram for Hajj or combined Hajj and Umrah, they did not remove ihram until the Day of Nahr.' (Bukhari, Abu Dawud) From this hadith it is understood that whoever assumes ihram for Hajj or Qiran will not remove ihram after Tawaf al-Qudum; rather, he stays in Makkah as a muhrim. (2) The saying of the Tabi'i Ata: 'I heard Ata being asked by strangers: Is tawaf better for us or prayer? He said: For you, tawaf is better, because you cannot perform tawaf in your land, whereas you can pray there.' (Abdur Razzaq) (3) The hadith of Ibn Abbas: 'The Messenger of Allah said: Whoever performs tawaf of the House fifty times, emerges from his sins like the day his mother bore him.' (Tirmidhi) From this, the reward of tawaf is great, so he should perform tawaf abundantly.
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling for a person performing Hajj ifrad (mufrad bil-hajj) or qiran. After completing the initial tawaf and sa'i, he remains in ihram and stays in Makkah performing as many tawafs as possible. The author states that for an afaqi (someone who came from outside Makkah), tawaf is superior to nafl prayer because he will not have the opportunity to perform tawaf after returning home, whereas he can pray nafl anywhere. The passage provides three proofs: (1) Hadith of Aisha that those who entered Hajj or Qiran did not remove ihram until the Day of Nahr. (2) The saying of Ata' ibn Abi Rabah that tawaf is better for strangers (afaqi) because they cannot perform tawaf in their own land. (3) The hadith that performing tawaf fifty times removes sins as on the day of birth.

Key Terms
آفاقی (afaqi): One who comes from outside the Haram (non-Makkan) to perform Hajj or Umrah.
مفرد بالحج (mufrad bil-hajj): One who performs Hajj ifrad (Hajj alone, without Umrah).

A) Because tawaf is obligatory and prayer is not

C) Because tawaf is faster than prayer
D) Because the Prophet specifically commanded tawaf

Key Takeaway
For a mufrid or qarin, remaining in ihram and performing tawaf frequently is emphasized, with tawaf being more virtuous than nafl prayer for the afaqi.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
beginner
8 min
Actions on Yawm al-Tarwiyah (8th of Dhul Hijjah)
Rulings for the day of Tarwiyah with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings for the 8th of Dhul Hijjah and identify the proofs for each action.

Core Idea
The pilgrim's day on 8th Dhul Hijjah: pray Fajr in Makkah, depart after sunrise, pray Zuhr in Mina, continue talbiyah except during tawaf, and stay overnight near Masjid al-Khaif.

Yawm al-Tarwiyah marks the beginning of the Hajj rituals. This lesson covers the three key actions recommended by the Hanafi school: departing to Mina after sunrise, praying Zuhr in Mina, and continuing talbiyah until the stoning of Jamrat al-Aqabah. We also learn the recommended overnight stay in Mina near Masjid al-Khaif. Each action is supported by authentic hadith proofs.

Guided Path
1
Locate the three actions
Identify the three main rulings in the passage: (1) departing to Mina after sunrise and praying Zuhr there, (2) continuing talbiyah except during tawaf, (3) staying overnight in Mina near Masjid al-Khaif until Fajr of the 9th.
The passage is structured as three numbered paragraphs.
2
Classify each ruling's hukm
For each action, determine the legal level: mustahab for the departure and staying, sunnah muakkadah for talbiyah. The text uses phrases like 'yastahibbu' (it is mustahab) and 'la yatruk' (do not abandon, indicating emphasis).
Talbiyah is sunnah muakkadah – its abandonment is disliked (makruh).
3
Trace the dalil for each ruling
The passage cites three hadiths: (a) hadith of Jabir showing the Prophet prayed Zuhr, Asr, Maghrib, Isha, and Fajr in Mina on this day; (b) hadith of Fadl ibn Abbas that the Prophet recited talbiyah until stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah; (c) hadith of Ibn Abbas that the mu'tamir recites talbiyah until touching the Black Stone.
These are ahad hadith, giving zanni thubut, but they establish the sunnah.
4
Understand the exception for talbiyah
Talbiyah is not recited during tawaf (as per the text's exception) and is permanently stopped after stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah (as per the hadith of Fadl). During Umrah, it stops upon touching the Black Stone.
This exception prevents interruption of the ritual with talbiyah during tawaf.
5
Apply the rulings to a practical sequence
On the morning of 8th Dhul Hijjah: pray Fajr in Makkah, then after sunrise head to Mina, pray Zuhr there, continue talbiyah, stay in Mina, pray the five prayers (Zuhr, Asr, Maghrib, Isha, Fajr), camp near Masjid al-Khaif, and after sunrise of 9th proceed to Arafat.
The overnight stay in Mina is mustahab; it is not required for the validity of Hajj.

فاذا صلّى الفجر بمكة ثامن ذى الحجة تأهّب للخروج الى منى فيخرج منها بعد طلوع الشمس ويستحب ان يصلي الظهر بمنى (۱۳۳۰) ولا يترك التلبية في احواله كلّها الا فى الطواف (۱۳۳۱) ويمكث بمنى الى ان يصلى الفجر بها بغلس ترجمه : (۱۳۲۹) پھر جب آٹھویں تاریخ کو مکہ میں نماز فجر پڑھے تو منی کی طرف چلنے کی تیاری کرے، اور مکہ مکرمہ سے سورج طلوع ہونے کے بعد نکلے، اور مستحب ہے کہ نماز ظہر منی میں پڑھے۔ تشریح : آٹھویں ذی الحجہ کو مکہ مکرمہ میں فجر کی نماز پڑھے اور سورج نکلنے کے بعد منی کی طرف چلے اور ظہر کی نما زمنی میں پڑھے۔ وجه (۱) حدیث یہ ہے۔ دخـلـنـا عـلـى جابر بن عبد الله فسال عن القوم حتى انتهى الى ... فلما كان يوم التروية توجهوا الى منى فاهلوا بالحج وركب رسول الله فصلى بها الظهر والعصر و المغرب والعشاء و الفجر. (مسلم شریف، باب حجتہ النبی ص ۵۱۵، نمبر ۲۹۵۰/۱۲۱۸ را بو داؤد شریف ، باب صلة حجمه النبي ، ص ۲۷۸، نمبر ۱۹۰۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ آٹھویں ذی الحجہ کو نئی آئے ، اور ظہر کی نماز منی میں پڑھے۔ ترجمه : (۱۳۳۰) اور ان تمام حالتوں میں سوائے طواف کے تلبیہ ترک نہ کرے۔ تشریح : طواف کے وقت تلبیہ نہ پڑھے باقی تمام حالتوں میں تلبیہ زیادہ سے زیادہ پڑھے۔ وجه : (۱) عن الفضل بن عباس ان رسول الله الله لبي حتى رمى جمرة العقبة ۔ (ابوداود شریف، باب متى ماقطع التلبية ؟ ص ۲۶۷، نمبر ۱۸۱۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ جمرہ عقبہ تک تلبیہ پڑھے۔ (۲) عن ابن عباس عن النبي علي قال يلبي المعتمر حتى يستلم الحجر ۔ (ابوداود شریف ، باب متى يقطع المعتمر التلبية ؟ ص ۲۶۷ نمبر ۱۸۱۷) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حجر اسود کے چھونے تک یعنی طواف شروع کرتے وقت تک تلبیہ پڑھے۔ تـرجـمـه : (۱۳۳۱) اور منی میں ٹھہرارہے یہاں تک کہ (۹ رذی الحجہ) کی نماز فجر اندھیرے میں پڑھے۔ اور مسجد خیف کے قریب اترے۔ تشريح مني دو میل کے اندر پھیلا ہوا ہے ، اس لئے فرماتے ہیں کہ مسجد خیف کے پاس ٹھہر نا زیادہ بہتر ہے، تاکہ کنکری مارنا آسان ہو جائے ۔مسجد خیف جمرات کے قریب ہے، اور یہاں پانچ نمازیں پڑھے ، ظہر، عصر،مغرب،عشاء،اور ۹ رذی الحجہ کی فجر ، اس کے بعد سورج نکلنے کے بعد عرفات جانے کی تیاری کرے۔ وجه (۱) حدیث یہ ہے۔ دخـلـنـا عـلـى جابر بن عبد الله فسال عن القوم حتى انتهى الى ... فلما كان يوم التروية توجهوا الى منى فاهلوا بالحج وركب رسول الله فصلى بها الظهر والعصر و المغرب و العشاء و الفجر
So when he prays Fajr in Makkah on the 8th of Dhul Hijjah, he prepares to go out to Mina, and he leaves from it after sunrise, and it is mustahab that he pray Zuhr in Mina. (1330) And he does not abandon talbiyah in all his states except during tawaf. (1331) And he stays in Mina until he prays Fajr there in darkness. Translation: (1329) Then when on the 8th date he prays Fajr prayer in Makkah, he prepares to go to Mina, and leaves from Makkah after sunrise, and it is mustahab that he pray Zuhr prayer in Mina. Explanation: On the 8th of Dhul Hijjah, he prays Fajr in Makkah, and after sunrise he goes to Mina and prays Zuhr in Mina. Proof: The hadith of Jabir: 'We entered upon Jabir ibn Abdullah... then on the day of Tarwiyah they headed to Mina and assumed ihram for Hajj, and the Messenger of Allah rode and prayed Zuhr, Asr, Maghrib, Isha, and Fajr there.' (Muslim, Abu Dawud) From this hadith it is understood that on the 8th of Dhul Hijjah, he came and prayed Zuhr in Mina. Translation: (1330) And in all these states, he does not abandon talbiyah except during tawaf. Explanation: He does not recite talbiyah during tawaf; in all other states he recites talbiyah abundantly. Proof: (1) Hadith of Fadl ibn Abbas: 'The Messenger of Allah recited talbiyah until he stoned Jamrat al-Aqabah.' (Abu Dawud) (2) Hadith of Ibn Abbas: 'The Prophet said: The mu'tamir recites talbiyah until he touches the Black Stone.' (Abu Dawud) Translation: (1331) And he stays in Mina until he prays Fajr (of the 9th) there in darkness, and he camps near Masjid al-Khaif. Explanation: Mina is spread over two miles, so it is better to stay near Masjid al-Khaif to make stoning easier. Masjid al-Khaif is close to the Jamarat. He prays five prayers there: Zuhr, Asr, Maghrib, Isha, and Fajr of the 9th. Then after sunrise he prepares to go to Arafat. Proof: (1) Hadith of Jabir... (repeated).
Source pages p. 364

Commentary
This passage covers the actions of Yawm al-Tarwiyah (8th Dhul Hijjah). After performing Fajr prayer in Makkah, the pilgrim should prepare to go to Mina, leaving after sunrise. It is mustahab to pray Zuhr in Mina. He should continue reciting talbiyah in all states except during tawaf. He should stay in Mina until he prays Fajr of the 9th in darkness (ghalas) and camp near Masjid al-Khaif. The proofs include: the hadith of Jabir that the Prophet prayed Zuhr, Asr, Maghrib, Isha, and Fajr in Mina on the day of Tarwiyah; the hadith of Fadl ibn Abbas that the Prophet recited talbiyah until stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah; and the hadith of Ibn Abbas that the mu'tamir recites talbiyah until touching the Black Stone.

Key Terms
یوم الترویة (Yawm al-Tarwiyah): The 8th of Dhul Hijjah, the day on which pilgrims go to Mina and prepare for the Hajj rituals.
تلبیہ (talbiyah): The formula 'Labbayk Allahumma labbayk...' recited by the pilgrim in ihram.
مسجد خیف (Masjid al-Khaif): A mosque in Mina near the Jamarat where it is recommended to camp.

Key Takeaway
On Yawm al-Tarwiyah, the pilgrim should depart after sunrise, pray Zuhr in Mina, continue talbiyah except during tawaf, and stay overnight near Masjid al-Khaif.
