Joining Zuhr and Asr on the Day of Arafah: Conditions and Proofs
Ruling with proof on conditions for joining prayers on Arafah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions for joining Zuhr and Asr on the day of Arafah according to the Hanafi school and explain the proof from the Prophet's practice.

Core Idea
Joining on Arafah is sunnah only for those in ihram, in Arafat, behind the Imam of Hajj.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on combining Zuhr and Asr prayers on the day of Arafah during Hajj. While many pilgrims assume they can join regardless of their situation, the Hanafi school restricts this practice to specific conditions derived from the Prophet's own actions. Understanding these conditions is essential for correct practice and avoiding invalid prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? It is joining (jama') between Zuhr and Asr on the day of Arafah. Determine the hukm level: is it fard, wajib, sunnah? According to the Hanafi school, it is sunnah muakkadah (confirmed sunnah) based on the Prophet's practice.
Sunnah muakkadah means the Prophet consistently did it, but it is not obligatory.
2
List the conditions for joining
Imam Abu Hanifah states three conditions: (1) being in the state of ihram, (2) being present in the field of Arafat, and (3) praying behind the Imam of Hajj (or his deputy). These are necessary for the permissibility of joining.
The text numbers them as two (ihram and imam) but the commentary clarifies three, including location.
3
Examine the primary evidence (dalil)
The main proof is the hadith of Jabir describing the Prophet's actions at Arafah: he delivered two sermons, then called adhan and iqamah, and prayed Zuhr and Asr consecutively without separation. This shows the Prophet combined under these conditions.
The hadith is from Sahih Muslim (1218/2950) and others.
4
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove the conditions? The Prophet combined while he was in ihram, in Arafat, and leading the prayer as the Imam of Hajj. His specific context restricts the ruling to those in similar circumstances.
Hanafi usul emphasizes that the Prophet's action (fi'l) is evidence, but its scope is limited by context.
5
Consider the opposite: when joining is not allowed
The text provides evidence from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i that if one prays in his own tent, he must pray each prayer at its proper time with separate adhan and iqamah. The reason is that the hardship (mashaqqah) of rejoining the imam is absent.
This distinguishes between those attending the imam's congregation and those praying alone.

فصل تركيب افعال الحج
وينزل بقرب مسجد الخيف ( ١٣٣٢ ) ثم بعد طلوع الشمس يذهب الى عرفات فيقيم بها فاذا زالت الشمس يأتى مسجد نمرة (۱۳۳۳) فيصلى مع الامام الاعظم او نائبه الظهر والعصر بعد ما يخطب الظهر (مسلم شریف، باب حجتہ النبی ص ص ۵۱۵، نمبر ۲۹۵۰/۱۲۱۸ را بو داؤد شریف ، باب صفة حجتہ النبی ، ص ۲۷۸، نمبر ۱۹۰۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ آٹھویں ذی الحجہ کو منی آئے ، اور ظہر سے لیکر فجر تک کی نمازیں منی میں پڑھے۔ ترجمه : (۱۳۳۲) ۔ پھر سورج طلوع ہونے کے بعد عرفات کی طرف جائے ، اور وہیں قیام کرے۔ پس جب سورج ڈھل جائے تو مسجد نمرہ آئے۔ تشریح : ۹ رذی الحجہ کو جب سورج نکل جائے تو عرفات کی طرف جائے ، اور وہاں ٹھہرا رہے اور جب سورج ڈھل جائے تو مسجد نمرہ آئے تا کہ امام حج کے ساتھ نماز پڑھ سکے۔ وجه : (1) اس حدیث میں ہے۔ دخلنا على جابر بن عبد الله فسال عن القوم حتى انتهى الى ... ،ثم مكث طلعت الشمس وامر بقبة من شعر تضرب له بنمرة فسار رسول الله ولا تشك قريش الا انه واقف عـنـد الـمـشـعـر الحرام كما كانت قريش تصنع في الجاهلية فاجاز رسول الله حتى اتى عرفة فوجد قليلا حتى القبة قد ضربت له بنمرة فنزل بها (مسلم شریف ، باب حجتہ النبی ص ۵۱۵) نمبر ۲۹۵۰/۱۲۱۸ ابوداؤد شریف، باب صفة حجمه النبي ، ص ۲۷۸، نمبر ۱۹۰۵) (۲) عن عائشة قالت كانت و من دان دينها يوقفون بالمزدلفة و كانوا يسمون الحمس و كان سائر العرب يقفون بعرفة ، قالت فلما جاء الاسلام أمر الله تعالى نبيه لله أن يأتى عرفات فيقف بها ثم يفيض منها فذالك قوله تعالى ثم افيضوا من حيث أفاض الناس ( آیت ۱۹۹،سورة البقرة ٢) (ابوداود شریف (داؤد شریف، باب الوقوف بعرفہ ، ص۲۸۰، نمبر ۱۹۱۰) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ قریش کے لوگ اور لوگوں سے الگ ہو کر مزدلفہ میں ٹھہرا کرتے تھے تو انکو اللہ نے حکم دیا کہ اور لوگوں کے ساتھ عرفہ میں ٹھہرا کریں، الگ تھلگ نہ ٹھہرا کریں۔(۳) اس حدیث میں بھی ہے۔ عن ابن عمر قال غدا رسول الله من منى حين صلى الصبح صبيحة يوم عرفة حتى أتى عرفة فنزل بنمرة و هى منزل الامام . (داؤد شریف، باب الخروج الى عرفة ص ۲۸۰، نمبر ۱۹۱۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ صبح کو عرفات کے لئے چلے اور مسجد نمرہ کے پاس ٹھہرے۔۔ جب منی سے عرفات پہنچتے ہیں تو میدان عرفات کے شروع ہی میں مسجد نمرہ ہے۔ ترجمه : (۱۳۳۳) اور امام حج یا اس کے نائب کے ساتھ نماز ظہر وعصر پڑھے۔ اس کے بعد کہ امام دو خطبے پڑھے اور ان کے درمیان میں بیٹھے۔ اور دونوں فرضوں کو ایک اذان اور دوا قامتوں سے پڑھے۔
تشریح : مسجد نمرہ میں حج کا امام یا انکا نائب ظہر اور عصر کی نماز ایک ساتھ پڑھائے ، اور جمع بین الصلاتین کریں ، دونوں خطبتين يجلس بينهما ويصلى الفرضين باذان واقامتين (۱۳۳۴ ) ولا يجمع بينهما الا بشرطين نمازوں سے پہلے اذان دی جائے گی ، اور دوا قامتیں کہی جائیں گی ، ایک اقامت ظہر کی نماز کے لئے اور دوسری اقامت عصر کی نماز کے لئے ۔ اور دونوں نمازوں سے پہلے جمعہ کی طرح دو خطبے ہوں ، اور دونوں کے درمیان امام بیٹھے ۔
وجه : (۱) حدیث میں ہے۔دخلنا على جابر بن عبد الله فسال عن القوم حتى انتهى الى . حتى اذا زاغت الشـمـس امـر بـالـقـصـواء فـرحـلـت لـه فـاتـي بطن الوادى فخطب الناس وقال ان دمائكم واموالكم حرام عليكم.... ثم اذن ثم اقام فصلى الظهر ثم اقام فصلى العصر و لم يفصل بينهما شيء . (مسلم شریف، باب حجة النبی ص ص ۵۱۵، نمبر ۲۹۵۰/۱۲۱۸ / ابو داؤد شریف ، باب صفہ حجتہ النبی ، ص ۲۷۸، نمبر ۱۹۰۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ نماز سے پہلے دو خطبے دئے ، اور ظہر اور عصر کی نماز ایک ساتھ پڑھائی ، اور دونوں کے لئے ایک اذان کہی اور دو اقامت کہی ۔ (۲) دو خطبے دینے کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے ، عن جابر فی حجة الاسلام قال فراح النبي علا الى الموقف بعرفة فخطب الناس الخطبة الاولى ثم اذن بلال ثم أخذ النبى فى الخطبة الثانية ففرغ من الخطبة و بلال من الاذان ثم أقام بلال فصلى الظهر ثم أقام فصلى العصر ( سنن بیہقی ، باب الخطبة یوم عرفة بعد الزوال والجمع بين الظهر والعصر با ذان واقامتين، ج خامس ،ص ۱۸۵ نمبر ۹۴۵۵) اس حدیث میں دو خطبوں کا تذکرہ ہے۔
ترجمه : (۱۳۳۴) اور ان دونوں کو دو شرطوں احرام اور امام حج کے بغیر جمع نہ کرے۔ تشريح : امام ابو حنیفہ کی رائے ہے کہ تین شرطیں ہوں تو جمع بین الصلاتین کر سکتا ہے [1] احرام کی حالت ہو [۲] میدان عرفات ہو [۳] اور امام حج نماز پڑھا رہے ہوں تو جمع بین الصلاتین کر سکتا ہے، ورنہ نہیں، کیونکہ آیت میں ہے کہ نماز اپنے وقت پر پڑھو اس لئے اس سے مقدم یا موخر اسی وقت کی جائے گی جب وہ شرائط پائی جائیں، جن شرائط کے ساتھ حضور نے مقدم فرمایا تھا اور حضور نے ان تین شرطوں کے ساتھ مقدم کیا ہے اس لئے یہ تین شرطیں ضروری ہیں۔
وجه : (۱) آیت میں ہے۔ ان الصلوة كانت على المومنين كتابا موقوتا. (آیت ۰۳ اسورۃ النساء۴) آیت سے معلوم ہوا کہ ہر نماز اپنے اپنے وقت کے ساتھ متعین ہے اس لئے بغیر مضبوط دلیل کے نماز اپنے وقت سے مقدم ومؤخر نہیں ہوسکتی ۔ (۲) جمع بین الصلاتین کا اصل مقصد ہے کہ دوبارہ امام کے ساتھ ملنا مشکل ہے اس لئے دونوں نمازیں ایک ساتھ پڑھ لیں لیکن جولوگ اپنے اپنے خیموں میں پڑھتے ہیں انکو ظہر کی نماز ظہر کے وقت میں اور عصر کی نماز عصر کے وقت میں پڑھنے میں کوئی دشواری نہیں ہے اس لئے انکے لئے جمع کرنے کی مجبوری نہیں ہے۔ (۳) عن ابراهيم قال : اذا صليت في رحلك بعرفة فصل كل واحدة منهما لوقتها و اجعل لكل واحدة منهما اذانا و اقامة - (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب في الرجل يصلي بعرفة في رحلہ ولا يشهد الصلوة مع الامام، ج ثالث ،ص ۲۵۲، نمبر ۱۴۰۳۵) اس اثر میں ہے کہ اپنے کجاوے میں نماز پڑھے تو ہر نماز اپنے اپنے
Section: Sequence of Hajj actions. And he descends near Masjid al-Khayf (1332). Then after sunrise, he goes to Arafat and stays there. When the sun declines, he comes to Masjid Namirah (1333) and prays with the great Imam or his deputy Zuhr and Asr after he delivers the sermon... (hadith references) ... From this hadith it is known that on the 8th of Dhul Hijjah he comes to Mina, and prays from Zuhr to Fajr prayers in Mina. Translation: (1332) Then after sunrise, he goes towards Arafat and stays there. So when the sun declines, he comes to Masjid Namirah. Explanation: On the 9th of Dhul Hijjah, when the sun rises, he goes to Arafat and stays there, and when the sun declines, he comes to Masjid Namirah so that he can pray with the Imam of Hajj. Evidence: (1) In this hadith... (2) From Aisha... (3) From Ibn Umar... Translation: (1333) And he prays Zuhr and Asr with the Imam of Hajj or his deputy, after the Imam delivers two sermons and sits between them, and prays the two obligatory prayers with one adhan and two iqamahs. Explanation: In Masjid Namirah, the Imam of Hajj or his deputy leads Zuhr and Asr together, making jama' bayn al-salatayn, with two sermons sitting between them, and prays the two obligatory prayers with one adhan and two iqamahs. (1334) And he does not combine them except with two conditions: ihram and the Imam of Hajj. Explanation: Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion is that jama' bayn al-salatayn can be done if three conditions are met: (1) state of ihram, (2) being in the field of Arafat, (3) the Imam of Hajj is leading the prayer. Otherwise not, because the verse says prayer is tied to its time, so it can only be advanced or delayed when those conditions are present, which the Prophet advanced with these three conditions, so these three conditions are necessary. Evidence: (1) The verse 'Indeed prayer has been a timed ordinance for the believers' (4:103). From the verse it is known that each prayer is fixed to its time, so without strong evidence, prayer cannot be advanced or delayed. (2) The original purpose of jama' is that it is difficult to meet the Imam again, so they pray both together. But those who pray in their own tents have no difficulty in praying Zuhr at its time and Asr at its time, so there is no compulsion for them to combine. (3) From Ibrahim: 'If you pray in your dwelling at Arafat, pray each one at its time, and for each one make a separate adhan and iqamah.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah) This report states that if one prays in his own saddle, then each prayer is at its own time.
Source pages p. 365

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school regarding the specific sequence of actions on the day of Arafah during Hajj. The author begins by stating that after spending the night of the 8th at Mina, the pilgrim proceeds to Arafat after sunrise on the 9th. Upon the sun's declination (zawal), he is to go to Masjid Namirah, where the Imam of Hajj (or his deputy) will deliver two sermons, then lead Zuhr and Asr prayers together (jama') with one adhan and two iqamahs. The author then provides hadith evidence from Sahih Muslim and Abu Dawood, showing the Prophet's practice of delivering two sermons and combining the prayers at Arafat. The text then explains the Hanafi position on the permissibility of jama' between Zuhr and Asr on the day of Arafah. According to Imam Abu Hanifah, three conditions are necessary for joining: (1) the pilgrim must be in the state of ihram, (2) he must be in the field of Arafat, and (3) he must pray behind the Imam of Hajj. The author supports this with the Quranic verse (4:103) that prayer has fixed times, so deviation requires strong evidence, which is the Prophet's practice under these specific conditions. The wisdom behind joining is that it overcomes the difficulty of meeting the Imam again after the first prayer. Therefore, those who pray in their own tents away from the Imam are not permitted to join, as they face no hardship. This is reinforced by the athar (report) from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i, instructing such individuals to pray each prayer at its own time with separate adhan and iqamah.

Key Terms
جمع بین الصلاتین (jama' bayn al-salatayn): Combining two obligatory prayers (Zuhr and Asr) at one time, either by advancing the second to the time of the first or delaying the first to the time of the second.
مسجد نمرہ (Masjid Namirah): A mosque located at the edge of the plain of Arafat, where the Prophet (peace be upon him) camped and delivered the sermon on the day of Arafah.
امام حج (Imam al-Hajj): The leader appointed to lead the Hajj congregation in prayer and rituals, typically the ruler or his deputy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifah, what are the three conditions required for joining Zuhr and Asr prayers on the day of Arafah?
A) Ihram, being in Mina, praying behind any imam
B) Ihram, being in Arafat, praying behind the Imam of Hajj
C) Being in Arafat, after sunset, with the intention of combining
D) None; joining is generally permissible for all pilgrims

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits joining Zuhr and Asr on Arafah only when one is in ihram, in Arafat, and behind the Imam of Hajj; otherwise each prayer must be at its time.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate

Combining Dhuhr and Asr at Arafat: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on combining prayers at Arafat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions required by Abu Hanifa for combining prayers at Arafat, explain the Sahibayn's opposing view, and apply the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) to a contemporary scenario.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa restricts combining at Arafat to those behind the Imam; the Sahibayn allow it for all.

The combining of Dhuhr and Asr at Arafat is a unique dispensation in the Hanafi school. However, a key disagreement exists between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two foremost students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), regarding who may avail this concession. This lesson unpacks the conditions, evidence, and practical consequences of this intra-Hanafi dispute, enabling you to apply the correct ruling in today's Hajj context.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the two positions
State clearly the contested point: May a pilgrim combine Dhuhr and Asr at Arafat when not praying behind the Imam of Hajj? Abu Hanifa says no (without three conditions), the Sahibayn say yes.
2
State Abu Hanifa's three conditions and his evidence
List the three conditions: ihram, being at Arafat, praying behind the Imam of Hajj. Then summarise his proofs: Quran 4:103 (fixed times), the purpose of combining (difficulty), and the hadith of Jabir showing the Prophet only combined with the imam.
Note the use of the hadith from Muslim and Abu Dawud.
3
State the Sahibayn's unconditional position and their evidence
The Sahibayn hold that any pilgrim at Arafat may combine, regardless of whether they pray with the imam. Their proofs: abundant unconditional hadiths about combining at Arafat, and the practice of Ibn Umar who combined when alone.
Athar from Ibn Abi Shaybah and Bayhaqi.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical difference: a pilgrim who prays alone in his tent must pray each prayer at its time according to Abu Hanifa, but may combine according to the Sahibayn.
5
Apply the contemporary resolution
The text states that nowadays with large crowds, acting on the Sahibayn's view is not objectionable. Discuss how this reflects a move toward the Sahibayn's position in fatwa due to necessity.
This illustrates the dynamic nature of fatwa within the Hanafi school.

ترجمه : (۱۳۳۴) اور ان دونوں کو دو شرطوں احرام اور امام حج کے بغیر جمع نہ کرے۔ تشريح : امام ابو حنیفہ کی رائے ہے کہ تین شرطیں ہوں تو جمع بین الصلاتین کر سکتا ہے [1] احرام کی حالت ہو [۲] میدان عرفات ہو [۳] اور امام حج نماز پڑھا رہے ہوں تو جمع بین الصلاتین کر سکتا ہے، ورنہ نہیں، کیونکہ آیت میں ہے کہ نماز اپنے وقت پر پڑھو اس لئے اس سے مقدم یا موخر اسی وقت کی جائے گی جب وہ شرائط پائی جائیں، جن شرائط کے ساتھ حضور نے مقدم فرمایا تھا اور حضور نے ان تین شرطوں کے ساتھ مقدم کیا ہے اس لئے یہ تین شرطیں ضروری ہیں۔
وجه : (۱) آیت میں ہے۔ ان الصلوة كانت على المومنين كتابا موقوتا. (آیت ۰۳ اسورۃ النساء۴) آیت سے معلوم ہوا کہ ہر نماز اپنے اپنے وقت کے ساتھ متعین ہے اس لئے بغیر مضبوط دلیل کے نماز اپنے وقت سے مقدم ومؤخر نہیں ہوسکتی ۔ (۲) جمع بین الصلاتین کا اصل مقصد ہے کہ دوبارہ امام کے ساتھ ملنا مشکل ہے اس لئے دونوں نمازیں ایک ساتھ پڑھ لیں لیکن جولوگ اپنے اپنے خیموں میں پڑھتے ہیں انکو ظہر کی نماز ظہر کے وقت میں اور عصر کی نماز عصر کے وقت میں پڑھنے میں کوئی دشواری نہیں ہے اس لئے انکے لئے جمع کرنے کی مجبوری نہیں ہے۔ (۳) عن ابراهيم قال : اذا صليت في رحلك بعرفة فصل كل واحدة منهما لوقتها و اجعل لكل واحدة منهما اذانا و اقامة - (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب في الرجل يصلي بعرفة في رحلہ ولا يشهد الصلوة مع الامام، ج ثالث ،ص ۲۵۲، نمبر ۱۴۰۳۵) اس اثر میں ہے کہ اپنے کجاوے میں نماز پڑھے تو ہر نماز اپنے اپنے
وقت میں پڑھے۔ (۴) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور کے ساتھ یعنی امام کے ساتھ نماز پڑھی تب ہی جمع بین الصلوتین کی ، حدیث یہ ہے۔ قال دخـلـنـا عـلـى جابر بن عبد الله ... ثم اذن ثم اقام فصلى الظهر ثم أقام فصلى العصر ولم يصل بينهما شيئا ثم ركب رسول الله حتى اتى الموقف. (مسلم شریف ، باب حجتہ النبی ص ۵۱۵، نمبر ۲۹۵۰/۱۲۱۸ را بو داؤد شریف ، باب صفتہ حجتہ النبی و ل اللہ ص ۲۷۸، نمبر ۱۹۰۵) اس حدیث سے استدلال کیا جا سکتا ہے کہ امام کے ساتھ نماز پڑھے تب ہی جمع بین الصلو تین کر سکتا ہے۔
نوٹ: صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ جو لوگ امام سے الگ ہو کر اپنے کجاوے میں نماز پڑھے وہ لوگ بھی جمع بین الصلوتین کر سکتے ہیں، اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ جمع بین الصلوتین اس لئے کرتے ہیں کہ زیادہ سے زیادہ وقوف عرفہ کر سکے ، اور جو تنہا نماز پڑھتا ہے اس کو بھی زیادہ سے زیادہ وقوف عرفہ کی ضرورت پڑتی ہے اس لئے وہ بھی جمع بین الصلوتین کرسکتا ہے۔
وجه : (۱) صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ حدیث میں عرفات میں جمع بین الصلوتین کا ذکر کثرت سے ہے اور بغیر کسی شرط کے ہے۔ اس لئے جو لوگ امام سے الگ نماز پڑھیں گے وہ بھی جمع بین الصلوتین کریں گے۔ (۲) انکی دلیل یہ اثر ہے۔ ان ابـن عـمـر كـان
يجمع بينهما اذا فاته مع الامام يوم عرفة ( سنن بیعتی ، باب الخطبة يوم عرفة والجمع بین الظهر والعصر، ج خامس ص ، ۱۸۶، للبيهقي ص،۱۸۶،
نمبر ۹۴۵۶ / مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب من جمع بین الظهر والعصر بعرفات ، ج ثالث ، ص ۱۲۸۸، نمبر ۱۴۴۰۶) اس اثر میں ہے کہ حضرت ابن عمر نے امام سے الگ ہو کر نماز پڑھی تب بھی جمع بین الصلوتین کی۔ (۳) اس اثر میں ہے ۔ عن ابن عمر انه كان اذا فاتته الصلوة مع الامام بعرفة جمع بين الظهر والعصر في رحله . (مصنف ابن ابي هيبة ، باب في الرجل يصلى بعرفة في رحله ولا يشهد الصلوة مع الامام، ج ثالث ص ۲۵۲، نمبر ۱۴۰۳۴) اس اثر میں ہے کہ کجاوے میں بھی نماز پڑھے تو جمع کر سکتا ہے۔ آج کل ۳۳ لاکھ حاجی جمع ہوتے ہیں اس لئے صاحبین کے مسلک پر عمل کر لیا تو کوئی حرج کی بات نہیں ہے۔ اور دوسرے مسلک والوں سے تو بالکل نہیں جھگڑنا چاہئے۔
Chapter on the Composition of the Actions of Hajj. Two sermons, sitting between them, and the two obligatory prayers are performed with one adhan and two iqamahs (1334). And they are not combined except with two conditions: before the prayers the adhan will be given, and two iqamahs will be said, one iqamah for Dhuhr and another for Asr. And before both prayers, two sermons like Jumu'ah, and the imam sits between them. Evidence: (1) Hadith: We entered upon Jabir ibn Abdullah... until the sun declined, he ordered the she-camel to be saddled for him, then he came to the bottom of the valley and delivered a sermon to the people saying: 'Your blood and your property are sacred...' Then he called the adhan, then the iqamah, and prayed Dhuhr, then the iqamah, and prayed Asr, and did not separate between them with anything. (Muslim, no. 1218; Abu Dawud, no. 1905) In this hadith, he gave two sermons before the prayer, and prayed Dhuhr and Asr together with one adhan and two iqamahs. (2) The evidence for two sermons is the hadith from Jabir in Hajjat al-Islam: The Prophet went to the standing at Arafat and delivered the first sermon, then Bilal gave the adhan, then the Prophet began the second sermon; when he finished the sermon and Bilal finished the adhan, Bilal gave the iqamah and he prayed Dhuhr, then gave the iqamah and prayed Asr. (Baihaqi, no. 9455) This hadith mentions two sermons. Translation: (1334) And do not combine them except with two conditions: ihram and the imam of Hajj. Explanation: Imam Abu Hanifa is of the opinion that if three conditions are met, one can combine: (1) state of ihram, (2) the plain of Arafat, (3) the imam of Hajj is leading the prayer. Otherwise not, because the verse says to pray at their appointed times. Therefore, advancing or delaying is only allowed when these conditions are present, as the Prophet advanced only with these three conditions. So these three conditions are necessary. Evidence: (1) The verse: 'Indeed prayer is a prescribed duty on the believers at specific times' (4:103). This shows prayer is fixed to its time, so without strong evidence it cannot be advanced or delayed. (2) The purpose of combining is that it is difficult to join the imam again, so they pray together. But those who pray in their tents have no difficulty praying each prayer at its time, so they have no necessity to combine. (3) From Ibrahim: 'If you pray in your camp at Arafat, then pray each one at its time, and make for each one an adhan and iqamah.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, no. 14035) This athar says to pray each at its time. (4) The hadith that the Prophet prayed with the imam, so only with the imam can one combine. Note: The Sahibayn say that those who separate from the imam and pray in their tents can also combine, because the reason for combining is to maximize standing at Arafat, and the one who prays alone also needs to maximize standing. Evidence: (1) The Sahibayn say that the hadith about combining at Arafat is abundant and unconditional. So those who pray separately from the imam can also combine. (2) Their evidence: Ibn Umar used to combine if he missed prayer with the imam on the day of Arafat. (Baihaqi, no. 9456; Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, no. 14406) This athar shows that Ibn Umar combined when separate from the imam. (3) Another athar: Ibn Umar used to combine Dhuhr and Asr in his camp if he missed the prayer with the imam at Arafat. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, no. 14034) This shows combining can be done in camp. Nowadays 33 lakh pilgrims gather, so acting on the Sahibayn's position is not objectionable. And one should not quarrel with those of other schools.
Source pages p. 366

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the conditions for combining Dhuhr and Asr at Arafat. The text begins by stating the general ruling: two sermons, with sitting between them, and the two prayers performed with one adhan and two iqamahs. The core disagreement is between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two foremost students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn). Abu Hanifa holds that combining requires three conditions: being in the state of ihram, being at the plain of Arafat, and praying behind the Imam of Hajj (the leader of the Hajj caravan). He argues that since prayer times are fixed by the Quran (4:103), any deviation requires strong evidence, and the Prophet's practice shows he only combined when leading the prayer at Arafat. The Sahibayn counter that the hadiths about combining at Arafat are general and unconditional, and that the purpose of combining is to maximize time for standing (wuquf) at Arafat, which applies to everyone, not just those with the imam. They cite the practice of Ibn Umar, who combined even when praying alone in his camp. The text concludes by noting that due to the huge crowds today (33 lakh pilgrims), acting on the Sahibayn's view is not objectionable, and one should not quarrel with other schools. The author thus leans toward the Sahibayn for practical application, while still presenting Abu Hanifa's position as the standard.

Key Terms
جمع بین الصلاتین (jam' bayn al-salatayn): Combining two prayers (Dhuhr and Asr) at Arafat during Hajj, performed at the earlier time (Dhuhr time) with one adhan and two iqamahs.
احرام (ihram): The sacred state of Hajj, marked by specific clothing and prohibitions, required for the validity of Hajj rituals.
امام حج (imam al-hajj): The leader of the Hajj caravan who leads the congregational prayers at Arafat.
صاحبین (al-Sahibayn): The two companions of Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, what is the condition for combining Dhuhr and Asr at Arafat?
A) Being in ihram
B) Praying behind the Imam of Hajj
C) Being at the plain of Arafat
D) Both A and B

Key Takeaway
The intra-Hanafi dispute on combining at Arafat centers on whether praying behind the Imam of Hajj is a condition; the contemporary mufta bihi follows the Sahibayn's unconditional permission due to necessity of large crowds.

Not Praying Nafl Between Combined Prayers at Arafat
States no nafl between combined prayers at Arafat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on omitting nafl prayers between Dhuhr and Asr when combining at Arafat, citing the Prophetic evidence.

Core Idea
No nafl between Dhuhr and Asr at Arafat — follow the Prophet's example.

In Hajj, at Arafat, the Prophet Muhammad combined Dhuhr and Asr without any supererogatory prayers in between. This lesson examines that practice and its ruling in the Hanafi school, emphasizing that the sunnah is to omit any voluntary prayers during that interval.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act in question is praying nafl (supererogatory prayer) between Dhuhr and Asr while combining at Arafat. The ruling is that it is sunnah to omit it.
The ruling is not obligation or prohibition, but a recommended omission.
2
Locate the Prophetic evidence
The primary evidence is the hadith of Jabir ibn Abdullah, which describes the Prophet's actions at Arafat. The hadith explicitly states that the Prophet did not pray anything between the two prayers.
The hadith is authentic (recorded by Muslim and Abu Dawud).
3
Analyze wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's deliberate omission (non-action) indicates a sunnah (recommended practice). In Hanafi usul, the Prophet's actions that are not clearly obligatory or prohibitive indicate preference.
Silence (absence of prayer) here is considered a positive practice.
4
Determine the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that it is sunnah to omit all nafl prayers, including the regular sunnah of Dhuhr, between the two prayers at Arafat. The mufta bihi is to refrain from praying any voluntary prayers.
This is based on the zahir riwayah from the six core books.
5
Note the context and limits
This ruling only applies when combining Dhuhr and Asr at Arafat during Hajj. In other situations, the regular sunnan prayers should be performed as usual.
The specificity of place and circumstance is crucial.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof that no nafl prayer should be offered between Dhuhr and Asr when combining at Arafat. The evidence is the explicit practice of the Prophet as narrated by Jabir ibn Abdullah: the Prophet did not pray anything between the two prayers. This is a confirmed sunnah, and thus one should avoid praying nafl during that time. The Hanafi school follows this practice. The condition only applies when combining at Arafat; normally, one would pray the sunnah of Dhuhr before Asr, but in this specific situation, the sunnah is not performed due to the Prophetic example.

Key Terms
نفل (nafl): A supererogatory prayer that is not obligatory but recommended at other times.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
When combining prayers at Arafat, it is sunnah to omit all voluntary prayers between them, following the Prophet's example.

Hajj — Pilgrimage

Combining at Arafat: The Imam Condition vs. Individual Permission
Intra-Hanafi dispute on combining with the Imam vs. alone

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain both Hanafi views on the condition for combining Zuhr and Asr at Arafat and apply the practical ruling (mufta bihi) in a modern Hajj scenario.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa requires the Imam for combining; the Sahibayn allow it for all pilgrims to maximize wuquf.

Combining the Zuhr and Asr prayers at Arafat is a well-known sunnah of Hajj, but the Hanafi school includes a subtle intra-madhhab dispute: does one need to be behind the official Imam to perform the combination, or can any pilgrim combine individually? This lesson explores the evidence from hadith and the reasoning of the two sides, and concludes with the practical guidance for today's massive gatherings.

Guided Path
1
Identify Abu Hanifa's position and its evidence
Read the hadith of Jabir cited in the text. Note that the Prophet (ﷺ) combined Zuhr and Asr while leading the prayer, and did not pray any nafl between them. Abu Hanifa uses this to argue that combining is only valid when praying behind the imam.
The focus is on the phrase 'لم يصل بينهما شيئا' (he did not pray anything between them).
2
Identify the Sahibayn's position and their evidence
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) counter that the purpose of combining is to maximise time at Arafat (wuquf), and that this purpose applies to anyone at Arafat, regardless of whether they pray with the imam. They cite the practice of Ibn Umar, who combined even when he missed the imam.
Their evidence includes athar from Ibn Umar combining in his saddle.
3
Analyse the difference in interpretation
Abu Hanifa sees the hadith of Jabir as establishing a condition (imam), while the Sahibayn see it as merely descriptive. The Sahibayn also use istihsan (juristic preference) to prioritise the goal of wuquf.
This is a classic example of how istihsan can override a literal reading of a hadith when a greater maslaha is present.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The difference affects every pilgrim who cannot or does not pray with the official imam. Following Abu Hanifa, they must pray each salah in its own time (Zuhr at zawal, Asr later). Following the Sahibayn, they may combine even alone.
Today, with over 3 million pilgrims, many may find it difficult to be with the imam. The text notes that following the Sahibayn is harmless (la haraj).
5
Note the mufta bihi ruling and modern application
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school is Abu Hanifa's, but because of the huge crowds, many contemporary scholars permit following the Sahibayn's view as a concession. The matn also prohibits praying any nafl between the combined prayers.
The prohibition of nafl is agreed upon by both sides in this context.

Source Text

فصل تركيب افعال الحج صل الاحرام والامام الاعظم (۱۳۳۵ ) ولا يفصل بين الصلوتين بنافلة وقت میں پڑھے۔ (۴) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور کے ساتھ یعنی امام کے ساتھ نماز پڑھی تب ہی جمع بین الصلوتین کی ، حدیث یہ ہے۔ قال دخـلـنـا عـلـى جابر بن عبد الله ... ثم اذن ثم اقام فصلى الظهر ثم أقام فصلى العصر ولم يصل بينهما شيئا ثم ركب رسول الله حتى اتى الموقف. (مسلم شریف ، باب حجتہ النبی ص ۵۱۵، نمبر ۲۹۵۰/۱۲۱۸ را بو داؤد شریف ، باب صفتہ حجتہ النبی و ل اللہ ص ۲۷۸، نمبر ۱۹۰۵) اس حدیث سے استدلال کیا جا سکتا ہے کہ امام کے ساتھ نماز پڑھے تب ہی جمع بین الصلو تین کر سکتا ہے۔ نوٹ: صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ جو لوگ امام سے الگ ہو کر اپنے کجاوے میں نماز پڑھے وہ لوگ بھی جمع بین الصلوتین کر سکتے ہیں، اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ جمع بین الصلوتین اس لئے کرتے ہیں کہ زیادہ سے زیادہ وقوف عرفہ کر سکے ، اور جو تنہا نماز پڑھتا ہے اس کو بھی زیادہ سے زیادہ وقوف عرفہ کی ضرورت پڑتی ہے اس لئے وہ بھی جمع بین الصلوتین کرسکتا ہے۔ وجه : (۱) صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ حدیث میں عرفات میں جمع بین الصلوتین کا ذکر کثرت سے ہے اور بغیر کسی شرط کے ہے۔ اس لئے جو لوگ امام سے الگ نماز پڑھیں گے وہ بھی جمع بین الصلوتین کریں گے۔ (۲) انکی دلیل یہ اثر ہے۔ ان ابـن عـمـر کـان يجمع بينهما اذا فاته مع الامام يوم عرفة ( سنن بیعتی ، باب الخطبة يوم عرفة والجمع بین الظهر والعصر، ج خامس ص ، ۱۸۶، للبيهقي ص،۱۸۶، نمبر ۹۴۵۶ / مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب من جمع بین الظهر والعصر بعرفات ، ج ثالث ، ص ۱۲۸۸، نمبر ۱۴۴۰۶) اس اثر میں ہے کہ حضرت ابن عمر نے امام سے الگ ہو کر نماز پڑھی تب بھی جمع بین الصلوتین کی۔ (۳) اس اثر میں ہے ۔ عن ابن عمر انه كان اذا فاتته الصلوة مع الامام بعرفة جمع بين الظهر والعصر في رحله . (مصنف ابن ابي هيبة ، باب في الرجل يصلى بعرفة في رحله ولا يشهد الصلوة مع الامام، ج ثالث ص ۲۵۲، نمبر ۱۴۰۳۴) اس اثر میں ہے کہ کجاوے میں بھی نماز پڑھے تو جمع کر سکتا ہے۔ آج کل ۳۳ لاکھ حاجی جمع ہوتے ہیں اس لئے صاحبین کے مسلک پر عمل کر لیا تو کوئی حرج کی بات نہیں ہے۔ اور دوسرے مسلک والوں سے تو بالکل نہیں جھگڑنا چاہئے۔ ترجمه : (۱۳۳۵) اور ان دونوں نمازوں کے درمیان نفل سے فاصلہ نہ کرے۔ تشریح : جو لوگ جمع بین الصلاتین کر رہے ہوں وہ ظہر اور عصر کے درمیان نفل نہ پڑھے۔ وجه : (۱)قال دخلنا على جابر بن عبد الله ... ثم اذن ثم أقام فصلى الظهر ثم اقام فصلى العصر ولم يصل بينهما شيئا ثم ركب رسول الله حتى اتى الموقف. (مسلم شریف ، باب حجتہ النبی ص ۵۱۵، نمبر ۲۹۵۰/۱۲۱۸ را بو داؤد شریف ، باب صفتہ حجتہ النبی ، ص ۲۷۸، نمبر ۱۹۰۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ دونوں نمازوں کے درمیان کچھ نہیں پڑھی۔(۲) (۲) اس حدیث میں بھی ہے کہ درمیان میں نقل نہ پڑھے . عن جعفر بن محمد عن ابيه أن النبي الله صلى الظهر و
Section: Structure of Hajj actions. The ihram and the Grand Imam (1335): And do not separate between the two prayers with supererogatory prayer. (4) In this hadith, it is that he prayed with the Prophet, i.e., with the Imam; only then did he combine the two prayers. The hadith is: 'We entered upon Jabir ibn Abdullah... then he gave adhan, then iqamah, prayed Zuhr, then iqamah, prayed Asr, and did not pray anything between them, then the Messenger of Allah rode until he came to the standing place.' (Muslim, Bab Hajjat al-Nabi, p. 515, no. 2950/1218; Abu Dawood, Bab Sifat Hajjat al-Nabi, p. 278, no. 1905). From this hadith it can be deduced that only if one prays with the Imam can he combine. Note: The two companions (Sahibayn) state that those who pray separately from the Imam in their own camel litters can also combine. The reason is that they combine in order to maximize the standing at Arafat, and the one who prays alone also needs to maximize standing at Arafat, so he can also combine. Proofs: (1) The Sahibayn say that the hadith mentions combining at Arafat frequently and without any condition. Therefore those who pray separately from the Imam will also combine. (2) Their proof is this athar: 'Ibn Umar used to combine the two prayers when he missed (praying with) the Imam on the Day of Arafah.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab al-Khutbah yawm Arafah wal-Jam' bayn al-Zuhr wal-Asr, vol. 5, p. 186, no. 9456; Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, Bab man jama'a bayn al-Zuhr wal-Asr bi-Arafat, vol. 3, p. 1288, no. 14406). This athar shows that Ibn Umar combined even when separating from the Imam. (3) This athar: 'From Ibn Umar that when he missed the prayer with the Imam at Arafat, he combined Zuhr and Asr in his saddle.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, vol. 3, p. 252, no. 14034). This athar shows that one can combine even when praying in the saddle. Nowadays 33 lakh pilgrims gather, so following the Sahibayn's school is not harmful. And one should not quarrel with those of other schools. Translation: (1335) And do not separate between the two prayers with supererogatory prayer. Commentary: Those who are combining should not pray nafl between Zuhr and Asr. Proof: (1) We entered upon Jabir ibn Abdullah... (repeat of earlier hadith). (2) This hadith also says do not pray nafl between them: from Ja'far ibn Muhammad from his father that the Prophet prayed Zuhr and... (incomplete).
Source pages p. 367

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling of combining the Zuhr and Asr prayers at Arafat during Hajj. It begins with the matn stating that one should not perform any supererogatory prayer between the two combined prayers. The commentary then presents an intra-Hanafi dispute. Imam Abu Hanifa (the Grand Imam) is of the view that combining the prayers is conditional upon praying behind the Imam (the official Hajj imam). He supports this with the hadith of Jabir, where the Prophet did not pray any nafl between Zuhr and Asr at Arafat, implying that he was leading the prayer. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) differ: they allow combining even for those who pray alone, as long as they are within Arafat. Their rationale is that the purpose of combining is to maximize the time spent in wuquf (standing at Arafat), and this purpose is equally relevant for those who pray alone. They support their view with the practice of Ibn Umar, who combined even when he missed praying with the Imam. The commentary then notes that due to the huge crowds today, it is permissible to follow the Sahibayn's position to avoid hardship. Finally, it reiterates the ruling about not separating the prayers with nafl, citing another hadith from Ja'far ibn Muhammad.

Key Terms
جمع بین الصلاتین (jam' bayn al-salatayn): Performing two obligatory prayers (Zuhr and Asr, or Maghrib and Isha) at the same time, either at the earlier or later time.
صاحبین (al-Sahibayn): The two main disciples of Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
وقوف عرفہ (wuquf Arafah): The essential standing at Arafat on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah; a pillar of Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what is required to combine Zuhr and Asr at Arafat?
A) Being in the state of ihram
B) Praying behind the Imam
C) Being on the mountain of mercy
D) Having performed wuquf

Key Takeaway
At Arafat, combining Zuhr and Asr is a sunnah, but Abu Hanifa requires praying behind the Imam; the Sahibayn allow it for all pilgrims to maximize standing, and following either is valid within the Hanafi school.

Praying in Own Time if Missing the Imam at Arafat
Ruling that each prayer is prayed in its normal time if one misses the Imam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a pilgrim misses the Imam at Arafat and identify the condition that makes combining invalid.

Core Idea
Combining prayers at Arafat requires praying behind the Imam; otherwise, pray each in its own time.

This lesson addresses a specific scenario during Hajj: what happens if a pilgrim at Arafat does not manage to pray Zuhr and Asr behind the Imam of Hajj? The concise ruling (matn) gives a clear answer—each prayer is prayed at its normal time. The commentary explains the underlying Hanafi principle: the Imam's presence is a necessary condition for the concession of combining prayers. Without it, the original obligation to pray each prayer in its prescribed time applies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The ruling applies when a pilgrim is at Arafat during Hajj and does not catch up with the 'Grand Imam' (the Imam leading the congregational combined prayer).
The 'Grand Imam' here refers to the Hajj Imam, not necessarily Abu Hanifa.
2
State the ruling
The matn instructs: 'pray each one in its usual time.' That means Zuhr should be prayed in its own time (before Asr) and Asr in its own later time, without combining.
3
Identify the condition
The commentary explains that combining prayers at Arafat is a concession that requires the Imam's presence. Without it, the condition is not met, so the original rule of praying separately prevails.
This condition is specific to the Hanafi school.
4
Apply the ruling
In practice, a late-arriving pilgrim should pray Zuhr at its normal time (even if alone) and then later pray Asr at its time, without shortening or combining.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۳۳۶ ) وان لم يدرك الامام الاعظم صلّى كل واحدة في وقتها المعتاد ترجمه : (۱۳۳۶) اگر امام حج کو نہ پائے تو ہر نماز کو اپنے مقررہ وقت میں پڑھے۔ تشریح : چونکہ امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک جمع بین الصلاتین کے لئے امام ہونا شرط ہے اس لئے اگر امام حج کے ساتھ نماز نہ پڑھے تو دونوں نمازیں اپنے اپنے وقت میں پڑھے۔
(1336) And if he does not catch up with the Grand Imam, he should pray each one in its usual time. Translation: (1336) If one does not find the Imam of Hajj, then pray each prayer at its appointed time. Commentary: Because according to Imam Abu Hanifa, for combining prayers the Imam is a condition; therefore if one does not pray with the Imam of Hajj, then both prayers are prayed in their own respective times.
Source pages p. 368

Commentary
This is a concise ruling (matn) with its commentary. The matn states: if a pilgrim does not catch up with the Grand Imam (i.e., does not pray the combined prayer behind the Imam of Hajj), then each prayer (Zuhr and Asr) should be performed at its own prescribed time. The commentary explains the reason: Imam Abu Hanifa insists that the presence of the Imam is a necessary condition for the combination. Therefore, failing that condition, one must pray Zuhr in its time (not at Arafat combined) and then pray Asr in its later time (or separately if time permits). This ruling highlights the legal precision of the Hanafi school regarding the conditions of rukhsah (concession) such as combining prayers.

Key Terms
امام الاعظم (al-Imam al-A'zam): Title for Abu Hanifa, the founder of the Hanafi school.
جمع بين الصلاتين (jam' bayn al-salatayn): Combining two prayers (Zuhr and Asr, or Maghrib and Isha) at one time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in the matn, what should a pilgrim do if he does not catch up with the Imam at Arafat?
A) Combine Zuhr and Asr by himself
B) Pray only Asr because Zuhr is no longer valid
C) Pray Zuhr and Asr each in their own times
D) Perform both prayers after Maghrib

Key Takeaway
When the condition of praying behind the Imam is not met, the default obligation of praying each salah in its own time applies.

The Valid Area for Wuquf at Arafat
Ruling on the valid area for wuquf at Arafat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the valid area for wuquf at Arafat according to the Hanafi school and explain the evidence for excluding Batn 'Arnah.

Core Idea
All of Arafat is valid for wuquf, except the valley of Batn 'Arnah.

Standing at Arafat is the rukn of Hajj. This lesson clarifies where exactly one must stand. The matn states that all of Arafat is a standing place, except Batn 'Arnah. The commentary expands with hadith evidence showing the Prophet's practice and explicit statements that the entire plain is valid, while warning against Batn 'Arnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The matn states the permissible area for wuquf: all of Arafat except Batn 'Arnah.
2
Note the exception
Batn 'Arnah is excluded based on prophetic instruction.
Companions of the Elephant were punished there.
3
Understand the proof
The hadith 'I stood here, and all of Arafat is a standing place' from Muslim establishes the general ruling.
Muslim, no. 2952/1218
4
Recognize the sunnah
Standing near Jabal al-Rahmah is recommended (sunnah) but not required.
Prophet stood there.
5
Apply the ruling
Due to crowding, one may stand anywhere within Arafat's boundaries; wuquf is valid as long as not in Batn 'Arnah.
Modern application.

(۱۳۳۷) فاذا صلّى مع الامام يتوجه الى الموقف وعرفات كلها موقف الا بطن عرنة (۱۳۳۸ ) ويغتسل بعد الزوال في العصر بأذان واحد بعرفة و لم يسبح بينهما و اقامتين و صلى المغرب و العشاء بجمع بأذان واحد و اقامتين و لم يسبح بينهما ۔ (ابوداود شریف، باب صلہ حجتہ النبی ا ت ص ۲۸۰ نمبر ۱۹۰۶) اس میں بھی ہے کہ درمیان میں نفل نہ پڑھے۔ ترجمه (۱۳۳۷) امام کے ساتھ نماز پڑھ چکے تو موقف کی طرف متوجہ ہو، اور وطن عرنہ کے علاوہ پورا عرفات ٹھہرنے کی جگہ ہے تشریح : پورا عرفات ٹھہرنے کی جگہ ہے اس سے حج ادا ہو جائے گا، البتہ جبل رحمت کے پاس ٹھہر نا بہتر ہے، حضور مجبل رحمت کے پاس ٹھہرے تھے ، اورپطن عرنہ میں نہ ٹھہرے اس میں اصحاب فیل کو عذاب ہوا تھا۔ ... وجه : (۱) عرفات میں جبل رحمت کے پاس ٹھہر نا بہتر ہے اس حدیث میں ہے۔ قال دخلنا على جابر بن عبد الله . ثم ركب رسول الله حتى اتى الموقف فجعل بطن ناقة القصواء الى الصخرات وجعل حبل المشاة بين يديه واسـتـقـبـل الـقبلة فلم يزل واقفا حتى غربت الشمس وذهبت الصفرة قليلا حتى غاب القرص . (مسلم شريف، باب حجتہ النبی ص ۵۱۵، نمبر ۲۹۵۰/۱۲۱۸ ابو داؤد شریف ، باب صفتہ حجتہ النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم ، ص ۲۷۸، نمبر ۱۹۰۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور ظہر وعصر کی نماز کے بعد وقوف کے لئے جبل رحمت کے پاس آئے اور وہاں وقوف کیا صحرات سے مراد جبل رحمت کا چٹان ہے۔ اس لئے یہاں وقوف کرنا بہتر ہے۔۔ آج کل بھیڑ بہت ہوتی ہے اس لئے یہاں جگہ ملنی مشکل ہوتی ہے، اس لئے جہاں آسانی سے جگہ مل جائے وہاں ٹھہر جائے، بس شرط یہ ہے کہ میدان عرفات کے اندر اندر ہو۔ (۲) عرفات کا پورا میدان ٹھہرنے کی جگہ ہے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے، عن جابر في حديثه ذالك أن رسول الله الله الله قال نحرت ههنا و منى كلها منحر فانحروا في رحالكم و وقفت ههنا و عرفة كلها موقف ووقفت ههنا و جمع كلها موقف ۔(مسلم شریف، باب ما جاء أن عرفہ کلھا موقف ،ص ۵۱۶، نمبر ۲۹۵۲/۱۲۱۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ پورا عرفہ ٹھہرنے کی جگہ ہے ۔ (۳) بطن عرنہ میں نہ ٹھہرے اس کی وجہ یہ حدیث ہے اخبرنـی مـحـمـد بـن منكدر ان النبي الله قال عرفة كلها موقف وارتفعوا عن بطن عرنة والمزدلفة كلها موقف وارتفعوا عن محســر للبيهقى تھی ، باب حيث ما وقف من عرفته اجزاه ص ۹۴۵۹،۱۸۶ رسنن ابن ماجہ شریف باب الموقف بعرفات ص۲۲۲) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ بطن عرنہ میں نہیں ٹھہر نا چاہئے ۔ ترجمه : (۱۳۳۸) اور زوال کے بعد وقوف عرفہ کے لئے غسل کرے۔
(1337) So when he prays with the Imam, he proceeds to the standing place, and all of Arafat is a standing place except Batn 'Arnah. (1338) And he performs ghusl after zawal in the afternoon with one adhan at Arafat, and does not glorify between them, and two iqamahs, and he prays Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah (Jam') with one adhan and two iqamahs, and does not glorify between them. (Abu Dawood...). In this also it is that do not pray nafl between them. Translation: (1337) After praying with the Imam, proceed to the standing place, and all of Arafat except Batn 'Arnah is a place of standing. Commentary: All of Arafat is a standing place; from this Hajj will be valid. However, it is better to stand near Jabal al-Rahmah; the Prophet stood near Jabal al-Rahmah. Do not stand in Batn 'Arnah, because the Companions of the Elephant were punished there. ... Proofs: (1) It is better to stand near Jabal al-Rahmah as per the hadith: 'We entered upon Jabir... then the Messenger of Allah rode until he came to the standing place, and he positioned the belly of his camel towards the rocks, and placed the rope of the walkers in front of him, and faced the qiblah, and remained standing until the sun set and the yellowing went away a little until the disk disappeared.' (Muslim, etc.). In this hadith, the Prophet came to Jabal al-Rahmah for wuquf after Zuhr and Asr prayers. So standing here is better. Nowadays there is a lot of crowd, so it is difficult to get a spot; therefore, wherever one can easily get a spot, he should stand, provided it is within the plain of Arafat. (2) The entire plain of Arafat is a standing place; the proof is this hadith: from Jabir that the Prophet said: 'I sacrificed here, and all of Mina is a place of sacrifice, so sacrifice in your tents; and I stood here, and all of Arafat is a standing place; and I stood here, and all of Muzdalifah is a standing place.' (Muslim). (3) Do not stand in Batn 'Arnah; the reason is this hadith: Muhammad ibn Munkadir informed me that the Prophet said: 'All of Arafat is a standing place, and stay away from Batn 'Arnah; and all of Muzdalifah is a standing place, and stay away from Muhassir.' (al-Bayhaqi, Ibn Majah). From this, it is understood that one should not stand in Batn 'Arnah. Translation: (1338) And perform ghusl after zawal for the standing at Arafat.
Source pages p. 368

Commentary
This passage combines two rulings from the matn: (1337) the ruling on the area of wuquf, and (1338) the recommendation of ghusl before wuquf. The commentary explains that all of Arafat is valid for standing, except the valley known as Batn 'Arnah. It is recommended (sunnah) to stand near Jabal al-Rahmah, following the example of the Prophet. However, due to overcrowding, one may stand anywhere within Arafat. The proofs include hadith from Jabir showing the Prophet's spot, and the explicit statement from the Prophet that all of Arafat is a standing place. The exclusion of Batn 'Arnah is based on a hadith instructing to stay away from it. The second ruling (1338) commands ghusl after zawal (afternoon) for the wuquf, which is a sunnah practice to be in a state of purity.

Key Terms
بطن عرنة (Batn 'Arnah): A valley within the boundaries of Arafat that is excluded from the standing area.
موقف (mawqif): The place of standing during wuquf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The area near Jabal al-Rahmah
B) The western boundary
C) Batn 'Arnah
D) The flat plain

Key Takeaway
All of Arafat except Batn 'Arnah is valid for wuquf.

Ghusl Before Wuquf at Arafat
Recommendation of ghusl before wuquf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ghusl before wuquf and identify its status as sunnah muakkadah.

Core Idea
Ghusl before wuquf is a sunnah muakkadah, not wajib.

The matn instructs the pilgrim to perform ghusl after zawal for wuquf. This lesson clarifies that this ghusl is a recommended practice (sunnah) to be in a state of purity, following the Prophet's example. The Hanafi school classifies it as sunnah muakkadah, emphasizing that wuquf is valid without it.

Guided Path
1
Translate the ruling
The matn says: 'He performs ghusl after zawal' – meaning the pilgrim should bathe after noon before proceeding to Arafat.
2
Identify the legal status
This ghusl is sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah) according to the Hanafi school.
Not fard or wajib.
3
Understand the timing
It is performed after zawal (sun pass zenith) before going to Arafat for wuquf.
Zawal is around noon.
4
Note the purpose
To present oneself in a state of ritual purity at the standing, emulating the Prophet.
5
Apply the ruling
If one does not perform ghusl, wuquf is still valid, but the sunnah is missed.
Combining with other acts of purification.

(۱۳۳۷) فاذا صلّى مع الامام يتوجه الى الموقف وعرفات كلها موقف الا بطن عرنة (۱۳۳۸ ) ويغتسل بعد الزوال في العصر بأذان واحد بعرفة و لم يسبح بينهما و اقامتين و صلى المغرب و العشاء بجمع بأذان واحد و اقامتين و لم يسبح بينهما ۔ (ابوداود شریف، باب صلہ حجتہ النبی ا ت ص ۲۸۰ نمبر ۱۹۰۶) اس میں بھی ہے کہ درمیان میں نفل نہ پڑھے۔ ترجمه (۱۳۳۷) امام کے ساتھ نماز پڑھ چکے تو موقف کی طرف متوجہ ہو، اور وطن عرنہ کے علاوہ پورا عرفات ٹھہرنے کی جگہ ہے تشریح : پورا عرفات ٹھہرنے کی جگہ ہے اس سے حج ادا ہو جائے گا، البتہ جبل رحمت کے پاس ٹھہر نا بہتر ہے، حضور مجبل رحمت کے پاس ٹھہرے تھے ، اورپطن عرنہ میں نہ ٹھہرے اس میں اصحاب فیل کو عذاب ہوا تھا۔ ... وجه : (۱) عرفات میں جبل رحمت کے پاس ٹھہر نا بہتر ہے اس حدیث میں ہے۔ قال دخلنا على جابر بن عبد الله . ثم ركب رسول الله حتى اتى الموقف فجعل بطن ناقة القصواء الى الصخرات وجعل حبل المشاة بين يديه واسـتـقـبـل الـقبلة فلم يزل واقفا حتى غربت الشمس وذهبت الصفرة قليلا حتى غاب القرص . (مسلم شريف، باب حجتہ النبی ص ۵۱۵، نمبر ۲۹۵۰/۱۲۱۸ ابو داؤد شریف ، باب صفتہ حجتہ النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم ، ص ۲۷۸، نمبر ۱۹۰۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور ظہر وعصر کی نماز کے بعد وقوف کے لئے جبل رحمت کے پاس آئے اور وہاں وقوف کیا صحرات سے مراد جبل رحمت کا چٹان ہے۔ اس لئے یہاں وقوف کرنا بہتر ہے۔۔ آج کل بھیڑ بہت ہوتی ہے اس لئے یہاں جگہ ملنی مشکل ہوتی ہے، اس لئے جہاں آسانی سے جگہ مل جائے وہاں ٹھہر جائے، بس شرط یہ ہے کہ میدان عرفات کے اندر اندر ہو۔ (۲) عرفات کا پورا میدان ٹھہرنے کی جگہ ہے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے، عن جابر في حديثه ذالك أن رسول الله الله الله قال نحرت ههنا و منى كلها منحر فانحروا في رحالكم و وقفت ههنا و عرفة كلها موقف ووقفت ههنا و جمع كلها موقف ۔(مسلم شریف، باب ما جاء أن عرفہ کلھا موقف ،ص ۵۱۶، نمبر ۲۹۵۲/۱۲۱۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ پورا عرفہ ٹھہرنے کی جگہ ہے ۔ (۳) بطن عرنہ میں نہ ٹھہرے اس کی وجہ یہ حدیث ہے اخبرنـی مـحـمـد بـن منكدر ان النبي الله قال عرفة كلها موقف وارتفعوا عن بطن عرنة والمزدلفة كلها موقف وارتفعوا عن محســر للبيهقى تھی ، باب حيث ما وقف من عرفته اجزاه ص ۹۴۵۹،۱۸۶ رسنن ابن ماجہ شریف باب الموقف بعرفات ص۲۲۲) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ بطن عرنہ میں نہیں ٹھہر نا چاہئے ۔ ترجمه : (۱۳۳۸) اور زوال کے بعد وقوف عرفہ کے لئے غسل کرے۔
(1337) So when he prays with the Imam, he proceeds to the standing place, and all of Arafat is a standing place except Batn 'Arnah. (1338) And he performs ghusl after zawal in the afternoon with one adhan at Arafat, and does not glorify between them, and two iqamahs, and he prays Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah (Jam') with one adhan and two iqamahs, and does not glorify between them. (Abu Dawood...). In this also it is that do not pray nafl between them. Translation: (1337) After praying with the Imam, proceed to the standing place, and all of Arafat except Batn 'Arnah is a place of standing. Commentary: All of Arafat is a standing place; from this Hajj will be valid. However, it is better to stand near Jabal al-Rahmah; the Prophet stood near Jabal al-Rahmah. Do not stand in Batn 'Arnah, because the Companions of the Elephant were punished there. ... Proofs: (1) It is better to stand near Jabal al-Rahmah as per the hadith: 'We entered upon Jabir... then the Messenger of Allah rode until he came to the standing place, and he positioned the belly of his camel towards the rocks, and placed the rope of the walkers in front of him, and faced the qiblah, and remained standing until the sun set and the yellowing went away a little until the disk disappeared.' (Muslim, etc.). In this hadith, the Prophet came to Jabal al-Rahmah for wuquf after Zuhr and Asr prayers. So standing here is better. Nowadays there is a lot of crowd, so it is difficult to get a spot; therefore, wherever one can easily get a spot, he should stand, provided it is within the plain of Arafat. (2) The entire plain of Arafat is a standing place; the proof is this hadith: from Jabir that the Prophet said: 'I sacrificed here, and all of Mina is a place of sacrifice, so sacrifice in your tents; and I stood here, and all of Arafat is a standing place; and I stood here, and all of Muzdalifah is a standing place.' (Muslim). (3) Do not stand in Batn 'Arnah; the reason is this hadith: Muhammad ibn Munkadir informed me that the Prophet said: 'All of Arafat is a standing place, and stay away from Batn 'Arnah; and all of Muzdalifah is a standing place, and stay away from Muhassir.' (al-Bayhaqi, Ibn Majah). From this, it is understood that one should not stand in Batn 'Arnah. Translation: (1338) And perform ghusl after zawal for the standing at Arafat.
Source pages p. 368

Commentary
This passage combines two rulings from the matn: (1337) the ruling on the area of wuquf, and (1338) the recommendation of ghusl before wuquf. The commentary explains that all of Arafat is valid for standing, except the valley known as Batn 'Arnah. It is recommended (sunnah) to stand near Jabal al-Rahmah, following the example of the Prophet. However, due to overcrowding, one may stand anywhere within Arafat. The proofs include hadith from Jabir showing the Prophet's spot, and the explicit statement from the Prophet that all of Arafat is a standing place. The exclusion of Batn 'Arnah is based on a hadith instructing to stay away from it. The second ruling (1338) commands ghusl after zawal (afternoon) for the wuquf, which is a sunnah practice to be in a state of purity.

Key Terms
غسل (ghusl): Full body washing prescribed for purification, recommended before wuquf.
زوال (zawal): The time when the sun passes its zenith (noon).

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Wajib
B) Sunnah muakkadah
C) Fard
D) Mustahab

Key Takeaway
Ghusl before wuquf is sunnah muakkadah, not obligatory.

Condition of Imam for Combining Prayers at Arafat and Muzdalifah
Ruling condition and proof for combining prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition for combining prayers (jam') at Arafat and Muzdalifah and identify the ruling when the pilgrim does not pray with the Imam.

Core Idea
Combining prayers at Arafat and Muzdalifah requires praying behind the Imam; otherwise each prayer in its own time.

This lesson explains a unique Hanafi ruling: the permissibility of combining Zuhr and Asr at Arafat and Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah depends on the presence of the Hajj Imam. If a pilgrim cannot join the Imam, he must pray each prayer in its usual time. This ruling is based on the Hanafi principle that jam' (combining) is a concession specific to the Hajj caravan led by an Imam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is combining two prayers (jam') at Arafat (Zuhr/Asr) and Muzdalifah (Maghrib/Isha). The ruling is that it is permissible (sunnah) only when prayed behind the Imam of Hajj.
The Hanafi school does not allow jam' without a valid excuse, except for the Hajj context with an Imam.
2
Locate the condition
The condition is the presence of the 'great Imam' (imam a'zam) leading the combined prayer. The text states: 'If he does not catch the great Imam, he prays each prayer in its usual time.'
3
Apply the condition to a scenario
Suppose a pilgrim arrives at Arafat after the Imam has finished the combined Zuhr/Asr prayer. He cannot combine his own Zuhr and Asr; he must pray each separately in its time.

ثم ركب رسول الله حتى اتى الموقف فجعل بطن ناقته القصواء الى الصخرات وجعل حبل المشاة بين يديه واستقبل القبلة فلم يزل واقفا حتى غربت الشمس وذهبت الصفرة قليلا حتى غاب القرص . (مسلم شريف، باب حجتہ النبی ص ص ۵۱۵، نمبر ۲۹۵۰/۱۲۱۸ / ابوداؤد شریف ، باب صفتہ حجتہ النبی ، ص ۲۷۸، نمبر ۱۹۰۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور ظہر عصر کی نماز کے بعد وقوف کے لئے جبل رحمت کے پاس آئے اور وہاں وقوف کیا۔اس لئے یہاں وقوف کرنا بہتر ہے۔ ترجمه : (۱۳۴۰) کعبہ کی طرف منھ کرتے ہوئے ہتکبیر تہلیل، تلبیہ پڑھتے ہوئے ، کھانا مانگنے والے کی طرح ہاتھوں کو پھیلا کر دعا مانگتے ہوئے۔ اور اپنے لئے ، والدین کے لئے ، (مسلمان) بھائیوں کے لئے دعا میں خوب محنت کرے، اور کوشش ہو کہ دعا میں آنکھوں سے آنسو کے قطرات بہیں ، اس لئے کہ یہ قبولیت کی علامت ہے۔ اور دعا میں قبولیت کی امید کے ساتھ خوب الحاح و زاری کرے۔ اور اس دن میں غفلت نہ برتے چونکہ اس دن کا تدارک ممکن نہیں خصوصاً آفاقی کے لئے۔ تشریح : عرفات کا موقع پھر جلدی ہاتھ نہیں آئے گا اس لئے بہت آہ وزاری کے ساتھ دعا کرے۔ خاص طور پر آفاقی اس میں غفلت نہ برتے۔ وجه : (۱) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور نے قبلہ کی طرف رخ کر کے وقوف فرمایا اور دعا کی،حدیث یہ ہے۔ قال دخلنا على
Chapter: Structure of Hajj Actions (1336) And if he does not catch the great Imam, he prays each prayer in its usual time. (1337) When he prays with the Imam, he proceeds to the standing place, and all of Arafat is a standing place except Batn 'Arnah. (1338) He performs ghusl after zawal, and prays Asr at Arafat with one adhan and two iqamas without praying nafl between them, and prays Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah with one adhan and two iqamas without praying nafl between them. (Abu Dawud) (1336 translation) If he does not catch the Imam of Hajj, he prays each prayer in its prescribed time. Explanation: Since according to Imam Abu Hanifah, for combining prayers the presence of the Imam is a condition, so if he does not pray with the Imam of Hajj, he prays both prayers separately in their own times. (1337 translation) Once he has prayed with the Imam, he proceeds to the standing place, and all of Arafat except Batn 'Arnah is a place for standing. Explanation: All of Arafat is a place for standing; Hajj will be valid with that. However, standing near Jabal al-Rahmah is better; the Prophet stood there. And do not stand in Batn 'Arnah; the People of the Elephant were punished there... (1338 translation) And after zawal, he performs ghusl for standing at Arafat. (1339) And he stands near Jabal al-Rahmah. (1340) Facing the Qibla, saying Allahu Akbar, La ilaha illallah, Labbayk, supplicating, stretching his hands like a beggar, striving in supplication for himself, his parents, and his brothers, trying to let drops of tears fall from his eyes, for that is a sign of acceptance, persisting in supplication with hope of response, not being negligent on this day because it cannot be made up, especially for one from afar...
Source pages p. 368

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of Hajj actions. It begins by addressing the ruling for a pilgrim who does not perform the combined prayers with the Imam (the leader of the Hajj caravan). According to Imam Abu Hanifah, combining Zuhr and Asr at Arafat, and Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah, requires praying behind an Imam. If the pilgrim does not do so, he must pray each prayer in its own time. Next, the passage clarifies the location of standing (wuquf) at Arafat. All of the plain of Arafat is a valid place for wuquf, except the valley of Batn 'Arnah. This is proven by hadith: the Prophet said, 'I stood here, and all of Arafat is a standing place.' The commentary notes that standing near Jabal al-Rahmah is recommended (mustahabb) because the Prophet stood there, but due to crowding one may stand anywhere within Arafat. The third ruling concerns ghusl on the day of Arafah after zawal (noon). This is based on the practice of the Prophet and the statement of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i. Then the passage describes the desirable actions during wuquf: standing near Jabal al-Rahmah, facing the Qibla, reciting takbir, tahlil, and talbiyah, raising hands in supplication like a beggar, striving in dua for oneself and others, shedding tears as a sign of acceptance, and being persistent. The commentator emphasizes not to be negligent on this day as the opportunity cannot be recovered, especially for distant pilgrims.

Key Terms
جمع بين الصلاتين (jam' bayn al-salatayn): Combining two prayers (Zuhr and Asr, or Maghrib and Isha) at the time of the earlier one, allowed only for the Hajj pilgrim with the Imam.
امام الاعظم (imam al-a'zam): The great Imam, referring to the leader of the Hajj caravan who leads the combined prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when can a pilgrim combine Zuhr and Asr at Arafat?
A) Any time on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah
B) Only when praying behind the Hajj Imam
C) Only if he is traveling from outside Mecca
D) Only if he is sick or in difficulty

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits combining prayers at Arafat and Muzdalifah solely as a concession for the Hajj congregation led by the Imam; without the Imam, each prayer must be offered in its normal time.

Valid Standing Area at Arafat: All Except Batn 'Arnah
Ruling on the valid location for wuquf at Arafat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the valid area for wuquf at Arafat, state the exception of Batn 'Arnah, and explain the recommendation to stand near Jabal al-Rahmah.

Core Idea
All of Arafat is a standing place except the valley of Batn 'Arnah; standing near Jabal al-Rahmah is recommended.

This lesson delineates the precise boundaries for the essential Hajj rite of standing (wuquf) at Arafat. The Hanafi school, relying on explicit hadith, affirms that the entire plain of Arafat is a valid mawqif, with the sole exclusion of the valley of Batn 'Arnah. Moreover, standing near the mountain of mercy (Jabal al-Rahmah) is a cherished sunnah, following the Prophet's practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on the area of wuquf
The text states: 'All of Arafat is a standing place except Batn 'Arnah.' This means any spot in Arafat outside that valley fulfills the wajib of wuquf.
The exclusion is based on a hadith: 'Arafat is all a standing place, and avoid Batn 'Arnah.'
2
Understand the exception of Batn 'Arnah
Batn 'Arnah is a specific valley within the Arafat area where the Prophet prohibited standing. Historically, the army of Abraha (people of the elephant) was destroyed there. Standing there would invalidate the wuquf.
3
Recognize the recommendation to stand near Jabal al-Rahmah
The text mentions that standing near Jabal al-Rahmah is better (afdal). This is based on the Prophet's own action: he stood there with his camel facing the rocks.
If crowded, one may stand anywhere within Arafat, as long as it is not Batn 'Arnah.

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of Hajj actions. It begins by addressing the ruling for a pilgrim who does not perform the combined prayers with the Imam (the leader of the Hajj caravan). According to Imam Abu Hanifah, combining Zuhr and Asr at Arafat, and Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah, requires praying behind an Imam. If the pilgrim does not do so, he must pray each prayer in its own time. Next, the passage clarifies the location of standing (wuquf) at Arafat. All of the plain of Arafat is a valid place for wuquf, except the valley of Batn 'Arnah. This is proven by hadith: the Prophet said, 'I stood here, and all of Arafat is a standing place.' The commentary notes that standing near Jabal al-Rahmah is recommended (mustahabb) because the Prophet stood there, but due to crowding one may stand anywhere within Arafat. The third ruling concerns ghusl on the day of Arafah after zawal (noon). This is based on the practice of the Prophet and the statement of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i. Then the passage describes the desirable actions during wuquf: standing near Jabal al-Rahmah, facing the Qibla, reciting takbir, tahlil, and talbiyah, raising hands in supplication like a beggar, striving in dua for oneself and others, shedding tears as a sign of acceptance, and being persistent. The commentator emphasizes not to be negligent on this day as the opportunity cannot be recovered, especially for distant pilgrims.

Key Terms
موقف (mawqif): Place of standing during Hajj, specifically at Arafat on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah.
بطن عرنة (batn 'arnah): A valley within Arafat where standing is prohibited because it is not part of Arafat.
جبل الرحمة (jabal al-rahah): A hill in Arafat where the Prophet stood; recommended to stand near it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which area is NOT valid for wuquf at Arafat?
A) Near Jabal al-Rahmah
B) The Masjid al-Namirah
C) The valley of Batn 'Arnah
D) The entire plain of Arafat

Key Takeaway
For a valid wuquf at Arafat, the pilgrim must avoid the valley of Batn 'Arnah; standing near Jabal al-Rahmah is a highly recommended sunnah but not obligatory.

Recommended Acts at Arafat: Ghusl and Manner of Supplication
Rulings on recommended acts: ghusl and supplication

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the recommendation of ghusl on the day of Arafah after zawal and describe the recommended manner of supplication (dua) during wuquf.

Core Idea
Ghusl on the day of Arafah is mustahabb; supplication should be earnest, with raised hands, facing Qibla, and seeking tears as a sign of acceptance.

This lesson focuses on two key recommended acts (mustahabb) during the day at Arafat: performing ghusl (full ritual wash) after zawal (noon) and engaging in heartfelt supplication. The text provides evidence from the Prophet's practice and from the tabi'i Ibrahim al-Nakha'i. The manner of supplication is detailed: facing the Qibla, raising hands like a beggar, reciting takbir, tahlil, and talbiyah, striving to shed tears, and persisting with hope of acceptance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommendation and timing of ghusl
The text says: 'He performs ghusl after zawal.' This means on the day of Arafah (9th of Dhul Hijjah), after the sun passes its zenith, the pilgrim should wash his entire body in preparation for wuquf.
Ghusl is mustahabb, not wajib. If water is scarce, wudu suffices.
2
Understand the evidence for ghusl
The text cites two proofs: (1) The Prophet (s) used to perform ghusl on the day of Arafah (hadith from Ibn Majah). (2) The tabi'i Ibrahim al-Nakha'i instructed: 'Go to Arafat, and when the sun declines, perform ghusl if you find water; otherwise perform wudu.'
3
Outline the recommended manner of supplication
The text lists: face the Qibla, raise hands like a beggar, recite takbir (Allahu Akbar), tahlil (La ilaha illallah), talbiyah (Labbayk), and make dua for oneself, parents, and Muslim brothers. Strive to let tears flow as a sign of acceptance. Be persistent and do not be negligent, as this day cannot be made up.
The emphasis on tears and persistence is based on spiritual benefits, not a legal requirement.

Chapter: Structure of Hajj Actions (1336) And if he does not catch the great Imam, he prays each prayer in its usual time. (1337) When he prays with the Imam, he proceeds to the standing place, and all of Arafat is a standing place except Batn 'Arnah. (1338) He performs ghusl after zawal, and prays Asr at Arafat with one adhan and two iqamas without praying nafl between them, and prays Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah with one adhan and two iqamas without praying nafl between them. (Abu Dawud) (1336 translation) If he does not catch the Imam of Hajj, he prays each prayer in its prescribed time. Explanation: Since according to Imam Abu Hanifah, for combining prayers the presence of the Imam is a condition, so if he does not pray with the Imam of Hajj, he prays both prayers separately in their own times. (1337 translation) Once he has prayed with the Imam, he proceeds to the standing place, and all of Arafat except Batn 'Arnah is a place for standing. Explanation: All of Arafat is a place for standing; Hajj will be valid with that. However, standing near Jabal al-Rahmah is better; the Prophet stood there. And do not stand in Batn 'Arnah; the People of the Elephant were punished there... (1338 translation) And after zawal, he performs ghusl for standing at Arafat. (1339) And he stands near Jabal al-Rahmah. (1340) Facing the Qibla, saying Allahu Akbar, La ilaha illallah, Labbayk, supplicating, stretching his hands like a beggar, striving in supplication for himself, his parents, and his brothers, trying to let drops of tears fall from his eyes, for that is a sign of acceptance, persisting in supplication with hope of response, not being negligent on this day because it cannot be made up, especially for one from afar...
Source pages p. 368

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of Hajj actions. It begins by addressing the ruling for a pilgrim who does not perform the combined prayers with the Imam (the leader of the Hajj caravan). According to Imam Abu Hanifah, combining Zuhr and Asr at Arafat, and Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah, requires praying behind an Imam. If the pilgrim does not do so, he must pray each prayer in its own time. Next, the passage clarifies the location of standing (wuquf) at Arafat. All of the plain of Arafat is a valid place for wuquf, except the valley of Batn 'Arnah. This is proven by hadith: the Prophet said, 'I stood here, and all of Arafat is a standing place.' The commentary notes that standing near Jabal al-Rahmah is recommended (mustahabb) because the Prophet stood there, but due to crowding one may stand anywhere within Arafat. The third ruling concerns ghusl on the day of Arafah after zawal (noon). This is based on the practice of the Prophet and the statement of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i. Then the passage describes the desirable actions during wuquf: standing near Jabal al-Rahmah, facing the Qibla, reciting takbir, tahlil, and talbiyah, raising hands in supplication like a beggar, striving in dua for oneself and others, shedding tears as a sign of acceptance, and being persistent. The commentator emphasizes not to be negligent on this day as the opportunity cannot be recovered, especially for distant pilgrims.

Key Terms
غسل (ghusl): Full body washing; recommended ghusl on the day of Arafah after zawal for the pilgrim.
دعاء (du'a): Supplication; the recommended manner at Arafat includes facing Qibla, raising hands, reciting specific phrases, and striving to shed tears.
الحاح (ilhaah): Persistent supplication; the text advises persistence with hope of response.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT recommended during supplication at Arafat according to the text?
A) Facing the Qibla
B) Raising hands like a beggar
C) Reciting the Quran loudly
D) Persisting in dua with hope

Key Takeaway
Ghusl on the day of Arafah is a recommended sunnah, and the manner of supplication should be humble, focused, and persistent, with heartfelt tears as a desirable sign.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
beginner
6 min
Recommended Acts at Arafat During the Standing (Wuquf)
Lists sunan and mustahabbat of wuquf with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended acts (sunan) of wuquf at Arafat and identify the hadith proofs for each act.

Core Idea
The standing at Arafat is the pinnacle of Hajj; its recommended acts perfect the worship and follow the Prophet's model.

The standing at Arafat (wuquf) is the essential pillar of Hajj. While the minimal obligation is to be present in Arafat, the Prophet (peace be upon him) demonstrated additional acts that elevate the experience and bring immense reward. This lesson details those sunan and mustahabbat, along with their scriptural proofs, so that the pilgrim can worship with both knowledge and devotion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended acts
Read the list of acts: standing near Jabal al-Rahmah, facing Qibla, reciting takbir/tahlil/talbiyah, raising hands like a beggar, striving in dua with tears, etc. Recognize each as sunnah (recommended) not wajib.
The Hanafi ruling is that these acts are mustahabb/sunnah, not required for validity.
2
Locate the primary hadith proof
Find the hadith of Jabir that describes the Prophet's own standing: he faced the Qibla, stood near the rocks (Jabal al-Rahmah), and remained until sunset.
This hadith is from Muslim and Abu Dawud.
3
Trace the legal indication (wajh al-dalalah)
Understand how the Prophet's action (fi'il) indicates recommendation. Since he did it consistently, it is sunnah muakkadah. The hadith also specifies the place and posture.
The Hanafi principle: the Prophet's action implies permissibility unless there is evidence of obligation.
4
Apply to other recommended acts
The other proofs (e.g., hadith on raising hands, best dua, ghusl) similarly establish recommendation. Note the narration from Ibn Abbas listing seven places for raising hands including Arafat.
Each act has its own dalil; collective evidence strengthens the sunnah status.
