ترجمه : (۱۳۳۹) اور جبل رحمت کے قریب وقوف کرے۔
وجه (۱) عرفات میں جبل رحمت کے پاس ٹھہرنا بہتر ہے اس حدیث میں ہے۔ قال دخلنا على جابر بن عبد الله ... ثم ركب رسول الله حتى اتى الموقف فجعل بطن ناقته القصواء الى الصخرات وجعل حبل المشاة بين يديه واستقبل القبلة فلم يزل واقفا حتى غربت الشمس وذهبت الصفرة قليلا حتى غاب القرص . (مسلم شريف، باب حجتہ النبی ص ص ۵۱۵، نمبر ۲۹۵۰/۱۲۱۸ / ابوداؤد شریف ، باب صفتہ حجتہ النبی ، ص ۲۷۸، نمبر ۱۹۰۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور ظہر عصر کی نماز کے بعد وقوف کے لئے جبل رحمت کے پاس آئے اور وہاں وقوف کیا۔اس لئے يہاں وقوف کرنا بہتر ہے۔ ترجمه : (۱۳۴۰) کعبہ کی طرف منھ کرتے ہوئے تكبیر تہلیل، تلبیہ پڑھتے ہوئے ، کھانا مانگنے والے کی طرح ہاتھوں کو پھیلا کر دعا مانگتے ہوئے۔ اور اپنے لئے ، والدین کے لئے ، (مسلمان) بھائیوں کے لئے دعا میں خوب محنت کرے، اور کوشش ہو کہ دعا میں آنکھوں سے آنسو کے قطرات بہیں ، اس لئے کہ یہ قبولیت کی علامت ہے۔ اور دعا میں قبولیت کی امید کے ساتھ خوب الحاح و زاری کرے۔ اور اس دن میں غفلت نہ برتے چونکہ اس دن کا تدارک ممکن نہیں خصوصاً آفاقی کے لئے۔ تشریح : عرفات کا موقع پھر جلدی ہاتھ نہیں آئے گا اس لئے بہت آہ وزاری کے ساتھ دعا کرے۔ خاص طور پر آفاقی اس میں غفلت نہ برتے۔ وجه : (۱) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور نے قبلہ کی طرف رخ کر کے وقوف فرمایا اور دعا کی،حدیث یہ ہے۔ قال دخلنا على جابر بن عبد الله ... واستقبل القبلة فلم يزل واقفا حتى غربت الشمس وذهبت الصفرة قليلا حتى غاب القرص. (مسلم شریف، باب حجتہ النبی ص ص ۵۱۵، نمبر ۲۹۵۰/۱۲۱۸ ابوداؤد شریف، باب صفتہ حجتہ النبی ، ص ۲۷۸، نمبر ۱۹۰۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور نے قبلہ کی طرف استقبال کر کے دعا کی (۲). قال ابن عباس قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ان لكل شيء شر فا و ان أشرف المجالس ما استقبل به القبلة و انكم تجالسون بينكم بالامانة . (مستدرك للحاكم، باب کتاب الادب، ج رابع ، ص ۳۰۰ نمبر ۷۷۰۶) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ بہترین مجلس وہ ہے جو قبلہ کی جانب ہو کر بیٹھے، اور يہاں دعا کے لئے بیٹھنا ہے اس لئے قبلہ کی طرف ہی ہو کر بیٹھے۔ (۳) عرفات کی دعا اہم ہے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن عمر بن شعيب عن ابيه عن جده ان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال خير الدعاء يوم عرفة ( ترمذی شريف، باب فی دعاء يوم عرفة،ص ۸۲۷، نمبر ۳۵۸۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ عرفات کی دعا بہترین دعا ہے۔ (۴) جیسے مسکین کھانا مانگتا ہو اس طرح ہاتھ اٹھا کر اور پھیلا پھیلا کر دعا کرے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال رايت رسول الله يدعو بعرفة و يداه الى صدره كاستطعام المسكين ( سنن بیہقی ، باب افضل الدعاء يوم عرفة ، ج خامس ص ۱۹۰ نمبر ۹۴۷۴) (۵) عرفات میں ہاتھ اٹھا کر دعا کرے اس کے لئے یہ اثر بھی ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال : لا ترفع الأيدى الا في سبع مواطن : اذا قام الى الصلوة [٢] و اذا رأى البيت [۳] و على الصفا [۴] و المروة [۵] و في عرفات [۶] و في جمع [۷] و عند الجمار ۔ (مصنف ابن ابی شيبة ، من کان یرفع ید یہ فی اول تكبيرة ثم لا يعود ، ج اول ، ص۲۱۴، نمبر ۰ ۲۴۵ رسن بیھقی ، باب رفع الیدین اذا رأی البیت ، ج خامس ص ۱۱۷ نمبر ۹۲۱۰) اس اثر میں ہے کہ عرفات میں ہاتھ اٹھا کر دعا کرے۔ (۱) حضرت علی سے ایک دعا یہ بھی منقول ہے۔عن علی بن طالب قال قال رسول الله صلے الله عليه وسلم أكثر دعائى و دعاء الانبياء قبلي بعرفة لا اله الا الله وحده لا شريك له له الملك و له الحمد و هو على كل شيء قدير ، اللهم اجعل في قلبي نورا و في سمعی نورا و في بصری نورا ، اللهم اشرح صدري و يسر لي أمري و أعوذ بک من وسواس الصدر و شتات الامر و فتنة القبر اللهم اني أعوذ بك من شر ما يلج في الليل و شر ما يلج في النهار و شر ما تهب به الرياح و من شر بوائق الدهر - ( سنن بیہقی ، باب افضل الدعاء دعاء يوم عرفة ، ج خامس ،ص۱۹۰، نمبر ۹۴۷۵ و مصنف ابن ابي شيبة ، باب ما يقال عشية عرفة و ما يستحب من الدعاء ، ج ثالث ص ۱۳۶۳، نمبر ۱۵۱۳۰) اس حدیث میں عرفہ کی دعاء موجود ہے۔ لغت : ماداند سے مشتق ہے، پھیلانا مستطعم : طعام سے مشتق ہے، کھانا مانگنے والا ۔ الدمع : آنسو۔ یلج : باب افعال میں الحاح سے دعا میں کوشش کرنا ۔ رجاء : امید اجابت : قبول ہونا ۔ رجاء الاجابة : قبول ہونے کی امید رکھنا۔ یقصر : قصر سے مشتق ہے ، کوتاہی کرنا ۔ سیما: خاص طور پر ۔ آفاق : جولوگ مکہ مکرمہ سے باہر کے ہوں۔
Section on the composition of the acts of Hajj. Arafat for standing (1339) 133 and he stands near the Mountain of Mercy (1340) facing the Qibla, saying takbir, tahlil, talbiyah, supplicating, extending his hands like a beggar, and he strives in supplication for himself, his parents, and his brothers, and he strives that drops of tears come out of his eyes, for that is a sign of acceptance, and he persists in supplication with strong hope of response, and he does not be negligent on this day because it cannot be made up, especially if he is from outside Mecca. Proof: (a) From his grandfather al-Fakih ibn Sa'd, who was a companion, that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) used to bathe on the day of Fitr, the day of Nahr, and the day of Arafah, and al-Fakih used to command his family to bathe on these days. (Ibn Majah, chapter on what is mentioned about bathing on the two Eids, p. 186, no. 1316). (2) And he should bathe after noon; for this there is this narration: From Ibrahim, he said: 'Proceed to Arafat, and when it is after noon, bathe if you find water, otherwise perform wudu.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, chapter on what is mentioned about bathing on the day of Arafah during Hajj, vol. 3, p. 404, no. 15558). In this saying of a Tabi'i, bathing after noon on the day of Arafah is mustahab. Translation: (1339) And he stands near the Mountain of Mercy. Proof (1) Standing near Jabal al-Rahmah in Arafat is better; there is this hadith: He said: We entered upon Jabir ibn Abdillah... Then the Messenger of Allah rode until he came to the standing place, and he turned the belly of his she-camel Qaswa towards the rocks, and he placed the rope of the walkers in front of him, and he faced the Qibla, and he continued standing until the sun set and the yellow color disappeared a little until the disk disappeared. (Muslim, chapter on the Prophet's Hajj, p. 515, no. 2950/1218; Abu Dawud, chapter on the description of the Prophet's Hajj, p. 278, no. 1905). In this hadith, after praying Zuhr and Asr, the Prophet came to the place near Jabal al-Rahmah for standing and stood there. Therefore, standing there is better. Translation: (1340) Facing the Ka'bah, saying takbir, tahlil, talbiyah, extending his hands like a beggar while supplicating. And he should strive hard in supplication for himself, his parents, and his (Muslim) brothers, and he should try that drops of tears flow from his eyes in supplication, because that is a sign of acceptance. And he should supplicate with insistence and pleading with hope of acceptance. And he should not be negligent on this day because it cannot be made up, especially for one from outside Mecca. Explanation: The opportunity of Arafat will not come again quickly, so he should supplicate with much weeping and wailing. Particularly the Afaqi should not be negligent in this. Proof: (1) In this hadith, the Prophet faced the Qibla and stood and supplicated. The hadith is: He said: We entered upon Jabir... and he faced the Qibla and continued standing until the sun set... (Muslim, etc.). In this hadith, the Prophet faced the Qibla and supplicated. (2) Ibn Abbas said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Everything has a best part, and the best of gatherings is that in which one faces the Qibla, and you sit with one another in trust.' (Mustadrak al-Hakim, chapter on good manners, vol. 4, p. 300, no. 7706). In this hadith, the best gathering is that in which one sits facing the Qibla, and here one is sitting for supplication, so one should sit facing the Qibla. (3) The supplication of Arafat is important; for this there is this hadith: From Amr ibn Shu'ayb from his father from his grandfather that the Prophet said: 'The best supplication is the supplication on the day of Arafah.' (Tirmidhi, chapter on supplication on the day of Arafah, p. 827, no. 3585). In this hadith, the supplication of Arafat is the best. (4) He should raise and spread his hands like a beggar asking for food; for this there is this hadith: From Ibn Abbas: 'I saw the Messenger of Allah supplicating at Arafat with his hands to his chest like a beggar asking for food.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on the best supplication on the day of Arafah, vol. 5, p. 190, no. 9474). (5) He should raise his hands in supplication at Arafat; for this there is also this narration: From Ibn Abbas: 'Hands are not raised except in seven places: when standing for prayer, when seeing the House (Ka'bah), on Safa, on Marwah, at Arafat, at Muzdalifah, and at the Jamarat.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, chapter on those who raise their hands at the first takbir and then do not return, vol. 1, p. 214, no. 245; Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on raising hands when seeing the House, vol. 5, p. 117, no. 9210). In this narration, one should raise hands in supplication at Arafat. (1) A supplication from Ali is also transmitted: From Ali ibn Talib, he said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'The most frequent of my supplication and the supplication of the prophets before me at Arafat is: La ilaha illallah wahdahu la sharika lah, lahul mulku wa lahul hamdu wa huwa 'ala kulli shay'in qadir. Allahumma aj'al fi qalbi nuran wa fi sam'i nuran wa fi basari nuran, Allahumma ishrah sadri wa yassir li amri wa a'udhu bika min waswasis sadri wa shatati al-amri wa fitnati al-qabr. Allahumma inni a'udhu bika min sharri ma yaliju fi al-layli wa sharri ma yaliju fi al-nahari wa sharri ma tahhabu bihi al-riyahu wa min sharri buwa'iqi al-dahr.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on the best supplication is the supplication of the day of Arafah, vol. 5, p. 190, no. 9475; Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, chapter on what is said on the evening of Arafah and what is recommended of supplication, vol. 3, p. 1363, no. 15130). In this hadith, the supplication of Arafah is present. Lexicon: Madan: derived from 'madd' (extend). Mustat'im: derived from 'ta'am' (food), one who asks for food. Ad-dam': tears. Yalij: from al-ilhah (persistence), to strive in supplication. Raja': hope. Ijabah: acceptance. Raja' al-ijabah: hoping for acceptance. Yuqassir: from qasr, to be negligent. Siyyama: especially. Afaq: those who are from outside Mecca.
Source pages p. 369

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof detailing the recommended acts (mustahabbat/sunan) during the standing (wuquf) at Arafat on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah. The author begins by listing the key practices: standing near Jabal al-Rahmah, facing the Qibla, reciting takbir, tahlil, and talbiyah, and supplicating with hands extended like a beggar. The emphasis is on sincere, earnest dua for oneself, parents, and fellow Muslims, with tears as a sign of acceptance. The author warns against negligence, especially for those coming from outside Mecca (Afaqi), as the opportunity of Arafat cannot be retrieved. Several proofs from hadith are then provided: (1) The Prophet (saw) used to bathe on the day of Arafah, indicating the recommendation of ghusl before standing. (2) A narration from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i recommends bathing after noon, or wudu if water is scarce. (3) The Prophet's own practice of standing near Jabal al-Rahmah, as narrated by Jabir, establishes the virtue of that location. (4) Multiple hadith emphasize facing the Qibla during supplication, including a hadith that the best gatherings are those facing the Qibla. (5) The Prophet declared that the best supplication is on the day of Arafah. (6) He demonstrated raising hands like a beggar seeking food. (7) A narration from Ibn Abbas lists seven places where hands are raised, including Arafat. Finally, a specific supplication of the Prophet transmitted through Ali is cited, containing the declaration of tawhid and a comprehensive plea for light in the heart, ears, and eyes, ease in affairs, and protection from evil. The passage concludes with a glossary of terms. The overall message is that the standing at Arafat is the pinnacle of Hajj, and the pilgrim should devote themselves entirely to worship, supplication, and seeking forgiveness, following the Prophetic model.

Key Terms
وقف (wuquf): The ritual standing at Arafat on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah; the essential pillar of Hajj.
جبل الرحمة (Jabal al-Rahmah): The Mountain of Mercy at Arafat, near which the Prophet stood and where standing is recommended.
آفاقي (Afaqi): A pilgrim coming from outside the Miqat boundaries of Mecca, as opposed to a resident of Mecca.
غسل (ghusl): Ritual bath, recommended before the standing at Arafat.
تلبیة (talbiyah): The chant 'Labbayk Allahumma Labbayk...' recited during Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited in the passage, which supplication is considered the best?
A) Supplication on the night of Arafah
B) Supplication on the day of Arafah
C) Supplication at the Black Stone
D) Supplication after the five prayers

Key Takeaway
The recommended acts at Arafat are sunnah based on Prophetic practice; observing them brings great reward but omitting them does not invalidate the Hajj.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
beginner
6 min
Etiquettes of Supplication at Arafat
Hadith-based recommendations for du'a at Arafat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the sunnah actions for du'a at Arafat and cite the supporting hadith evidence from the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
Facing Qibla and raising hands at Arafat are sunnah; the best supplication is on the Day of Arafah.

In this passage, the author compiles several authentic hadith and athar that guide the pilgrim on the etiquettes of supplication at Arafat. These include facing the Qibla, raising hands in a pleading manner, and reciting a specific du'a. Understanding these recommendations helps the pilgrim follow the Prophet's example and maximise the blessings of this sacred day.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended actions
List the three main actions prescribed in the passage: facing the Qibla, raising hands like a beggar, and reciting the prophetic du'a.
Each action is supported by its own hadith or athar.
2
Locate the dalil for each action
For each action, find the corresponding hadith cited: facing Qibla from Jabir's hadith; raising hands from Ibn Abbas's athar; du'a from Ali's hadith.
3
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah
Determine how each hadith indicates recommendation (sunnah) rather than obligation. For example, the phrase 'khayr al-du'a' (best supplication) shows preference, not compulsion.
The Hanafi principle: a prophetic action without explicit command remains sunnah.
4
Determine the hukm level
Classify each action as sunnah muakkadah (confirmed sunnah). None are fard or wajib; their omission does not invalidate Hajj but loses virtue.
Check the hanafi_position_box for more details.
5
Apply the ruling to practice
In a real Hajj scenario, advise the pilgrim to perform these sunnan, and respond if someone asks about their necessity.
The al-mukhtalaf fih (if needed) discusses minor cross-madhhab differences in the number of places to raise hands.

فصل تركيب افعال الحج
جابر بن عبد الله ... واستقبل القبلة فلم يزل واقفا حتى غربت الشمس وذهبت الصفرة قليلا حتى غاب القرص. (مسلم شریف، باب حجتہ النبی ص ص ۵۱۵، نمبر ۲۹۵۰/۱۲۱۸ ابوداؤد شریف، باب صفتہ حجتہ النبی ، ص ۲۷۸، نمبر ۱۹۰۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور نے قبلہ کی طرف استقبال کر کے دعا کی (۲). قال ابن عباس قال رسول الله الله ان لكل شيء شر فا و ان أشرف المجالس ما استقبل به القبلة و انكم تجالسون بينكم بالامانة . (متدرك للحاكم، باب کتاب الادب، ج رابع ، ص ۳۰۰ نمبر ۷۷۰۶) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ بہترین مجلس وہ ہے جو قبلہ کی جانب ہو کر بیٹھے، اور یہاں دعا کے لئے بیٹھنا ہے اس لئے قبلہ کی طرف ہی ہو کر بیٹھے۔ (۳) عرفات کی دعا اہم ہے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن عمر بن صلى الله عليه وسلم قال خير الدعاء يوم عرفة ( ترندى شريف، باب فی دعاء يوم عرفته ،ص ۸۲۷، نمبر ۳۵۸۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ عرفات کی دعا بہترین دعا ہے۔ (۴) جیسے مسکین کھانا مانگتا ہو اس طرح ہاتھ اٹھا کر اور پھیلا پھیلا کر دعا کرے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال رايت رسول الله يدعو بعرفة و يداه الى صدره كاستطعام المسكين ( سنن سبیھقی ، باب افضل الدعاء يوم عرفته ، ج خامس ص ۱۹۰ نمبر ۹۴۷۴) (۵) عرفات میں ہاتھ اٹھا کر ، ۱۹۰، دعا کرے اس کے لئے یہ اثر بھی ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال : لا ترفع الأيدى الا في سبع مواطن : اذا قام الى الصلوة [٢] و اذا رأى البيت [۳] و على الصفا [۴] و المروة [۵] و في عرفات [۶] و في جمع [۷] و عند الجمار ۔ (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ، من کان یرفع ید یہ فی اول تكبيرة ثم لا يعود ، ج اول ، ص۲۱۴، نمبر ۰ ۲۴۵ رسن بیھقی ، باب رفع الیدین اذا رأی البیت ، ج خامس ص ۱۱۷ نمبر ۹۲۱۰) اس اثر میں ہے کہ عرفات میں ہاتھ اٹھا کر دعا کرے۔ (۱) حضرت علی سے ایک دعا یہ بھی منقول ہے۔عن علی بن طالب قال قال رسول الله الا الله أكثر دعائى و دعاء الانبياء قبلي بعرفة لا اله الا الله وحده لا شريك له له الملك و له الحمد و هو على كل شيء قدير ، اللهم اجعل في قلبي نورا و في سمعی نورا و في بصری نورا ، اللهم اشرح صدري و يسر لي أمري و أعوذ بک من وسواس الصدر و شتات الامر و فتنة القبر اللهم اني أعوذ بك من شر ما يلج في الليل و شر ما يلج في النهار و شر ما تهب به الرياح و من شر بوائق الدهر - ( سنن بیہقی ، باب افضل الدعاء دعاء يوم عرفة ، ج خامس ،ص۱۹۰، نمبر ۹۴۷۵ رمصنف ابن ابی شبيبة ، باب ما يقال عشية عرفتة و ما يستحب من الدعاء ، ج ثالث ص ۱۳۶۳، نمبر ۱۵۱۳۰) اس حدیث میں عرفہ کی دعاء موجود ہے۔ لغت : ماداند سے مشتق ہے، پھیلانا منتطم : طعام سے مشتق ہے، كھانا مانگنے والا ۔ الدمع : آنسو۔ بیلج : باب افعال میں الح سے دعا میں کوشش کرنا ۔ رجاء : امید اجابت : قبول ہونا ۔ رجاء الاجابة : قبول ہونے کی امید رکھنا۔ یقصر : قصر سے مشتق ہے ، کوتاہی کرنا ۔ سیما: خاص طور پر ۔ آفاق : جولوگ مکہ مکرمہ سے باہر کے ہوں۔
Chapter on the composition of Hajj actions. Jabir ibn Abdullah... and he faced the Qibla and did not cease standing until the sun set and the yellowness diminished a little until the disk disappeared. (Muslim, Bab Hajjat al-Nabi, p. 515, no. 2950/1218; Abu Dawud, Bab Sifat Hajjat al-Nabi, p. 278, no. 1905) In this hadith it is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) made supplication facing the Qibla. (2) Ibn Abbas said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Indeed everything has a noble part, and indeed the noblest of gatherings are those in which the Qibla is faced, and you sit amongst each other with trustworthiness.' (Mustadrak al-Hakim, Bab Kitab al-Adab, vol. 4, p. 300, no. 7706) In this hadith it is that the best gathering is that which is seated facing the Qibla, and here it is for supplication, so one should sit facing the Qibla. (3) The supplication at Arafat is important; for this there is this hadith: From Amr ibn Shu'ayb from his father from his grandfather that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The best supplication is on the Day of Arafah.' (Tirmidhi, Bab fi Du'a Yawm 'Arafah, p. 827, no. 3585) In this hadith it is that the supplication at Arafat is the best. (4) He should raise and spread his hands like a beggar asking for food; for this there is this hadith: From Ibn Abbas: I saw the Messenger of Allah supplicating at Arafat with his hands near his chest, like a beggar asking for food. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab Afdal al-Du'a Yawm 'Arafah, vol. 5, p. 190, no. 9474) (5) Raising hands at Arafat in supplication; for this there is also this athar: From Ibn Abbas: 'Do not raise hands except in seven places: when standing for prayer, when seeing the House, on Safa, on Marwah, at Arafat, at Muzdalifah, and at the Jamarat.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, no. 245; Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab Raf' al-Yadayn, vol. 5, p. 117, no. 9210) In this athar it is that hands should be raised at Arafat. (1) Also a supplication is transmitted from Ali: From Ali ibn Abi Talib said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'The most abundant of my supplication and the supplication of the prophets before me at Arafat is: There is no god but Allah alone, no partner with Him, to Him belongs the dominion, to Him belongs all praise, and He is over all things potent. O Allah, place in my heart light, in my hearing light, in my sight light. O Allah, expand my chest and ease my affair and I seek refuge in You from the whisperings of the chest, the scattering of the affair, and the trial of the grave. O Allah, I seek refuge in You from the evil that enters in the night, the evil that enters in the day, the evil brought by the winds, and from the calamities of time.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab Afdal al-Du'a Yawm 'Arafah, vol. 5, p. 190, no. 9475; Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, Bab ma Yuqal 'Ashiyat 'Arafah, vol. 3, p. 1363, no. 15130) In this hadith is the supplication of Arafat. Vocabulary: maddand: derived from 'mad', spreading; muta'attim: derived from 'ta'am', one who asks for food; al-dam': tears; yalij: from bab if'al, means to strive in supplication; raja': hope; ijabah: acceptance; raja' al-ijabah: hoping for acceptance; yaqsir: from qasr, to shorten; sima: specifically; afaq: those outside Makkah.
Source pages p. 370

Commentary
This passage is a collection of hadith proofs for the recommended actions and etiquettes of supplication (du'a) at Arafat during Hajj. The author begins by citing that the Prophet himself faced the Qibla while standing at Arafat until sunset (hadith of Jabir). This establishes facing Qibla as a Sunnah. Next, a hadith from Ibn Abbas declares that the best gatherings are those facing the Qibla, reinforcing the recommendation. The third hadith from Tirmidhi states that the best supplication is on the Day of Arafah, highlighting the virtue of this time. Then, the manner of raising hands is detailed: the Prophet raised his hands like a beggar asking for food, meaning palms facing up and spread. An athar from Ibn Abbas specifies seven places where hands are raised in worship, including at Arafat. Finally, a long supplication attributed to Ali ibn Abi Talib (and via him to the Prophet) is provided as a recommended du'a to recite at Arafat. The author then gives a glossary of key Arabic terms. Overall, these texts establish the recommended practices—facing Qibla, choosing Arafat for supplication, raising hands in a pleading manner, and reciting a specific du'a—as Sunnah (mustahabb). No disagreement is noted; these are agreed-upon etiquettes within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
عرفات (Arafat): The plain near Makkah where pilgrims stand on the 9th of Dhul-Hijjah; the most essential part of Hajj.
دعاء (du'a): Supplication; in this context, the specific act of raising hands and praying to Allah at Arafat.
القبلة (al-Qiblah): The direction of the Ka'bah in Mecca; facing it during du'a is recommended.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited in this lesson, which day has the best supplication?
A) Day of Arafah
B) Day of Nahr
C) Friday
D) Laylat al-Qadr

Key Takeaway
Facing Qibla and raising hands at Arafat are sunnah; the best du'a is on the Day of Arafah.

The Recommended Manner of Wuquf at Arafat
States preference hierarchy for wuquf at Arafat with hadith proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the preferred manner of standing at Arafat and identify the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Standing on a mount at Arafat is recommended, not obligatory, based on the Prophet's practice.

This lesson examines a key ruling in Hajj: the manner of the standing (wuquf) at Arafat. While wuquf itself is a pillar, its performance has recommended characteristics. The Hanafi school, following the Prophet's example, gives preference to standing on a mount, then standing on foot, and lastly sitting. We will explore the textual evidence and the hierarchy of actions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the wuquf (standing) at Arafat. The ruling is that standing on a mount is afdal (superior).
This is a recommended action (mustahabb/sunnah), not obligatory.
2
Understand the hierarchy
The text states: mount > standing on ground > sitting. This is the order of preference.
The hierarchy is derived from the Prophet's practice and his explicit action.
3
Locate the dalil
The hadith of Umm al-Fadl shows the Prophet standing on his camel while drinking milk. This establishes the practice.
The dalil is a hadith ahad (single transmission) but considered sufficient for recommendation.
4
Determine the hukm level
It is mustahabb (recommended), not wajib, because the Prophet's action is a fi'l (practice) that indicates preference, not obligation.
Omitting this sunnah does not invalidate the Hajj, but leaving it without excuse is a loss of reward.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل تركيب افعال الحج
(۱۳۴۱) والوقوف على الراحلة افضل والقائم على الارض افضل من القاعد (۱۳۴۲) فاذا غربت الشمس افاض الامام والناس معه على هينتهم .
ترجمه : (۱۳۴۱) اور وقوف سواری پر افضل ہے، اور زمین پر کھڑا ہونے والا بیٹھنے والے سے افضل ہے۔ تشریح : حضور نے عرفات میں قصواء اونٹنی پر سوار ہو کر وقوف عرفہ کیا تھا ۔ اس لئے مستحب یہ ہے کہ امام اپنی سواری پر وقوف کرے۔ وہ نہ ہو تو کھڑا ہو کر وقوف کرے، یا کم از کچھ دیر کے لئے ہی کھڑا ہو، اور وہ بھی نہ ہو سکے تو زمین پر بیٹھے۔
صلى الله
وجه : (۱) عن ام الفضل بنت الحارث ان اناسا اختلفوا عندها يوم عرفة في صوم النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال بعضهم هو صائم وقال بعضهم ليس بصائم فارسلت اليه بقدح لبن وهو واقف على بعيره فشر به ۔ ( بخاری شریف، باب الوقوف على الدالبتہ بعرفہ ص ۱۲۵ نمبر (۱۶۶) اوپر کی حدیث مسلم شریف نمبر ۲۹۵۰ سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ آپ قصواء اوٹنی پر سوار تھے۔
Section: The framework of Hajj actions. (1341) Standing on a mount is superior, and the one standing on the ground is superior to the one sitting. Translation: (1341) And standing on a mount is superior, and the one standing on the ground is superior to the one sitting. Explanation: The Prophet (peace be upon him) performed the standing at Arafat riding on his she-camel Qaswa. Therefore it is recommended that the Imam stand on his mount. If not possible, then stand, even if for a short while, and if unable, then sit on the ground. May Allah bless him. Evidence: (1) From Umm al-Fadl bint al-Harith that people differed before her on the day of Arafat concerning the fasting of the Prophet (peace be upon him); some said he was fasting, others said not. So she sent him a cup of milk while he was standing on his camel, and he drank it. (Bukhari, chapter on standing on the mount at Arafat, p. 125, no. 166; the earlier hadith from Muslim no. 2950 also indicates that he was riding his she-camel Qaswa.)
Source pages p. 371

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the preferred manner of standing at Arafat. The text states that standing on a mount (such as a camel) is superior to standing on the ground, and standing on the ground is superior to sitting. The Hanafi position, as derived from the Prophet's practice, is that it is recommended (mustahabb) for the Imam to stand on a mount during the waquf at Arafat. If that is not possible, then standing on foot is recommended, even for a short duration; if even that is not possible, then sitting on the ground is allowed. The proof is the hadith of Umm al-Fadl where the Prophet was standing on his camel, and also the widely reported hadith that he rode Qaswa at Arafat. This ruling falls under the category of recommended actions (sunan) within the Hajj.

Key Terms
الوقوف (al-wuquf): The standing (pause) at Arafat during Hajj, which is a pillar (rukn) of Hajj.
الراحلة (al-rahilah): A riding animal, typically a camel, used for travel.
مستحب (mustahabb): Recommended, but not obligatory; omitting it is not sinful but leaves reward.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the best way to perform the standing at Arafat?
A) Standing on the ground
B) Standing on a mount
C) Sitting on the ground
D) Sitting on a mount

Key Takeaway
The preferred manner of wuquf at Arafat is standing on a mount; if not possible, standing on foot; sitting is allowed but less preferred.

Departure from Arafat After Sunset
Rules on when and how to depart from Arafat after sunset

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the timing and manner of departure from Arafat, identify the three proofs (hadith of Jabir, hadith of Usama, Quran 2:198), and explain why calmness is required.

Core Idea
Depart from Arafat after sunset, calmly — the Prophet's practice is our guide.

The departure from Arafat (ifada) is a key moment of Hajj. The Hanafi school emphasizes two aspects: the timing (after sunset) and the manner (with dignity). This lesson examines the proofs from the Quran and Sunnah that establish this ruling, helping you understand not just what to do, but why it is done that way.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is ifada (departure from Arafat). According to the Hanafi school, it is sunnah (recommended) to perform ifada after sunset, with calmness. Departing before sunset is not allowed (makruh tahrimi).
The ruling is derived from the Prophet's practice and explicit command.
2
Locate the primary proof
The primary proof is the detailed hadith of Jabir ibn Abdullah (Muslim, no. 2950). It describes the Prophet remaining in Arafat until sunset, then departing calmly, saying 'al-sakinah, al-sakinah'.
This hadith is the most comprehensive evidence.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's action (remaining until sunset) indicates the timing; his command 'sakinah' indicates the required manner. The word 'sakinah' is an imperative implying recommendation.
Hanafi usul: al-amr li al-nadb (command for recommendation) unless evidence for obligation.
4
Note the supplementary proofs
The hadith of Usama (Abu Dawud, no. 1925) confirms the timing: 'When the sun set, the Prophet departed.' The Quranic verse (2:198) uses the word 'ifada' implying departure from Arafat, understood as after sunset due to the Sunnah.
These support the primary proof.
5
Consider the ikhtilaf
Some scholars allow departure before sunset. The Hanafi school insists on after sunset because the explicit hadith shows the Prophet waited. The practical consequence: Hanafis wait until full sunset, while others may leave earlier.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf in the furu'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۳۴۲) فاذا غربت الشمس افاض الامام والناس معه على هينتهم .
ترجمه : (۱۳۴۲) پھر جب سورج غروب ہو جائے تو لوگ اطمینان سے امام کے ساتھ کوچ کریں۔ تشریح میدان عرفات میں شام تک رہے اور غروب آفتاب کے بعد وہاں سے چلے۔ پہلے امام چلے پھر عوام ان کے ساتھ چلے اور دوڑے نہیں ۔ بلکہ اپنی ہیئت پر اطمینان سے چلے۔
وجه (۱) اس حدیث میں ہے ۔ قال دخلنا على جابر بن عبد الله ... فلم يزل واقفا حتى غربت الشمس وذهبت الصفرة قليلا حتى غاب القرص واردف اسامة خلفه ودفع رسول الله الله وقد شنق للقصواء الزمام حتى ان رأسها ليصيب مورک رحله ويقول بيده اليمنى ايها الناس السكينة السكينة كلما اتي حبلا من الحبال ارخـى لهـا قليلا حتى تصعد حتى اتى المزدلفة . (مسلم شریف ، باب حجتہ النبی ص ص ۱۵۱۵، نمبر ۲۹۵۰/۱۲۱۸ ابوداؤد شریف، باب صفته حجت النبی ، ص ۲۷۸، نمبر ۱۹۰۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مغرب کے بعد عرفہ سے چلے اور یہ بھی معلوم ہوا کہ اطمینان سے چلے تیزی نہ کرے۔ (۲) مغرب کے بعد چلے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث بھی ہے . عن أسامة قال كنت ردف النبي الله فلما وقعت الشمس دفع رسول الله الله (ابوداود شریف الدفعة من عرفته ، ص۲۸۲، نمبر ۱۹۲۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ سورج غروب ہونے کے بعد چلے۔ (۳) اس آیت میں بھی اس کا اشارہ ہے۔ فاذا افضتم من عرفات فاذكروا الله عند المشعر الحرام (آیت ۱۹۸ سورة البقرة ٢) افتم کا ترجمہ ہے چلے، یعنی عرفات سے چلے۔
(1342) Then when the sun sets, the Imam and the people with him depart with calmness. Translation: (1342) Then when the sun sets, the people should depart with the Imam calmly. Explanation: Stay in the field of Arafat until evening, and after sunset leave from there. The Imam leaves first, then the people with him, and they do not run but walk calmly in their usual manner. Evidence (1): In this hadith: He said, 'We entered upon Jabir ibn Abdullah...' and he continued standing until the sun set and the yellowness faded a little until the disk disappeared, and he seated Usama behind him, and the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) moved, and he had tightened the bridle of Qaswa so much that its head touched the saddle, and he said with his right hand, 'O people, calmness, calmness.' Whenever he came to a hill, he would loosen it a little so that it could ascend until he came to Muzdalifah. (Muslim, Bab Hajjat an-Nabi, p. 1515, no. 2950/1218; Abu Dawud, Bab Sifat Hajjat an-Nabi, p. 278, no. 1905) From this hadith it is known that he departed from Arafat after Maghrib, and also that he moved calmly and did not rush. (2) Another hadith for departing after Maghrib: From Usama, he said, 'I was riding behind the Prophet (peace be upon him); when the sun set, the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) departed.' (Abu Dawud, Bab ad-Daf'ah min Arafat, p. 282, no. 1925) This hadith states that he departed after sunset. (3) There is also an indication in this verse: 'Then when you depart from Arafat, remember Allah at the Sacred Monument' (2:198). The word 'afadtum' means you departed, i.e., from Arafat.
Source pages p. 371

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling that the departure from Arafat (ifada) should occur after sunset, and that it should be done calmly, without haste. The Hanafi position is that the Imam leads the people, and all should proceed with dignity (sakinah). The proofs are multiple: (1) the detailed hadith of Jabir describing the Prophet's calm departure after sunset, (2) the hadith of Usama confirming the timing, and (3) the Quranic verse implying departure from Arafat towards Muzdalifah. The commotion and rushing done by some ignorant people is avoided.

Key Terms
الإفاضة (al-ifadah): The departure from Arafat to Muzdalifah after sunset.
السكينة (as-sakinah): Calmness, dignity, tranquility in movement; opposite of haste.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does the departure from Arafat (ifada) begin according to the Hanafi school?
A) Before sunset
B) At sunset
C) After sunset
D) At any time after noon

Key Takeaway
The departure from Arafat should be after sunset, with calmness and dignity, following the Prophet's example as established by authentic hadith and the Quran.

Hastening to Muzdalifah: Permissible Speed and Prohibited Harm
Guidelines on when to hasten and what to avoid during the journey

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hastening during the journey from Arafat to Muzdalifah, identify the conditions under which it is permissible, and explain why causing harm is haram.

Core Idea
Hasten only when space is clear; harming others is always haram.

During the Hajj journey from Arafat to Muzdalifah, pilgrims often wonder about the proper pace. The Hanafi school provides a balanced ruling: slight acceleration is allowed when there is an opening in the crowd, but reckless speeding, crowding, and causing harm are strictly forbidden. This lesson unpacks the evidence from the Prophet's practice and the underlying principle of avoiding harm.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the passage covers two scenarios: hastening when there is a clear path, and the actions of ignorant people (speeding, crowding, harming). The ruling for the former is permissible (mubah) with conditions; the latter is explicitly haram.
The act of hastening is not inherently prohibited; it becomes haram only when it leads to harm.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites two hadiths: one from Jabir showing the Prophet would accelerate slightly when space allowed, and another from Ibn Abbas where the Prophet commanded calmness and condemned rough driving.
These are ahad hadiths, but their meaning is clear and supported by the general principle of avoiding harm.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
From the first hadith, the phrase 'whenever he came to a hill, he would loosen it a little' indicates that acceleration is only when there is space. The second hadith explicitly says 'righteousness is not in making camels run,' proving that harming others by speeding is not part of righteousness.
The evidence shows a distinction: permissible haste when no harm, prohibited when harm occurs.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools may consider slight haste as sunnah in all circumstances, but the Hanafis emphasize the condition of safety. The authoritative position is that any form of harm is haram.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf rooted in different interpretations of the same hadiths.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi because it harmonizes both hadiths and prioritizes the overarching principle of avoiding harm (la darar wa la dirar). The Prophet's own practice of accelerating only when there was space is the operative example.
The ruling is practical and considers crowded conditions during Hajj.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۳۴۳) واذا وجدفرجة يُسرع من غير ان يؤذى احدا ويتحرّز عما يفعله الجهلة من الاشتداد في السير والازدحام والايذاء فانه حرام (۱۳۴۴) حتى يأتى مزدلفة فينزل بقرب جبل قُزح ويرتفع عن
ترجمه : (۱۳۴۳) اگر کشادگی پائے تو بغیر کسی کو تکلیف دیئے جلدی چلیں۔ اور بچے ان باتوں سے جو جاہل لوگ کرتے ہیں، مثلا چلنے میں تیزی کرنا، بھیڑ کرنا ، تکلیف دینا (وغیرہ) کیونکہ یہ حرام ہیں۔ تشریح : راستہ ملے تو تھوڑی تیزی سے چلے تاکہ عشاء تک مزدلفہ پہنچ جائے ، البتہ لوگوں کو تکلیف دینے سے، یا بھیٹر کرنے سے بچے ، کیونکہ یہ حرام ہیں۔
صلى الله
وجه : (۱) اس کے لئے حدیث یہ ہے۔ قال دخـلـنـا عـلـى جابر بن عبد الله ... ويقول بيده اليمنى ايها الناس السكينة السكينة كلما اتى حبلا من الحبال ارخى لها قليلا حتى تصعد حتى اتى المزدلفة . (مسلم شريف، باب حجتہ النبی ص ۵۱۵، نمبر ۲۹۵۰/۱۲۱۸ / ابو داؤد شریف ، باب صفت حجتہ النبی ص ۲۷۸، نمبر ۱۹۰۵) اس حدیث میں ہے که کشادگی ملتی تو اونٹنی کو ذرا تیز کرتے ، ورنہ خود بھی آہستہ چلتے اور دوسروں کو بھی آہستہ چلنے کی ترغیب دیتے ۔ (۲) اس حدیث میں بھی ہے کہ اطمینان سے چلے . حدثنی ابن عباس أنه دفع مع النبى الله يوم عرفة فسمع النبي ل ورائه زجرا شدیدا و ضربا شديدا و ضربا للابل فأشار بسوطه اليهم و قال أيها الناس عليكم بالسكينة فان البر ليس بالا يضاع - ( بخاری شریف ، باب امرالنبی ا بالسكيديه عند الافاضة واشارت اليهم بالسوط میں ۲۷۱، نمبر ۱۶۷) اس حدیث میں بھی ہے کہ اطمینان سے چلے۔ لغت : فرجه : کشادگی ، راستہ ۔ یو ڈی ایذاء سے مشتق ہے، تکلیف دینا۔ تحرز تجرز سے مشتق ہے احتراز کرے، بچے۔ الجملة : جاہل کی جمع ہے، جاہل لوگ۔ اشتداد: شد سے مشتق ہے، دوڑ نا سختی کرنا۔ ازدحام: زحام سے مشتق ہے، بھیٹر کرنا۔
(1343) And if he finds an opening, he may hasten without harming anyone, and he should avoid what the ignorant do of speeding in walking, crowding, and causing harm; for indeed that is haram. (1344) Until he comes to Muzdalifah and alights near Mount Quzah, and rises above... Translation: (1343) If he finds space, he may walk quickly without causing harm to anyone. And he should avoid those things that ignorant people do, such as speeding in walking, crowding, causing harm (etc.), because these are haram. Explanation: If there is space, he may walk with slight haste to reach Muzdalifah by Isha. However, he should avoid harming others or crowding, for that is haram. Evidence: (1) For this there is a hadith: 'We entered upon Jabir ibn Abdullah...' and he said with his right hand, 'O people, calmness, calmness.' Whenever he came to a hill, he would loosen it a little so that it could ascend until he came to Muzdalifah. (Muslim, Bab Hajjat an-Nabi, p. 515, no. 2950/1218; Abu Dawud, Bab Sifat Hajjat an-Nabi, p. 278, no. 1905) In this hadith, when there was space, he would make the camel go a little faster; otherwise he walked slowly and encouraged others to do so. (2) Another hadith also indicates calmness: Ibn Abbas narrated that he left with the Prophet on the day of Arafat and heard behind him severe shouting and beating of camels; the Prophet pointed with his whip to them and said, 'O people, be calm, for righteousness is not in making (camels) run.' (Bukhari, Bab Amr an-Nabi bis-Sakinah 'inda al-Ifadah, p. 271, no. 167) This hadith also commands calmness. Vocabulary: فرجة: space, opening; يؤذي: to harm; يتحرز: to avoid; الجهلة: ignorant people; الاشتداد: speeding; الازدحام: crowding.
Source pages p. 372

Commentary
This passage addresses the manner of traveling from Arafat to Muzdalifah. The ruling is that if there is a clear path (فرجة), one may hasten slightly to reach Muzdalifah in time for Isha prayer, but without causing harm or inconvenience to others. The acts of the ignorant – excessive speed, crowding, and harming others – are explicitly declared haram (forbidden). The proof is from the hadith of Jabir where the Prophet would increase speed when space allowed, but otherwise maintained calmness. The second hadith from Ibn Abbas shows the Prophet commanding calmness and prohibiting rough driving. Thus, the Hanafi position balances the need to reach Muzdalifah with the obligation to avoid harm and maintain order.

Key Terms
فرجة (furjah): An opening or clear space in the path allowing for slight acceleration.
حرام (haram): Religiously forbidden; incurring sin.
الجهلة (al-jahilah): Ignorant people who act without knowledge of proper Hajj conduct.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on causing harm to others during the journey from Arafat to Muzdalifah?
A) Permissible if one is in a hurry
B) Makruh (disliked)
C) Haram (forbidden)
D) Recommended

Key Takeaway
Hastening is permissible only when there is a clear path and no harm; causing harm is always haram.

Stopping at Muzdalifah Near Mount Quzah
Ruling on the recommended stopping place in Muzdalifah with evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended place to stop in Muzdalifah and explain its basis in Quran and Sunnah.

Core Idea
Stop near Mount Quzah in Muzdalifah — the Mash'ar al-Haram — following the Prophet's example.

This lesson explains the preferred location for the overnight stay in Muzdalifah. While the entire plain is permissible, the Hanafi school strongly encourages halting near Mount Quzah, identified as the 'Mash'ar al-Haram' mentioned in the Quran. The Prophet's practice confirms this recommendation. You will learn the ruling, its evidence, and why avoiding the valley floor respects other pilgrims.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the overnight halt in Muzdalifah. The ruling is 'mustahabb' (recommended) to stop near Mount Quzah, not obligatory.
2
Locate the primary proof
The Quranic verse 2:198 commands remembrance at the 'Mash'ar al-Haram'. The Hanafis identify this as Mount Quzah.
Quran is qat'i in transmission; its dalala is zanni when identifying the location.
3
Trace the secondary proof
The hadith of Jabir (Muslim) shows the Prophet rode to the Mash'ar al-Haram, i.e., Mount Quzah, and stopped there.
The hadith is ahad, but its meaning is clear.
4
Apply the ruling in practice
The recommendation includes staying slightly above the valley floor to allow people to pass. The entire Muzdalifah is valid, but proximity to Mount Quzah is best.
Wadi Muhassar is not a place of halt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۳۴۴) حتى يأتى مزدلفة فينزل بقرب جبل قُزح ويرتفع عن بطن الوادى ليمر الناس .
ترجمه : (۱۳۴۴) یہاں تک کہ مزدلفہ آئے ، اور قزح پہاڑ کے قریب اترے، اور گزرنے والوں کی سہولت کے خیال سے بطن وادی کے اوپر ٹھہرے۔ تشریح : مزدلفہ میں مستحب یہ ہے کہ جبل قزح کے قریب ٹھہرے۔ یوں تو وادی محسر کے علاوہ پورا مزدلفہ ٹھہرنے کی جگہ ہے۔لیکن جبل قزح کے قریب ٹھہر نا مستحب ہے۔ بطن وادی سے لوگ گزرتے ہیں اس لئے اس سے تھوڑا اوپر ہٹ کر ٹھہرے۔ وجه (۱) کیونکہ حضور وہیں ٹھہرے تھے۔ آیت میں ہے۔ فاذا افضتم من عرفات فاذكروا الله عند المشعر الحرام ( آیت ۱۹۸ سورۃ البقرۃ ۲) اس آیت میں ہے کہ عرفات سے چلو تو مشعر الحرام کے پاس اللہ کو خوب یاد کرو اور جبل قزح کو مشعر الحرام کہتے ہیں (۲) حدیث میں ہے۔ قال دخلنا علی جابر بن عبد الله ... ثم ركب القصواء حتى اتى المشعر الحرام .
(1344) Until he comes to Muzdalifah and alights near Mount Quzah and rises above the bottom of the valley to allow people to pass. Translation: (1344) Until he comes to Muzdalifah, and alights near Mount Quzah, and stays above the valley floor to facilitate the passage of people. Explanation: In Muzdalifah, it is recommended to stay near Mount Quzah. Although the entire Muzdalifah is a place of halt except for Wadi Muhassar, it is recommended to stay near Mount Quzah. People pass through the valley, so one should stay slightly above it. Evidence: (1) Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) stayed there. The verse states: 'Then when you depart from Arafat, remember Allah at the Sacred Monument' (2:198). This verse mentions remembering Allah near the Sacred Monument, and Mount Quzah is called the Sacred Monument. (2) The hadith: 'We entered upon Jabir ibn Abdullah... then he rode Qaswa until he came to the Sacred Monument.'
Source pages p. 372

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling on where to stop in Muzdalifah. It is recommended (mustahabb) to alight near Mount Quzah, which is identified as the 'Mash'ar al-Haram' (Sacred Monument) mentioned in the Quran. The Prophet (peace be upon him) stopped there. Additionally, one should avoid the middle of the valley to allow people to pass, so a spot slightly elevated is preferred. The entire Muzdalifah is permissible for halting except for Wadi Muhassar, but the nearness to Mount Quzah is the sunnah. The proof is both from the Quranic command to remember Allah at the Mash'ar al-Haram and from the hadith of Jabir describing the Prophet's action.

Key Terms
مزدلفة (Muzdalifah): A place between Arafat and Mina where pilgrims halt after Arafat.
جبل قزح (Jabal Quzah): A mountain in Muzdalifah; considered the Mash'ar al-Haram.
المشعر الحرام (al-Mash'ar al-Haram): The Sacred Monument; identified as Mount Quzah in Muzdalifah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following best describes the Hanafi ruling on stopping in Muzdalifah?
A) It is wajib to stop at Mount Quzah.
B) It is sunnah to stop near Mount Quzah.
C) It is fard to avoid the valley floor.
D) Stopping anywhere in Muzdalifah is makruh except near the mountain.

Key Takeaway
The sunnah is to halt near Mount Quzah (Mash'ar al-Haram) in Muzdalifah, avoiding the valley floor for ease of others.

Ruling on Hastening at Muzdalifah and Avoiding Harm
Ruling on permissible speed during Hajj journey

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hastening during the Hajj journey and apply the condition that distinguishes permissible haste from haram harm.

Core Idea
Hastening is sunnah only when no harm is done; harming others in Hajj is haram.

Many pilgrims rush during the critical journey from Arafah to Muzdalifah, often jostling and causing harm. This lesson examines the precise Hanafi ruling: a moderate increase in pace is encouraged when there is space, but any act of crowding, pushing, or harm is strictly forbidden. We will explore the textual proof from the Prophet's practice and his explicit command for tranquillity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Possible Rulings
The passage describes two types of behavior: hastening when there is a gap, and the actions of the ignorant—rushing, crowding, harming. First, determine the hukm for each.
2
Locate the Dalil
Two hadith are cited: one from Jabir showing the Prophet quickening when the path was clear, and another from Ibn Abbas where the Prophet rebuked harsh driving and commanded calmness. Identify the proof type.
The hadith are ahad (zanni al-thubut) but sufficient for establishing the ruling.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
The command 'alaykum bi al-sakinah' is a verbal prohibition of haste that causes harm, while the Prophet's own action of occasionally quickening indicates permissibility when conditions are safe.
The Hanafi principle: a command (amr) indicates obligation unless contextual evidence shows otherwise.
4
Note the Ikhtilaf
The passage implies agreement on the prohibition of harm, but the permissibility of moderate haste may be debated. The Hanafi position follows the Prophet's practice.
Intra-school and inter-school differences exist on whether moderate haste is recommended or merely permitted.
5
Apply the Ruling to a New Scenario
Consider a pilgrim who pushes others to reach the front quickly. Apply the ruling: this is haram because it causes harm. Contrast with one who walks faster when the path is clear.
The key distinction is the presence or absence of harm.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا وجدفرجة يُسرع من غير ان يؤذى احدا ويتحرّز عما يفعله الجهلة من الاشتداد في السير والازدحام والايذاء فانه حرام ترجمه : إذا وجد فرجة يسرع من غير إيذاء أحد ويتحرز مما يفعله الجهلة من الإشتداد والإزدحام والإيذاء فإنه حرام تشريح : راستہ ملے تو تھوڑی تیزی سے چلے تاکہ عشاء تک مزدلفہ پہنچ جائے ، البتہ لوگوں کو تکلیف دینے سے، یا بھیٹر کرنے سے بچے ، کیونکہ یہ حرام ہیں۔ وجه : (۱) اس کے لئے حدیث یہ ہے۔ قال دخـلـنـا عـلـى جابر بن عبد الله ... ويقول بيده اليمنى ايها الناس السكينة السكينة كلما اتى حبلا من الحبال ارخى لها قليلا حتى تصعد حتى اتى المزدلفة . (مسلم شريف، باب حجتہ النبی ص ۵۱۵، نمبر ۲۹۵۰/۱۲۱۸ / ابو داؤد شریف ، باب صفت حجتہ النبی ص ۲۷۸، نمبر ۱۹۰۵) (۲) حدثني ابن عباس أنه دفع مع النبى الله يوم عرفة فسمع النبي ل ورائه زجرا شدیدا و ضربا شديدا و ضربا للابل فأشار بسوطه اليهم و قال أيها الناس عليكم بالسكينة فان البر ليس بالا يضاع - ( بخاری شریف ، باب امرالنبی ا بالسكيديه عند الافاضة واشارت اليهم بالسوط میں ۲۷۱، نمبر ۱۶۷) لغت : فرجه : کشادگی ، راستہ ۔ یو ڈی ایذاء سے مشتق ہے، تکلیف دینا۔ تحرز تجرز سے مشتق ہے احتراز کرے، بچے۔ الجملة : جاہل کی جمع ہے، جاہل لوگ۔ اشتداد: شد سے مشتق ہے، دوڑ نا سختی کرنا۔ ازدحام: زحام سے مشتق ہے، بھیٹر کرنا۔
If he finds a gap, he hastens without harming anyone and avoids what the ignorant do of rushing in walking, crowding, and harming – for indeed it is haram. Translation: If he finds a gap, he hastens without harming anyone and avoids what the ignorant do of rushing, crowding, and harming – for indeed it is haram. Commentary: When the road is clear, he walks a bit quickly so that he reaches Muzdalifah before Isha. However, he should avoid causing trouble to people or crowding, because these are haram. Evidence: (1) For this is the hadith: We entered upon Jabir ibn Abdullah... he said with his right hand: O people, tranquillity, tranquillity. Whenever he came to a mountain path, he loosened (the reins) a little until it ascended, until he came to Muzdalifah. (Muslim, number 2950/1218; Abu Dawud, number 1905) (2) Ibn Abbas narrated that he departed with the Prophet on the day of Arafah, and the Prophet heard behind him severe urging and beating of camels, so he gestured to them with his whip and said: O people, adhere to tranquillity, for righteousness is not attained by rushing. (Bukhari, number 167) Lexicon: فرجة: opening, path. إيذاء: causing harm. تحرز: to guard against. الجهلة: ignorant people. اشتداد: rushing. ازدحام: crowding.
Source pages p. 372

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Sunnah. It addresses the behavior during the journey from Arafah to Muzdalifah. The ruling states that if one finds a gap (space in the crowd), they may hasten their pace slightly, but must avoid harming others, rushing excessively, crowding, or causing any harm – as these actions are haram (forbidden) because they violate the sanctity of the pilgrimage and cause injury. The commentary explains that the purpose of hastening is to reach Muzdalifah in time for Isha prayer. The evidence includes two hadith: one from Jabir showing the Prophet (peace be upon him) occasionally quickened his pace when the path was clear, but otherwise commanded tranquility; and another from Ibn Abbas where the Prophet forbade harsh driving and emphasized calmness. Thus, the Hanafi position is that moderate haste when there is room is sunnah, but any form of harmful behavior is strictly prohibited.

Key Terms
فرجة (farijah): A gap or opening in the crowd along the path.
ازدحام (izdiham): Crowding or pushing against others.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on crowding and harming others during the journey to Muzdalifah?
A) It is permitted if one is in a hurry.
B) It is makruh tahrimi.
C) It is haram.
D) It is mustahabb for reward.

Key Takeaway
Hastening in Hajj is permissible only when it causes no harm; any act of crowding or harm is strictly haram.

Staying at Muzdalifah near Jabal Quzah
Ruling on the recommended place to stay in Muzdalifah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended (mustahabb) place to stay in Muzdalifah and explain the evidence from Quran and Sunnah.

Core Idea
Staying near Jabal Quzah in Muzdalifah is sunnah, though all of Muzdalifah except Wadi Muhassir is valid.

When the pilgrim reaches Muzdalifah after departing Arafat, he must know where to stay. While the entire plain of Muzdalifah (except the valley of Muhassir) is a valid place for the night, the Prophet ﷺ specifically stood near Jabal Quzah, which is identified as the 'Mash'ar al-Haram' (Sacred Monument). This lesson examines the ruling and its proof from the Quran and the practice of the Prophet.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended location
From the text, note that the pilgrim should descend near Jabal Quzah (the hill known as the Sacred Monument). This is stated as mustahabb (recommended).
The term 'Jabal Quzah' is the specific hill in Muzdalifah.
2
Understand the exception: avoid the valley floor
The text advises to stay above the valley floor (baṭn al-wādī) to allow passersby to move freely. This is a practical consideration for crowd management.
This does not affect the validity of staying in the valley, but it is a recommended conduct.
3
Note the scope: all of Muzdalifah is a standing place
The text explicitly states that the entire Muzdalifah (except Wadi Muhassir) is a place for staying. Thus, the recommendation is not a requirement; any location within Muzdalifah fulfills the obligation.
Wadi Muhassir is excluded because it is not part of Muzdalifah for the night stay.
4
Examine the Quranic evidence
The passage cites Quran 2:198: 'When you depart from Arafat, remember Allah at the sacred monument.' The 'sacred monument' (al-mash'ar al-ḥarām) is interpreted as Jabal Quzah, linking the verse to the Prophet's practice.
The Quranic command is general, but the Prophet's specific action provides the interpretation.
5
Examine the hadith evidence
Two hadith are cited: one from Jabir describing the Prophet riding to the sacred monument, and another from Ali that the Prophet stood at Quzah and declared 'this is the standing place, and all of Muzdalifah is a standing place.' This establishes both the preferred spot and the permissibility of other areas.
The hadith from Abu Dawud (no. 1935) is a sound (ṣaḥīḥ) hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Commentary: In Muzdalifah, it is mustahabb to stay near Jabal Quzah. Although the entire Muzdalifah except Wadi Muhassir is a place for staying, staying near Jabal Quzah is mustahabb. Allah says: 'When you depart from Arafat, remember Allah at the sacred monument.' (2:198) (2) Hadith: We entered upon Jabir ibn Abdullah... then he rode al-Qaswa until he came to the sacred monument. Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the recommended place to stay in Muzdalifah during Hajj. The ruling states that the pilgrim should descend near Jabal Quzah (the 'Sacred Monument') and avoid the middle of the valley to allow space for others to pass. The commentary clarifies that the entire plain of Muzdalifah except Wadi Muhassir is valid for staying, but the area near Jabal Quzah is mustahabb based on the Prophet's practice. The evidence includes the Quranic verse about remembering Allah at the 'Mash'ar al-Haram' (Sacred Monument), which is interpreted as Jabal Quzah, and hadith from Jabir and Ali confirming that the Prophet stood there. Thus, the Hanafi position emphasizes following the sunnah by staying near this specific location when possible.

Key Terms

بطن الوادي (baṭn al-wādī): The middle or floor of the valley, where people pass through.

Combining Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah
Ruling on combining prayers at Muzdalifah with one adhan and iqamah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on combining Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah and explain the evidence from hadith.

Core Idea
At Muzdalifah, combine Maghrib and Isha with one adhan and one iqamah; a gap requires repeating the iqamah.

The pilgrim at Muzdalifah has a unique opportunity to combine two prayers with a single adhan and iqamah. This practice is rooted in the Prophet's ﷺ sunnah, but its implementation requires attention to sequence. The ruling clarifies when a new iqamah becomes necessary, ensuring the unity of the two prayers is preserved.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is combining Maghrib (3 rak'ahs) and Isha (2 rak'ahs) at Muzdalifah. The hukm level is sunnah muakkadah (confirmed sunnah), not fard or wajib.
This is specific to the hajj context; not general jama'.
2
Locate the dalil
Two ahadith are cited: one from Jabir (with one adhan and two iqamahs) and one from Ibn Umar (with one iqamah). The Hanafi school relies on the latter as the preferred practice.
Both are from Sahih Muslim and Abu Dawud.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's ﷺ explicit action demonstrates the permissibility and desirability of combining with one adhan and one iqamah. The condition to repeat iqamah if a gap occurs is derived from the need to maintain the connection between the two prayers.
The command to repeat iqamah is implied by the sunnah.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Jabir's hadith mentions two iqamahs. The Hanafi school reconciles by considering one iqamah sufficient, as it is simpler and consistent with Ibn Umar's report.
This is an intra-Hanafi variation; the mufta bihi is one iqamah.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The majority of Hanafi scholars prefer the version with one iqamah for practicality and ease, following the principle of taking the lighter side when evidence is not fully explicit.
Al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah supports this view.

And he prays Maghrib and Isha there with one adhan and one iqamah. And if he prays a voluntary prayer between them or busies himself, he repeats the iqamah. Translation: And in Muzdalifah, he prays Maghrib and Isha with one adhan and one iqamah. If he prayed nafl between them or engaged in some work, he should repeat the iqamah. Commentary: He should pray Maghrib and Isha with one adhan and one iqamah, and not pray nafl between them. If he did pray nafl or do something, he should say the iqamah again. Evidence: (1) Hadith: We entered upon Jabir ibn Abdullah... until he came to Muzdalifah and prayed Maghrib and Isha there with one adhan and two iqamahs, and he did not pray anything between them. (Muslim, number 2950/1218; Abu Dawud, number 1905) (2) Ibn Umar said: The Messenger of Allah combined Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah, praying Maghrib three rak'ahs and Isha two rak'ahs with one iqamah. (Muslim, number 3114/1288)
Source pages p. 373

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the method of combining prayers at Muzdalifah. It states that the pilgrim should pray Maghrib (three rak'ahs) and Isha (two rak'ahs) together with a single adhan and a single iqamah. There should be no voluntary prayer or other activity between them. If one does perform a nafl or becomes occupied, they must repeat the iqamah to re-establish the connection. The evidence comes from two hadith: one from Jabir mentioning one adhan and two iqamahs, and another from Ibn Umar mentioning one iqamah. The Hanafi school reconciles these by preferring the ruling that one iqamah suffices, as it is the simplest and most consistent with the practice of Ibn Umar. The commentary clarifies that the iqamah should be repeated only if a significant gap occurs, not for a momentary pause.

Key Terms
اذان (adhān): The call to prayer announcing the time; here used for both Maghrib and Isha together.
اقامة (iqāmah): The call to commence the prayer; repeated if a gap occurs between the combined prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Nothing; the prayer is still valid.
B) He must repeat both prayers.
C) He should repeat the iqamah only.
D) He should say a new adhan.

Key Takeaway
At Muzdalifah, Maghrib and Isha are combined with one adhan and one iqamah; if a gap occurs, repeat only the iqamah.

Ruling on Praying Maghrib on the Road to Muzdalifah
Ruling that Maghrib is not valid on the road; must be repeated

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that Maghrib prayed before reaching Muzdalifah is invalid and explain the proof and obligation to repeat it before Fajr.

Core Idea
Maghrib on the night of Muzdalifah is only valid at Muzdalifah; praying en route invalidates it.

In the Hajj rituals, the night at Muzdalifah (9th–10th Dhul Hijjah) carries a unique rule for the Maghrib and Isha prayers. The Hanafi school holds that both prayers must be performed after arriving at Muzdalifah; Maghrib cannot be prayed on the road. This lesson examines the ruling and its proof, clarifying why such a prayer is invalid and what the pilgrim must do.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is praying Maghrib while still on the road to Muzdalifah on the night of the 10th. The ruling is that it is invalid (la tajuz) and must be repeated before Fajr.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is based on the established practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) who combined Maghrib and Isha only after arriving at Muzdalifah. This indicates that the time for Maghrib on that night is specifically tied to being at Muzdalifah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'la tajuz' directly states invalidity. The reasoning: praying before arriving is like praying before its prescribed time, which is defective. The Prophet did not pray Maghrib on the road but waited.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some other schools allow praying Maghrib at its usual time even while travelling, but the Hanafi school requires the combination at Muzdalifah as a binding sunnah.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is that Maghrib on the road is invalid and must be repeated before Fajr. This is the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school.

Commentary
This passage states a key Hanafi ruling: the Maghrib prayer on the night of Muzdalifah (9th Dhul Hijjah) has a specific time that only begins after arriving at Muzdalifah. If one prays Maghrib while still on the road, it is invalid (la tajuz) and must be repeated before Fajr of the following day. The commentary adds that this is the madhhab of Imam Abu Hanifa. The reasoning is that the time for Maghrib on this night is deferred to Muzdalifah for the purpose of combining with Isha. Thus, praying it on the road is like praying before its proper time. The hadith text that appears mixed in the OCR (about Jabal Quzah) likely belongs to the previous lesson and is a copy-paste error. The focus of this lesson is the invalidity of pre-Muzdalifah Maghrib.

D) It becomes qada and can be made up later.

Key Takeaway
Maghrib on the night of Muzdalifah is only valid after arriving at Muzdalifah; praying it on the road is invalid and must be repeated before Fajr.

Combining Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah
Ruling and proof for combining prayers at Muzdalifah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for combining Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah, identify the required adhan and iqamah, and explain the consequence of performing optional prayers between them.

Core Idea
At Muzdalifah, combine Maghrib and Isha with one adhan and one iqamah; optional acts between them require repeating the iqamah.

This lesson covers a specific ritual of Hajj: the combination of Maghrib and Isha prayers at Muzdalifah. The Hanafi school derives this practice from the Prophet's sunnah, emphasizing the proper sequence and the prohibition of intervening optional prayers. Understanding this ruling ensures that pilgrims perform this wajib act correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what is being ruled upon: the combination of Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah. The Hanafi school classifies this as wajib.
Wajib means obligatory but with a proof that is zanni al-thubut (single transmission).
2
Locate the dalil
Find the evidence: hadith from Jabir and Ibn Umar describing the Prophet's practice. These are ahad hadith, thus zanni in transmission.
The Prophet combined Maghrib and Isha with one adhan and one or two iqamahs, and did not perform any optional prayers between them.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the dalil proves the ruling. The Prophet's action demonstrates the prescribed method, and the absence of optional acts implies prohibition.
The hadith do not explicitly forbid optional prayers, but the Hanafi school infers the rule from the perfect example of the Prophet.
4
Note the consequence of violation
If optional prayers are performed between the two, the iqamah is invalidated and must be repeated. The prayers themselves remain valid.
This is a unique Hanafi ruling; the iqamah is considered a necessary part of the combined act.
5
Consider cross-madhhab differences
The Shafi'i school allows optional prayers between the two, as they do not see an explicit prohibition. The Hanafi position is stricter.
The practical difference: a Shafi'i pilgrim may pray sunnahs; a Hanafi pilgrim must avoid them or repeat the iqamah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويصلّى بها المغرب والعشاء باذان واحد واقامة واحدة ولو تطوّع بينهما او تشاغل اعاد الاقامة. عن جابر بن عبد الله قال: حتى أتى المزدلفة فصلى بها المغرب والعشاء بأذان واحد و إقامتين و لم يسبح بينهما شيئا. و عن ابن عمر قال: جمع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بين المغرب والعشاء بجمع صلى المغرب ثلاثا والعشاء ركعتين باقامة واحدة.
And Maghrib and Isha are prayed there with one adhan and one iqamah. If one prays optional prayers between them or busies himself, he repeats the iqamah. From Jabir ibn Abdullah: He came to Muzdalifah and prayed Maghrib and Isha there with one adhan and two iqamahs, and did not pray anything between them. And from Ibn Umar: The Messenger of Allah combined Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah, praying Maghrib as three and Isha as two with one iqamah.
Source pages p. 373

Commentary
This is a ruling from the chapter on Hajj regarding the combination of Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah. The ruling states that both prayers are performed with a single adhan and a single iqamah. If one engages in optional prayers or other activities between the two prescribed prayers, he must repeat the iqamah before the second prayer. This is based on the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) as narrated by Jabir and Ibn Umar. The hadith of Jabir indicates one adhan and two iqamahs, while Ibn Umar's narration mentions one iqamah. The Hanafi school reconciles these by considering both narrations valid, with the preferred practice being one adhan and one iqamah. The prohibition of optional prayers between them ensures that the combination is performed properly without interruption.

Key Terms
أذان (adhan): The call to prayer announcing the beginning of the prescribed prayer time.
إقامة (iqamah): The second call to prayer immediately before the start of the congregational prayer.
تطوع (tatawwu'): Optional or supererogatory prayers performed voluntarily.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) He must repeat only the adhan.
D) No action is needed; optional prayers are allowed.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires one adhan and one iqamah for combining Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah, and forbids optional prayers between them; violation necessitates iqamah repetition.

Maghrib Prayer on the Way to Muzdalifah: Invalid and Must Be Repeated
Ruling with evidence and intra-Hanafi dispute on Maghrib during Hajj.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Maghrib prayer performed before reaching Muzdalifah, explain the evidence, and distinguish the position of Abu Hanifa from Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Maghrib on the way to Muzdalifah is invalid; repetition before dawn is wajib according to Abu Hanifa.

The Hajj journey from Arafat to Muzdalifah on the 9th of Dhul-Hijjah has a specific ruling for Maghrib prayer. This lesson examines the Hanafi position that Maghrib must be delayed until reaching Muzdalifah, and if prayed earlier, it is invalid and must be repeated. We will also explore the intra-Hanafi dispute with Imam Abu Yusuf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is praying Maghrib on the way to Muzdalifah. The ruling: invalid, must be repeated before dawn.
2
Locate the dalil
The text cites hadith from Usamah ibn Zaid and the saying of Ibn Mas'ud. Identify these as evidence.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's statement 'Prayer is ahead of you' and his action of delaying indicate that the time for Maghrib is transferred to Muzdalifah.
4
Identify the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Yusuf holds that Maghrib is valid if prayed on the way because the time has entered; the delayed prayer is sunnah, not wajib.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is Abu Hanifa's, requiring repetition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم تجز المغرب في طريق المزدلفة وعليه اعادتها ما لم يطلع الفجر. عن أسامة بن زيد أنه سمع النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول: الصلاة أمامك فجاء المزدلفة فصلى المغرب. عن عبد الله بن مسعود قال: هما صلاتان تحولان عن وقتهما: صلاة المغرب بعد ما يأتي الناس المزدلفة، والفجر حين يبزغ الفجر.
And Maghrib is not valid on the way to Muzdalifah, and one must repeat it as long as dawn has not risen. From Usamah ibn Zaid: He heard the Prophet say, 'Prayer is ahead of you,' so he came to Muzdalifah and prayed Maghrib. From Abdullah ibn Mas'ud: They are two prayers that are shifted from their times: Maghrib after people come to Muzdalifah, and Fajr when dawn breaks.
Source pages p. 373

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling for Maghrib prayer on the evening of the 9th of Dhul-Hijjah. The Hanafi position, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, is that Maghrib must be delayed until reaching Muzdalifah. If someone prays Maghrib on the way, the prayer is invalid and must be repeated before Fajr of the next day. The evidence is from the hadith of Usamah ibn Zaid, where the Prophet (peace be upon him) delayed the prayer until Muzdalifah, and from the statement of Ibn Mas'ud that the time for Maghrib is changed to after reaching Muzdalifah. However, there is a dispute within the Hanafi school: Imam Abu Yusuf holds that if someone prays Maghrib on the way or even at Arafat after sunset, the prayer is valid and does not need to be repeated, because the actual time for Maghrib has entered. For Abu Yusuf, performing it at Muzdalifah is a sunnah, not a wajib. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school is that of Imam Abu Hanifa, requiring repetition before dawn.

Key Terms
إعادة (i'adah): The repetition of a prayer that was performed invalidly or before its proper time.
طريق المزدلفة (tariq al-muzdalifah): The road or path leading to Muzdalifah from Arafat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what must a pilgrim do if he prays Maghrib on the way to Muzdalifah?
A) Nothing; the prayer is valid.
B) He must repeat it before dawn.
C) He must repeat it after dawn.
D) He must offer a sacrifice as expiation.

Key Takeaway
Maghrib prayer performed before reaching Muzdalifah during Hajj is invalid and must be repeated before dawn, according to the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Staying Overnight at Muzdalifah: Sunnah or Wajib?
Ruling on mabit at Muzdalifah with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for mabit at Muzdalifah according to this text, identify the proofs, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on its wajib/sunnah status.

Core Idea
Mabit at Muzdalifah is sunnah according to this text but wajib in the relied-upon Hanafi position.

This passage from Thamaratun Najah addresses the legal status of spending the night at Muzdalifah during Hajj. It classifies the act as sunnah, but a deeper look reveals a well-known intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: many authoritative Hanafi works consider it wajib. We will analyze the textual proofs and the reasoning behind the difference, building skill in evaluating fiqh rulings across authoritative layers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Read the opening phrase 'Wa yusanna al-mabit bi al-Muzdalifah' – the ruling is sunnah (recommended). Note that this is a categorical statement.
The term 'yusanna' is a clear indicator of the sunnah classification.
2
Locate the proofs cited
The author then cites Quran 2:198 ('اذكروا الله عند المشعر الحرام') and the hadith of Urwah ibn Mudarris. Identify each as Quran (qat'i thubut, zanni dalala) and hadith ahad (zanni thubut and dalala).
The hadith is from Urwah ibn Mudarris as recorded in Sunan al-Kubra.
3
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah (how the proofs support the ruling)
The Quranic verse commands remembrance at the Sacred Monument (Muzdalifah), but it does not explicitly command staying overnight – the obligation is to remember Allah, not to sleep there. The hadith emphasizes attending the Fajr prayer at Muzdalifah, but does not mandate staying the whole night. Hence, the author deduces sunnah, not wajib.
Other Hanafis interpret the command as implying wajib because the remembrance is part of the hajj rituals at that place; they consider staying a necessary means.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The commentary points out that other Hanafi books (especially Zahir al-Riwayah) consider mabit wajib. This is because the command to 'remember Allah' is taken as an obligation, and staying overnight enables the recommended acts like praying Fajr early and making supplications.
The discrepancy reflects different usuli approaches: amr (command) for obligation vs. recommendation, and the role of qiyas.
5
Evaluate the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
Though this text says sunnah, the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school (mufta bihi) is that mabit at Muzdalifah is wajib. This is based on the weight of evidence in Zahir al-Riwayah and the tarjih by later authorities.
In practice, pilgrims should treat it as wajib to avoid missing a required element.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويُسنّ المبيت بالمزدلفة. فاذكروا الله عند المشعر الحرام. عن عروة بن مضرس الطائي قال: أتيت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بالموقف يعني بجمع فقلت: جئت يا رسول الله من جبلي طيء أكللت مطيتي وأتعبت نفسي، والله ما تركت من حبل إلا وقفت عليه، فهل لي من حج؟ فقال: من أدرك معنا هذه الصلاة، وأتى عرفات قبل ذلك ليلا أو نهارا فقد تم حجه.
And staying overnight at Muzdalifah is sunnah. 'And remember Allah at the Sacred Monument.' From Urwah ibn Mudarris al-Ta'i: I came to the Messenger of Allah at the standing place, meaning at Jam', and said: I came, O Messenger of Allah, from the mountains of Tayy, my mount is exhausted and I tired myself, by Allah I did not leave any mountain pass but I stood at it, so is there Hajj for me? He said: Whoever attends this prayer with us and comes to Arafat before that, night or day, his Hajj is complete.
Source pages p. 374

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling for spending the night (mabit) at Muzdalifah on the night of the 10th of Dhul-Hijjah. The text explicitly states that it is sunnah. However, the commentary notes that in other Hanafi books it is considered wajib. The proof is twofold: first, the Quranic verse (2:198) commanding remembrance at the Sacred Monument (al-Mash'ar al-Haram), which is interpreted as Muzdalifah; second, the hadith of Urwah ibn Mudarris, where the Prophet (peace be upon him) linked the completion of Hajj to attending the prayer (Fajr) at Muzdalifah and having been at Arafat. The hadith implies that being present at Muzdalifah for the prayer is significant, but the author of this text classifies it as sunnah, indicating a difference of opinion within the Hanafi school. The apparent discrepancy is resolved by noting that some consider it wajib due to the command 'remember Allah' being interpreted as obligatory, while others view it as sunnah based on the general permissibility of leaving early.

Key Terms
المبيت (al-mabit): Spending the night at a specific location, here Muzdalifah, during Hajj.
المشعر الحرام (al-mash'ar al-haram): The Sacred Monument; identified as Muzdalifah or a specific hill (Qazah) within it.

Mabit at Muzdalifah is classified as sunnah in this passage, but the Hanafi mufta bihi is wajib; pilgrims should treat it as wajib to avoid dam.

Entire Muzdalifah is a Standing Place Except Batn Muhassir
Ruling specifying the boundaries of valid standing at Muzdalifah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the correct boundaries for standing at Muzdalifah and identify the exception of Batn Muhassir.

Core Idea
The entire Muzdalifah is valid for standing except Batn Muhassir.

In this lesson, we examine the ruling on the standing place at Muzdalifah, a key obligation of Hajj. The Prophet (ﷺ) clearly specified the boundaries, and we will analyse the proof from hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is standing (wuquf) at Muzdalifah. The Hanafi school holds it is wajib.
This is not a rukn; its omission requires dam.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith from Sunan al-Bayhaqi and Ibn Majah where the Prophet (ﷺ) said: 'All of Muzdalifah is a standing place, but avoid Batn Muhassir.'
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit prohibition ('avoid') indicates that Batn Muhassir is excluded from the valid area.
The command is understood as indicating prohibition.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is no ikhtilaf; all schools agree on this ruling.
The hadith is clear and accepted by all.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The mufta bihi is the same as the zahir riwayah: standing must be within Muzdalifah proper, not in Batn Muhassir.
Authority weight: zahir riwayah.

Supplication at Muzdalifah and Departure Before Sunrise
Ruling on earnest supplication at Muzdalifah and departure before sunrise

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on supplication at Muzdalifah and identify the sunnah time for departing to Mina.

Core Idea
The Prophet made earnest dua until bright then departed before sunrise — follow his example.

After the Fajr prayer at Muzdalifah, the pilgrim enters a precious window for intimate supplication. The Prophet stood facing Qibla, raising his hands, beseeching Allah for his ummah. This lesson examines the recommended practice of dua at this sacred station and clarifies the sunnah timing for departing to Mina, based on the hadith of Jabir.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Two acts are described: earnest supplication (dua) at Muzdalifah and departure for Mina. Both are sunnah muakkadah (strongly recommended).
None
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Jabir (Muslim, Abu Dawood) detailing the Prophet's actions at Muzdalifah.
The hadith is ahad, thus zanni in transmission.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's continuous dua until isfar (very bright) and departure before sunrise demonstrates the sunnah practice.
The command is implicit in his action (fi'l).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some may depart immediately after Fajr or after sunrise, but the overwhelming evidence supports the Prophet's specific timing.
All four schools agree on the sunnah timing.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi school adheres to the explicit sunnah as reported. The mufta bihi is to depart before sunrise.
Authority: Zahir al-Riwayah.
