Standing at Muzdalifah: Permissible Areas and Supplication
Explains standing place limits and recommended supplication.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on standing at Muzdalifah, identify the excluded area (Batn Muhassir), and apply the recommended acts of supplication and dhikr as demonstrated by the Prophet.

Core Idea
All of Muzdalifah is a standing place except Batn Muhassir; supplication there is a confirmed sunnah.

This passage establishes both the geographical limits of wuquf at Muzdalifah and the spiritual conduct expected. It provides hadith proofs for the prohibition of stopping in Batn Muhassir and the virtue of earnest dua at this place, following the Prophet's own practice. The author emphasizes that the pilgrim should strive in supplication and engage in dhikr until the time of isfar (brightness) before departing for Mina.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling on standing at Muzdalifah
Identify the legal ruling: the entire area of Muzdalifah is a valid standing place (mawqif) except Batn Muhassir.
The hadith explicitly says 'Muzdalifah is all a standing place' so no specific spot is required.
2
Identify the proof for the exception
Locate the hadith from Muhammad ibn Munkadir that commands to avoid Batn Muhassir.
The command 'ارتفعوا' indicates prohibition.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
Understand how the dalil proves the prohibition: the imperative verb used by the Prophet is understood as a prohibition (nahy) in Hanafi usul.
This is a zanni dalala but sufficient for a makruh tahrimi ruling.
4
Extract the sunnah acts at Muzdalifah
From the hadith of Jabir, list the recommended actions: face qiblah, make dua, say takbir and tahlil, remain standing until isfar, then depart before sunrise.
These are sunnah muakkadah based on the Prophet's practice.
5
Appreciate the virtue of dua at Muzdalifah
Use the story of 'Abbas ibn Mirdas to see how the Prophet's supplication was answered at Muzdalifah after delay at 'Arafah.
This encourages earnest dua at this station.

Section on the composition of the actions of Hajj. All of it is a standing place except the bottom of Muhassir (1350). And he should strive in his supplication and ask Allah to fulfill his desire and request. In explanation: (1) Do not stop in Wadi Muhassir. The reason is this hadith: Muhammad ibn Munkadir informed me that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Arafah is all a standing place, and avoid the bottom of 'Uranah. And Muzdalifah is all a standing place, and avoid Muhassir. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab haythu ma waqafa min 'Arafah ajzah, p. 9459, 186; Sunan Ibn Majah, Bab al-mawqif bi 'Arafat, p. 436, no. 3013) From this hadith it is learned that one should not stop in Batn Muhassir. Translation (1350): And during the state of standing, he should strive greatly in supplication, and at this standing place, he should pray for the completion of his request and desire, just as Allah Ta'ala fulfilled the desire of our leader (peace be upon him). Explanation: At the time of standing in Muzdalifah, especially after the Fajr prayer, he should make many supplications with weeping, because at that time the special supplication of the Prophet was accepted. Allah. Explanation (1): This is the hadith: From 'Abbas ibn Mirdas al-Sulami that his father informed him from his father that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) prayed for forgiveness for his community on the evening of 'Arafah, and he was answered: 'I have forgiven them except the oppressor, for I will take for the oppressed from him.' He said: 'O Lord, if You wish, give the oppressed Paradise and forgive the oppressor.' But he was not answered that evening. When he reached Muzdalifah in the morning, he repeated the supplication and was answered what he asked. He said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) laughed or smiled. Abu Bakr and 'Umar said: 'May our fathers and mothers be sacrificed for you, this is not a time when you usually laugh, so what made you laugh? May Allah keep your teeth cool (i.e., make you smile).' He said: 'When the enemy of Allah, Iblis, learned that Allah the Mighty and Majestic had answered my supplication and forgiven my community, he took dust and began to throw it on his head and called out woe and destruction. So what I saw of his distress made me laugh.' (Ibn Majah, Bab al-du'a' bi 'Arafah, p. 216, no. 3013; Musnad Ahmad, Bab hadith 'Abbas ibn Mirdas al-Sulami, vol. 4, p. 587, no. 15774) From this hadith it is learned that the Prophet made a supplication on the day of 'Arafah, the portion concerning the oppressed was not accepted, and it was accepted on the day of Muzdalifah due to striving in supplication. (2) And until the appearance of dawn, he should continue saying takbir, tahlil, and making supplication. For this there is this hadith: He said: We entered upon Jabir ibn 'Abd Allah... then he rode al-Qaswa' until he came to al-Mash'ar al-Haram, faced the qiblah, made supplication, said Allahu Akbar, La ilaha illa Allah, and affirmed His oneness. He continued standing until it became very bright, then he departed before the sun rose. (Muslim, Bab hujjat al-nabi, p. 515, no. 2950/1218; Abu Dawud, Bab sifat hujjat al-nabi, p. 278, no. 1905) From this hadith it is learned that until it becomes very bright, he continues saying takbir, tahlil, and tahmid, and making supplications. And also that he should leave from there for Mina before sunrise.
Source pages p. 376

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the standing at Muzdalifah. The author first states the ruling that the entire area of Muzdalifah is permissible for standing (wuquf) except Batn Muhassir. He then emphasizes that the pilgrim should strive in supplication at this place. The proof for the prohibition of standing in Batn Muhassir is a hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) said that 'Arafah is all a standing place, and one should avoid Batn 'Uranah and Batn Muhassir. The author then provides a second hadith about the virtue of supplication at Muzdalifah, showing that the Prophet's own supplication for his community was answered when he made it at Muzdalifah after it was delayed at 'Arafah. This illustrates the importance of earnest prayer at this station. Finally, a third hadith describes the Prophet's practice at Muzdalifah: he stood at al-Mash'ar al-Haram, faced the qiblah, and engaged in takbir, tahlil, and supplication until it became very bright, before departing before sunrise. This indicates that the recommended acts at Muzdalifah include abundant dhikr and dua until the time of isfar (brightness). The commentary thus establishes both the legal boundaries of the standing place and the devotional conduct expected there.

Key Terms
بطن محسر (Batn Muhassir): A valley between Muzdalifah and Mina where it is prohibited to stop.
موقف (mawqif): A place of standing where the pilgrim performs wuquf.
اسفار (isfar): The time when the dawn light becomes bright and widespread.

Departure from Muzdalifah Before Sunrise
Ruling on the time to leave Muzdalifah for Mina

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the time of departure from Muzdalifah and explain the evidence from the Prophet's practice.

Core Idea
Depart Muzdalifah before sunrise after it becomes bright — a necessary act based on the Prophet's opposition to polytheists.

This lesson examines the timing of a key Hajj rite: leaving Muzdalifah for Mina on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah. The Hanafi school classifies this as a wajib act, drawing on the explicit practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and the Companions. Let's explore the proofs and the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the ifada (departure) from Muzdalifah to Mina on the morning of the 10th. The Hanafi ruling: it is wajib to depart before sunrise after the time of isfar (brightness).
Wajib means obligatory; omitting it without excuse is sinful.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites two hadiths: the practice of 'Umar ibn al-Khattab and the detailed report of Jabir ibn 'Abd Allah. Both show the Prophet departed before sunrise.
The dalil is fi'li (actions of the Prophet) and taqriri (approval of 'Umar's practice).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit action of the Prophet departing before sunrise, and his opposition to the polytheists who waited until sunrise, establishes that departing before sunrise is the Sunnah. The Hanafi school takes this as an indication of wujub because the Prophet deliberately differed from the polytheists in a ritual matter.
Hanafi principle: the Prophet's disapproval of a practice indicates the opposite is required.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
All schools agree that departing before sunrise is recommended, but the Hanafi school uniquely considers it wajib. The Shafi'i school regards it as sunnah, not wajib.
This difference affects whether a dam (sacrifice) is required if one delays.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is based on the strength of the evidence and the principle of opposing polytheists. The mufta bihi is that departure before sunrise is wajib; leaving after sunrise is makruh tahrimi but the Hajj is valid without a dam according to later authorities.
The text does not specify dam; standard Hanafi fiqh states no dam but it is makruh.

ترجمه : (۱۳۵۱) پھر جب زیادہ روشنی ہو جائے تو امام اور لوگ آفتاب طلوع ہونے سے پہلے روانہ ہوں اور منی آئیں۔

فصل تركيب افعال الحج
ثمرة النجاح جلد ٢ هذا الموقف كما اتمه لسيد محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم (۱۳۵۱) فاذا اسفر جدا افاض الامام والناس قبل طلوع الشمس فيأتي الى منى وينزل بها (۱۳۵۲) ثم يأتى جمرة العقبة فيرميها من بطن تشریح : جب روشنی زیادہ ہو جائے تو امام اور لوگ سورج نکلنے سے پہلے مزدلفہ سے منی کے لئے چل پڑے۔ وجه : (۱) مشرکین سورج کے طلوع ہونے کے بعد مزدلفہ سے چلا کرتے تھے۔ لیکن آپ نے ان کی مخالفت کی اور سورج طلوع ہونے سے پہلے وہاں سے منی کے لئے چل پڑے حدیث یہ ہے۔ سمعت عمر بن میمون يقول شهدت عمر صلى بــجـمـع الصبح ثم وقف فقال ان المشركين كانوا لا يفيضون حتى تطلع الشمس ويقولون اشرق ثبير وان
صل الله
النبي وخالفهم ثم افاض قبل ان تطلع الشمس (بخاری شریف ، باب متی یدفع من جمع ص ۲۲۸ نمبر ۱۶۸۴) اس الا الله . ، متی نمبر۱۲۸۴) حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ سورج طلوع ہونے سے پہلے مزدلفہ سے منی کے لئے روانہ ہو۔ (۲) اس حدیث میں بھی ہے۔ قال دخلنا
على جابر بن عبد الله ... ثم ركب القصواء حتى اتى المشعر الحرام فاستقبل القبلة فدعاه وكبره وهلله
ووحده فلم يزل واقفا حتى اسفر جدا فدفع قبل ان تطلع الشمس (مسلم شریف، باب حجتہ النبی می ص ۵۱۵ ، نمبر ۲۹۵۰/۱۲۱۸ ابوداؤد شریف ، باب صفته حجۃ النبی ، ص ۲۷۸، نمبر ۱۹۰۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ طلوع آفتاب سے پہلے آپ مزدلفہ سے چلے۔
Translation (1351): Then when it becomes very bright, the Imam and the people should depart before sunrise and come to Mina. Section on the composition of the actions of Hajj. Thamarat al-Najah Vol. 2. This standing place as completed for our master Muhammad (peace be upon him). (1351) When it becomes very bright, the Imam and the people depart before sunrise and come to Mina and stay there. (1352) Then he comes to Jamrat al-Aqabah and stones it from the bottom. Explanation: When it becomes very bright, the Imam and people should leave Muzdalifah for Mina before sunrise. Reason: (1) The polytheists used to depart from Muzdalifah after sunrise. But the Prophet (peace be upon him) opposed them and left before sunrise for Mina. This is the hadith: I heard 'Umar ibn Maymun say: I witnessed 'Umar perform the Fajr prayer at Muzdalifah, then he stood and said: The polytheists used not to depart until the sun rose, and they would say: 'Shine, Thabir!' But the Prophet (peace be upon him) opposed them and departed before the sun rose. (Bukhari, Bab mata yadfa' min Jam', p. 228, no. 1684) From this hadith it is learned that one should leave Muzdalifah for Mina before sunrise. (2) And in this hadith also: We entered upon Jabir ibn 'Abd Allah... then he rode al-Qaswa' until he came to al-Mash'ar al-Haram, faced the qiblah, made supplication, said Allahu Akbar, La ilaha illa Allah, and affirmed His oneness. He continued standing until it became very bright, then he departed before the sun rose. (Muslim, Bab hujjat al-nabi, p. 515, no. 2950/1218; Abu Dawud, Bab sifat hujjat al-nabi, p. 278, no. 1905) This hadith states that the Prophet left Muzdalifah before sunrise.
Source pages p. 376

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the timing of departure from Muzdalifah on the morning of the 10th of Dhul Hijjah. The author states that after it becomes very bright (isfar), the Imam and the people should depart before sunrise. The proof is twofold: first, the practice of 'Umar ibn al-Khattab who, based on the Prophet's Sunnah, departed before sunrise in opposition to the polytheists who waited until sunrise. Second, the hadith of Jabir explicitly states that the Prophet rode to al-Mash'ar al-Haram, stood until isfar, then departed before sunrise. This establishes that the recommended time (sunnah) is to leave after the Fajr prayer and after it becomes bright, but crucially before sunrise. The Hanafi school considers this departure as a necessary (wajib) act, and delaying until sunrise is makruh.

Key Terms
اسفار جدا (isfar jiddan): The time when daylight becomes very bright and widespread, after Fajr prayer.
فيض (fayd / ifada): Departure from Muzdalifah to Mina.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling regarding the time of departure from Muzdalifah according to the Hanafi school based on the hadith cited?
A) After sunrise
B) At sunrise
C) Before sunrise after it becomes bright
D) Anytime after Fajr

Key Takeaway
Departure from Muzdalifah to Mina must occur after Fajr prayer and before sunrise, as a necessary act (wajib) in the Hanafi school, based on the Prophet's practice.

Stoning of Jamrat al-Aqabah on the Day of Sacrifice
Ruling with proof on stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah and identify the supporting evidence from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
Stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah with seven small pebbles from the valley bottom is wajib.

This lesson presents the Hanafi ruling on the stoning of Jamrat al-Aqabah, the only jamrah pelted on the Day of Sacrifice. We will examine the prescribed method, the number and size of pebbles, and the preferred location. The proof is drawn from authentic hadiths that describe the Prophet's practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being described and its legal classification in the Hanafi school. Is it fard, wajib, sunnah, etc.?
2
Locate the dalil
Find the hadiths cited as evidence. Note their sources and authenticity (thubut, dalala).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how each hadith proves the ruling—what specific words or actions indicate the method (number of pebbles, size, location, takbir).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Check if other schools differ on any detail. The source indicates no significant ikhtilaf on the core obligation.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi position
Summarize the mufta bihi position: stoning with seven small pebbles from the bottom of the valley, saying takbir with each.

ترجمه : (۱۳۵۲) پھر جمرہ عقبہ کے پاس آکر بطن وادی سے سات ٹھیکری کی کنکری جیسی کنکر سے رمی کریں۔ تشریح : تین جمرات ہیں۔ [1] جمرہ اولی ، [۲] جمرہ وسطی اور [۳] جمرہ عقبہ، اور اس وقت تینوں جگہ سیمنٹ کے کھمبے کھڑے ہیں۔ دسویں ذی الحجہ کو صرف جمرہ عقبہ کی رمی کرے گا اور بطن وادی سے سات کنکری مارے گا۔ جس طرح ٹھیکرے پھینکتے ہیں اس طرح پھینک کر مارے۔

صلى الله وجه : (۱) اس حدیث میں ہے . اخبر نا سلیمان ابن عمر بن الاحوص عن امه قالت رأيت رسول الله الله يرمى الجمرة من بطن الوادى و هو راكب يكبر مع كل حصاة ، ورجل من خلفه يستره فسألت عن الرجل ؟ فقالوا الفضل بن العباس ، و ازدحم الناس فقال النبى الله يا أيها الناس ! لا يقتل بعضكم بعضا و اذا رميتــم الــجــمـــة فارموا بمثل حصى الخذف (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب فی رمی الجمارص ۲۸۷ نمبر ۱۹۶۶ رابن ماجہ شریف، باب قد رصی الرمی ، ص ۴۳۹، نمبر ۳۰۲۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ بطن وادی سے جمرہ عقبہ کی رمی کرے، اور یہ بھی ہے کہ ٹھیکرے کی طرح چھوٹی چھوٹی کنکری لے کر مارے، اور بہت بھیٹر نہ کرے (۲) اس حدیث میں بھی ہے کہ بطن وادی سے اس دن صرف جمرہ عقبہ کی رمی کرے۔ قال دخلنا على جابر بن عبد الله ... ثم سلك الطريق الوسطى التي تخرج على الجمرة الكبرى حتى اتى الجمرة التي عند الشجرة فرماها بسبع حصيات يكبر مع كل حصاة منها مثل حصى
Translation (1352): Then he comes to Jamrat al-Aqabah and stones it from the bottom of the valley with seven pebbles like those used for throwing pottery pieces. Explanation: There are three jamarat: [1] Jamrat al-Ula, [2] Jamrat al-Wusta, [3] Jamrat al-Aqabah. At this time, concrete pillars stand at all three places. On the tenth of Dhul Hijjah, he will only stone Jamrat al-Aqabah, and from the bottom of the valley he will throw seven pebbles. He should throw them like one throws pottery pieces. Reason: (1) In this hadith: Sulayman ibn 'Umar ibn al-Ahwas informed us from his mother who said: I saw the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) stoning the jamrah from the bottom of the valley while riding, saying takbir with every pebble. A man behind him was covering him. I asked about the man, and they said: Al-Fadl ibn al-'Abbas. The people crowded, so the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'O people! Do not kill one another. When you stone the jamrah, stone with pebbles like those used for throwing (khadhf).' (Abu Dawud, Bab fi ramy al-jimar, p. 287, no. 1966; Ibn Majah, Bab qadr al-ramy, p. 439, no. 3028) From this hadith it is learned that he should stone Jamrat al-Aqabah from the bottom of the valley, and also that he should take small pebbles like pottery pieces, and not make them too big. (2) In this hadith also that he should only stone Jamrat al-Aqabah from the bottom of the valley on that day. He said: We entered upon Jabir ibn 'Abd Allah... then he took the middle path that leads to the big jamrah until he came to the jamrah that is by the tree, and he stoned it with seven pebbles, saying takbir with every pebble, each like pebbles...
Source pages p. 377

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the stoning of Jamrat al-Aqabah on the Day of Sacrifice (10th Dhul Hijjah). The author states that the pilgrim should come to Jamrat al-Aqabah and stone it from the bottom of the valley (batn al-wadi) with seven small pebbles. The explanation clarifies that there are three jamarat, but on this day only the Jamrat al-Aqabah is stoned. The proof is from two hadiths: the first from the mother of Sulayman ibn 'Umar ibn al-Ahwas, describing the Prophet stoning from the bottom of the valley while riding, saying takbir with each pebble, and instructing to use pebbles like those used for khadhf (small pebbles thrown between the fingers). The second hadith of Jabir confirms the practice of stoning with seven pebbles while saying takbir. The Hanafi school holds that stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah on this day is wajib, and the pebbles should be small (like chickpeas or small beans). Stoning from the bottom of the valley is recommended.

Key Terms
جمرة العقبة (Jamrat al-Aqabah): The largest jamrah, located near Mina, stoned on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah.
بطن الوادي (batn al-wadi): The bottom or inner part of the valley, specifically the area where the jamrah is stoned.
حصى الخذف (hasa al-khadhf): Small pebbles that can be thrown between two fingers, like those used for catapulting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah on the Day of Sacrifice is a wajib act in Hajj, performed with seven small pebbles from the bottom of the valley, following the practice of the Prophet.

Hajj — Pilgrimage

Taking Pebbles for Rami: Mustahabb from Muzdalifah, Makruh from Near Jamrah
Ruling on where to obtain pebbles for stoning Jamrah al-Aqabah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on where to take pebbles for rami al-Jamrah al-Aqabah and identify the three key proofs that support it.

Core Idea
Taking pebbles from Muzdalifah is sunnah; from near the jamrah is makruh tanzihi, but rami remains valid.

This lesson examines a specific sunnah of Hajj — the preferred method of obtaining pebbles for stoning Jamrah al-Aqabah. The Hanafi school distinguishes between recommended and disliked sources based on prophetic practice and a subtle hadith about accepted versus rejected pebbles. Understanding this ruling helps a pilgrim follow the complete sunna of the Prophet (peace be upon him) without unnecessary hardship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the act is taking pebbles for rami. The ruling is that it is mustahabb (recommended) to take from Muzdalifah or the path, and makruh (disliked) to take from the jamrah site itself.
This ruling applies specifically to Jamrah al-Aqabah, the largest jamrah.
2
Locate the dalil
Three proofs are cited: (1) The Prophet's command to pick pebbles from the path (Ibn Majah). (2) Ibn 'Umar's practice of taking pebbles from Muzdalifah (Bayhaqi). (3) The hadith that accepted pebbles are raised, implying remaining pebbles are rejected (Darqutni).
All three are ahadith with zanni thubut and dalala.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's imperative 'Pick up pebbles for me' indicates recommendation, especially as he was on the path. Ibn 'Umar's action shows explicit preference for Muzdalifah. The third hadith implies that pebbles at the jamrah site are rejected, thus disliked for use.
The combination of action and explicit saying strengthens the Hanafi position.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other madhahib (e.g. Shafi'i) consider it permissible to take pebbles from any location without distinction. They may not see the third hadith as prohibiting or even disliking.
The disagreement is over the strength of the evidence for the disliked ruling.
5
Evaluate the thamarah
The practical difference: a Hanafi pilgrim will prefer to collect pebbles from Muzdalifah or the path, while a non-Hanafi may collect from anywhere. If one collects from the jamrah site, the rami is still valid but the sunna is missed.
The rami is not invalidated by using such pebbles.

فصل تركيب افعال الحج الوادي بسبع حصيات مثل حصى الخذف(۱۳۵۳) ويستحب اخذ الجمار من المزدلفة او من الطريق ويكره من الذى عند الجمرة الخذف رمى من بطن الوادى ثم انصرف الى المنحر ( مسلم شریف ، باب حجتہ النبی ص ۵۱۵، نمبر ۲۹۵۰/۱۲۱۸ را بو صا الله داؤد شریف ، باب صفہ حجۃ النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم ، ص ۲۷۸، نمبر ۱۹۰۵) اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ بطن وادی سے جمرہ عقبہ پر سات کنکریاں مارے لغت العقبة : آخری، پیچھے، چونکہ یہ آخری جمرہ ہے اور دو جمروں کے پیچھے ہے اس لئے اس کو جمرہ عقبہ، کہتے ہیں۔ رمی بیرمی کنکری پھینکنا۔ بطن وادی : جمرہ عقبہ کے پاس جگہ کا نام ہے۔ حصیات: حصاۃ کی جمع ہے کنکری۔ الخذف : خذف کا معنی ہے اتنی چھوٹی کنکری ہو کہ دو انگلیوں سے پھینکی جاسکے ٹھیکرا پھینکنا، چھوٹی کنکری۔ ترجمه : (۱۳۵۳) اور کنکری کا مزدلفہ یا ر استے سے لینا مستحب ہے، اور جمرہ کے پاس سے لینا مکروہ ہے۔ تشریح : مزدلفہ کے راستے سے کنکری لینا مستحب ہے، اور جمرات کے پاس سے لینا مکروہ ہے، کیونکہ یہ جمرات کے اوپر ماری ہوئی کنکریاں ہیں۔ تاہم ليكر مارلی تو تورمی ادا ہو جائے گی۔ وجه : (۱) اس حدیث میں اشارہ ہے کہ آپ نے مزدلفہ کے راستے سے کنکری لی. عن ابن عباس قال قال رسول الله علم غداة العقبة و هو على ناقته : (( القط لى حصى (( فلقطت له سبع حصيات من حصى ا الخذف . (ابن ما جہ شریف ، باب قد رصی الرمی ،ص ۲۳۹، نمبر ۳۰۲۹) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ آپ جمرہ عقبہ کی صبح کو اونٹنی پر تھے اور کنکری چننے کے لئے فرمایا ، جس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ مزدلفہ کے راستے سے کنکری لی۔ (۲) اس قول صحابی میں ہے کہ مزدلفہ سے کنکری لی . عـــن ابن عمر انه كان يأخذ الحصى من جمع كراهية أن ينزل - ( سنن بیہقی ، باب أخذ الحصى لرمی جمرة العقبة وكيفيته ذالك، ج خامس ، ص ۲۰۹، نمبر ۹۵۴۴) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ مزدلفہ ہی سے کنکری لے لے۔ (۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ جو کنکری قبول ہوتی ہے وہ اٹھالی جاتی ہے اور جو قبول نہیں ہوتی وہ پڑی رہتی ہے، اس لئے وہاں پڑی ہوئی کنکریاں جو مردود ہو چکی ہیں ان سے رمی کرنا مکروہ ہے۔ عن ابی سعید قال قلنا یا رسول الله هذه الجمار التي يرمى بها كل عام فتحتسب أنها تنقص ؟ فقال انه ما تقبل منها رفع و لو لا ذالك لرأيتها أمثال الجبال (دارقطنی ، باب کتاب الحج ، ج ثانی ص ۲۶۳ نمبر ۲۷۶۳/مستدرک للحاکم ، باب کتاب المناسک ج اول ص ۶۵۰ نمبر ۱۷۵۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ جوکنکری مقبول ہوئی وہ اٹھا لی جاتی ہے اس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ جو رہ گئی وہ مردود ہے اس لئے اس کنگری کو استعمال نہ کرے۔
Chapter: Composition of Hajj Actions. The valley with seven pebbles like pebbles of al-khadhf (1353). And it is mustahabb to take pebbles from Muzdalifah or from the path, and it is makruh to take from the one at the jamrah. Al-khadhf: throwing from the bottom of the valley, then he turned to the slaughtering place (Muslim, Abu Dawud). From this it is understood that he threw seven pebbles at Jamrah al-Aqabah from the bottom of the valley. Lexicon: al-Aqabah: last, behind; because it is the last jamrah and behind two jamrahs, it is called Jamrah al-Aqabah. Ramy: throwing stones. Batan al-Wadi: the place near Jamrah al-Aqabah. Hasyat: plural of hasah, pebbles. Al-Khadhf: pebbles small enough to be thrown between two fingers, small stones. Translation (1353): And taking pebbles from Muzdalifah or from the path is mustahabb, and taking from near the jamrah is makruh. Explanation: Taking pebbles from the path of Muzdalifah is mustahabb, and taking from near the jamrahs is makruh because they are pebbles that have been thrown at the jamrahs. However, if one takes and throws, the rami is valid. Evidence (1): This hadith indicates that the Prophet took pebbles from the path of Muzdalifah. From Ibn ‘Abbas: The Messenger of Allah, on the morning of the ‘Aqabah while on his she-camel, said: 'Pick up pebbles for me.' So I picked up seven pebbles from pebbles of al-khadhf. (Ibn Majah) In this hadith is that the Prophet was on his camel on the morning of Jamrah al-Aqabah and said to pick up pebbles, meaning he took them from the path of Muzdalifah. (2) In this saying of a Companion: He used to take pebbles from Muzdalifah. From Ibn ‘Umar: He used to take pebbles from Jam‘ (Muzdalifah) disliking to descend. (Bayhaqi) This effect shows that he should take pebbles from Muzdalifah itself. (3) In this hadith: The pebbles that are accepted are taken away, and those not accepted remain. Therefore, using pebbles lying there that are rejected for rami is makruh. From Abu Sa‘id: We said, O Messenger of Allah, these pebbles thrown every year, are they considered to decrease? He said: 'What is accepted is raised; if not, you would see them like mountains.' (Darqutni, Hakim) This hadith means the accepted pebbles are taken away, so the remaining are rejected; thus one should not use those pebbles.
Source pages p. 378

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof in the Hanafi school regarding obtaining pebbles for rami al-Jamarah al-Aqabah. The matn states that it is mustahabb (recommended) to take pebbles from Muzdalifah or from the path en route, and makruh (disliked) to take them from the area near the jamrah itself. The author explains that the pebbles near the jamrah are those that were thrown and rejected, hence disliked. The evidence includes three proofs: a hadith of Ibn ‘Abbas showing the Prophet took pebbles from the path, the practice of Ibn ‘Umar taking from Muzdalifah, and a hadith indicating accepted pebbles are raised, so remaining ones are rejected. The commentary emphasizes that even if one uses pebbles from a disliked source, the rami is still valid (the obligation is fulfilled) but the sunna is not followed. The Hanafi position is that this is a sunna act; the ruling is not fard but mustahabb for the method of obtaining pebbles.

Key Terms
مستحب (mustahabb): Act recommended but not obligatory; omission is not sinful but is contrary to the better practice.
مکروہ (makruh): Disliked act; not sinful but against the preferable practice.
خذف (khadhf): Small pebbles that can be thrown between two fingers, like small stones.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
From where is it mustahabb to take pebbles for rami al-Jamrah al-Aqabah?
A) From the area around the jamrah itself
B) From Muzdalifah or the path en route
C) From any random place in Mina
D) Only from the valley of Mina

Key Takeaway
It is mustahabb to take pebbles for rami from Muzdalifah or the path, and makruh tanzihi to take them from the jamrah site, but the rami remains valid in either case.

Throwing from Above Jamrah al-Aqabah: Makruh but Valid
Ruling with proof on throwing location for Jamrah al-Aqabah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on throwing from above Jamrah al-Aqabah, identify the sunnah location, and apply the principle of necessity to validate the act.

Core Idea
Throwing from above Jamrah al-Aqabah is valid but disliked; under necessity it becomes permissible.

The Hanafi school maintains that the sunnah is to throw from the valley floor (batan al-wadi), as the Prophet (peace be upon him) did. However, the matn in this passage states that throwing from above the Jamrah al-Aqabah is makruh because it causes harm to people. Yet, it is still valid, and under conditions of extreme crowding, it becomes permissible. This lesson unpacks the ruling, the reasoning behind the dislike, and the evidentiary basis from the action of Umar ibn al-Khattab, which allows for flexibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Default Ruling
The act is throwing pebbles at Jamrah al-Aqabah from above (as opposed to from the valley floor). The ruling from the matn is that it is makruh (disliked).
Makruh here is tanzihi – disliked but not sinful; the act remains valid.
2
Locate the Sunnah Practice
The sunnah is to throw from the valley floor (batan al-wadi), as the Prophet did. This is understood from the hadith reference in the passage.
The passage cites Muslim and Abu Dawud referring to the Prophet's practice.
3
Understand the Reason for Dislike
The dislike is because throwing from above harms other pilgrims below, either through hitting them or creating danger.
The reason (illah) is causing harm – i.e., the principle of la darar wa la dirar.
4
Examine the Dalil for Permissibility
The text cites the action of Umar ibn al-Khattab, who threw from above. This is a qawl sahabi and indicates permissibility, as a companion would not perform a forbidden act.
This dalil is zanni in thubut and dalala (narration and meaning), but it is used to override the general dislike when necessary.
5
Apply the Principle of Necessity
The commentary states that if due to crowding or other reasons one throws from above, it is still valid. This uses istihsan to move from makruh to permissible under necessity.
The mufta bihi opinion: throwing from above is permissible when needed; otherwise, the sunnah is from the valley.

Commentary
This passage provides a Hanafi ruling on the location of throwing for Jamrah al-Aqabah. The matn states it is makruh (disliked) to throw from above the jamrah because it causes harm to people. The sunnah is to throw from the valley floor (batan al-wadi) as the Prophet did. The evidence cited is the action of ‘Umar ibn al-Khattab who threw from above, indicating permissibility. The commentary emphasizes that while the sunnah is from the valley, the validity of the act is not compromised by location. This aligns with the Hanafi principle of making the act easy while maintaining the recommended form.

مکروہ (makruh): In this context, makruh tanzihi: disliked but not sinful; the act is valid.

Picking and Washing Pebbles for Rami
Ruling on picking and washing pebbles for rami

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on obtaining pebbles for rami, distinguish between sunnah and obligatory actions, and apply the evidence from the hadith.

Core Idea
Pebbles for rami should be picked, not broken; washing is sunnah, not required.

When performing rami in Hajj, the pilgrim needs pebbles. The Hanafi school teaches that pebbles should be collected naturally, not manufactured by breaking stones. Washing them is recommended to ensure purity, but not obligatory. This lesson examines the ruling, the evidence from the Prophet's practice, and the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is obtaining pebbles for rami. Rulings: picking is sunnah, breaking is makruh, washing is sunnah muakkadah.
The matn uses imperative forms for picking and washing, but the commentator clarifies they are not obligatory.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith from Ibn Abbas: the Prophet said 'Pick up pebbles for me' (القِط لي حصى).
This is a hadith ahad, so it yields zanni evidence.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'qat' indicates collection from the ground, not manufacturing by breaking stones. This supports the sunnah method.
Hanafi usul: al-amr yufidu al-nadb (command indicates recommendation) unless there is evidence for wujub.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) require purity as a condition; Hanafi considers washing sunnah and allows impure pebbles (makruh).
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf based on different usul principles.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The relied-upon position is to pick and wash, but not washing does not invalidate. The mufta bihi is the sunnah method.
Breaking stones is makruh tanzih; washing is mustahabb.

(1355) And he picks them up by picking, and does not break a stone into pebbles, and washes them to be certain of their purity, because by them an act of worship is performed. And if he throws with an impure (pebble), it suffices him and is makruh. Translation (1355): And he should pick up the pebbles from anywhere, and should not break stones for this, and should wash them so that he is certain of their purity because an act of worship is performed with them. If he throws with an impure pebble, it is permissible but it is makruh. Explanation: Breaking stones to make pebbles is not good; therefore he should pick pebbles from anywhere, and wash them to be certain they are pure because an act of worship is performed with them. However, if he does not wash, it is still permissible because pebbles on the ground are considered pure. But if he is certain that the pebbles are impure, and still throws with them, it is valid but makruh. Evidence (1): This hadith indicates that pebbles should be picked, not broken. Source pages p. 379

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi ruling on the method of obtaining pebbles for rami. The matn instructs that one should pick up pebbles (i.e., collect them from the ground), not break stones to make them, and wash them to ensure they are ritually pure (tahir) because rami is an act of worship (qurbah). However, the ruling on washing is mustahabb, not mandatory; if one does not wash, the pebbles are considered pure by default unless impurity is known. Even if one uses a known impure pebble, the rami is valid (ajza'a) but makruh. The evidence is the hadith where the Prophet said 'pick up pebbles for me' using the word 'qat' (pick), which implies collection, not breaking. The Hanafi school emphasizes that the pebbles should be naturally occurring small stones, not manufactured by breaking larger stones. This follows the sunnah of the Prophet.

نجس (najis): Ritually impure (e.g., touched by najasah).

When to Stop Talbiyah: With the First Pebble at Jamrah al-Aqabah
Ruling on the time to discontinue the talbiyah during rami

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when the talbiyah ends during the rami of Jamrah al-Aqabah and cite the evidence from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
The talbiyah ends with the first pebble thrown at Jamrah al-Aqabah; thereafter, glorify Allah with takbir.

In the rites of Hajj, the talbiyah is a declaration of presence and devotion to Allah. However, when the pilgrim begins the symbolic stoning of the devil, the sunnah is to cease the talbiyah with the first stone and instead recite the takbir. This lesson examines the precise timing and the evidence from the Prophet's practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is cutting the talbiyah during rami. The ruling is sunnah muakkadah: it is recommended to stop with the first pebble.
The matn states 'with the first pebble he throws'.
2
Locate the dalil
Two hadiths from Sahih Bukhari are cited. Find the specific reports from Ibn Abbas and al-Fadl ibn Abbas.
Bukhari, Hadith 1685.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith 'until he threw Jamrah al-Aqabah' indicates cessation at that moment. The second hadith 'when he threw it, he cut' specifies the first pebble.
The word 'rami' includes the first pebble.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school holds that talbiyah ends when one begins the stoning process, not necessarily with the first pebble.
Both schools agree that talbiyah ends at Jamrah al-Aqabah.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school relies on the explicit wording of al-Fadl's hadith, making the first pebble the point of cessation.
This is the mufta bihi position.

Source Text

(1356) And he cuts the talbiyah with the first pebble he throws. Translation (1356): And he should end the talbiyah with the first pebble. Explanation: The meaning of talbiyah is 'I am present'. Now, at the place of the devil, saying 'I am present' would be contradictory. Therefore, when striking the devil, he should end the talbiyah and proclaim Allah's greatness and say takbir. Evidence: (1) In a hadith: From Ibn ‘Abbas that the Prophet continued talbiyah until he threw Jamrah al-Aqabah. (Bukhari) This hadith indicates that he recited talbiyah until Jamrah al-Aqabah, not after. (2) In another hadith: Al-Fadl ibn ‘Abbas said: I was riding behind the Prophet, and I kept hearing him say talbiyah until he threw Jamrah al-Aqabah. When he threw it, he cut (the talbiyah).
Source pages p. 379

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi ruling on the time to terminate the talbiyah during the rites of Hajj. The matn states that one should stop reciting talbiyah with the first pebble thrown at Jamrah al-Aqabah. The explanation gives a rationale: talbiyah is a declaration of presence for the rites of Allah, but at the jamrah (symbolic of Satan), the appropriate response is to glorify Allah (takbir) and supplicate, not to declare labbayk. The evidence includes two hadiths from Bukhari showing that the Prophet continued talbiyah until he threw Jamrah al-Aqabah, and then stopped. The second hadith specifies that he stopped at the first pebble. This is the Hanafi position: talbiyah ends with the commencement of rami at Jamrah al-Aqabah. One then says Allahu Akbar with each throw.

Key Terms
تلبیہ (talbiyah): Recitation of 'Labbayk Allahumma labbayk...' as a declaration of assuming ihram and presence for Hajj.

Rulings on Picking and Washing Pebbles for Stoning (Rami)
Ruling on selecting and purifying pebbles for rami

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on picking, not breaking, and washing pebbles for rami, and apply the evidence from the hadith of Ibn Abbas.

Core Idea
Pebbles for stoning must be picked, not broken; washing is recommended but not required for validity.

This passage addresses three actions related to preparing pebbles for the stoning ritual during Hajj: picking them from the ground, avoiding breaking stones, and washing them. The ruling distinguishes between sunnah practices and conditions of validity, and provides a hadith as evidence. We will work through the text to understand the hierarchy of these rulings and their practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three actions and their rulings
From the text, list the three actions concerning pebbles: picking, not breaking, and washing. Determine the hukm (legal classification) of each: sunnah, sunnah, and mustahabb respectively.
Picking and not breaking are sunnah of the Prophet; washing is recommended to ensure purity but not obligatory.
2
Analyze the effect of impurity
Examine what happens if one uses pebbles that are known to be impure. According to the text, the rami is valid but disliked (makruh). Understand the basis: the default ruling of earth is purity, but certainty of impurity triggers dislike.
Contrast with schools that require purity for validity.
3
Locate and examine the proof (dalil)
The text cites the hadith where the Prophet asked Ibn Abbas to pick pebbles for him. Identify the operative phrase 'iltiqat' and explain how it supports the ruling against breaking stones.
The command indicates the recommended action (amr), but it is not imperative for obligation.
4
Apply the ruling to a concrete scenario
Consider a pilgrim who breaks large stones into small pieces for stoning because he cannot find suitable pebbles. Evaluate this action using the text's rulings and identify the correct practice.
Breaking stones is discouraged; the pilgrim should search for naturally small pebbles.

ترجمه : (۱۳۵۵) اور ان کنکریوں کو کہیں سے اٹھالے، اور اس کے لئے پتھر نہ توڑے، اور اس کو دھولے تا کہ طہارت کا یقین ہو جائے اس لئے کہ اس سے ایک عبادت ادا کی جاتی ہے۔ اگر نا پاک کنکر سے رمی کی تو جائز ہے مگر مکروہ ہوگی۔ تشریح : پھر کوتو ڑ کر نگریاں بنانا اچھا نہیں ہے اس لئے کنکریاں کہیں سے چنے، اور انکو دھولے تا کہ یقین ہو جائے کہ یہ پاک ہیں کیونکہ ان سے ایک عبادت ادا کی جارہی ہے، لیکن اگر نہ دھوئے تب بھی جائز ہے، کیونکہ زمین کی کنکریاں پاک ہی شمار کی جاتی ہیں۔ لیکن اگر یقین ہو کہ یہ کنکریاں ناپاک ہیں پھر بھی ان سے رمی کر لی تو ادا ہو جائے گی ، البتہ مکروہ ہے۔ وجه : (۱) اس حدیث میں اشارہ ہے کہ کنکریاں چنا چاہئے پتھر سے نہیں تو ڑنا چاہئے. عن ابن عباس قال قال رسول الله : ( القط لي حصى ) فلقطت له سبع حصيات من حصى الخذف . ( ابن ماجہ شریف ، باب قدر هی الرمی ، ص ۱۴۳۹، نمبر ۳۰۲۹) اس حدیث میں ہے القط لي حصی: کہ میرے لئے کنکریاں چنو ، جس سے پتہ چلا کہ کنکریاں چنے پتھر سے نہ توڑے۔
He picks them up, does not break a stone into pebbles, washes them to be certain of their purity, because an act of worship is performed with them. If he throws with impure [pebbles], it suffices but is disliked. Translation: (1355) And he picks up these pebbles from somewhere, and does not break stones for them, and washes them so that certainty of purity is achieved, because an act of worship is performed with them. If he throws with impure pebbles, it is allowed but disliked. Explanation: Breaking stones to make pebbles is not good; therefore he should pick pebbles from somewhere and wash them to be sure they are pure, because an act of worship is being performed with them. But if he does not wash, it is still allowed, because the earth's pebbles are considered pure. However, if he is certain the pebbles are impure and still throws with them, it suffices but is disliked. Evidence: (1) This hadith indicates that pebbles should be picked, not broken from stones. From Ibn Abbas: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Pick pebbles for me.' So I picked for him seven pebbles from the pebbles of al-khadhf (small pebbles). (Ibn Majah, chapter on the size of pebbles for stoning, p. 1439, no. 3029) In this hadith: 'Pick pebbles for me'—showing that pebbles should be picked, not broken from stones.
Source pages p. 379

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on three aspects of pebble preparation for rami: picking, not breaking, and washing. The author states that pebbles must be picked from the ground, not artificially broken from large stones, because the prophetic example shows picking (iltiqat). The ruling to wash pebbles is recommended to ensure certainty of purity, since they are used for an act of worship. However, if one does not wash, it is still valid because the default ruling of earth is purity. If one throws with an impure pebble knowingly, the act of stoning is valid but makruh (disliked) because impurity contradicts reverence. The proof is a hadith where the Prophet asked Ibn Abbas to pick pebbles for him, which indicates the action of picking rather than breaking.

Key Terms
يلتقط (yaltiqitu): To pick up from the ground, as opposed to breaking or cutting.
جمار (jimar): Pebbles used for stoning (plural of jamrah).
رجس / نجس (najis): Impure; in this context, impure pebbles that are known to be najis.

Cutting Talbiyah with the First Pebble
Timing to end the talbiyah at Jamrat al-Aqaba

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when to cut the talbiyah during hajj and identify the hadith evidence supporting it.

Core Idea
Talbiyah ends with the first pebble at Jamrat al-Aqaba, not after.

This lesson explains the precise moment to cut the talbiyah during the hajj stoning ritual. The Hanafi school teaches that the pilgrim should stop saying 'Labbayk' as soon as the first pebble is thrown at the large jamrah. This timing is based on the direct practice of the Prophet ﷺ, as reported by his companion Fadl ibn Abbas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the act under discussion is cutting the talbiyah during stoning at Jamrat al-Aqaba. The ruling is sunnah muakkadah (emphasized recommendation), not fard or wajib.
The ruling is derived from the Prophet's practice.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The primary proof is the hadith of Fadl ibn Abbas: 'I was riding behind the Prophet and I kept hearing him say talbiyah until he stoned Jamrat al-Aqaba. When he stoned it, he cut the talbiyah.' This is recorded in Bukhari and Ibn Majah.
The hadith is ahad (single-narrator), thus zanni al-thubut, but sufficient for a sunnah ruling.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah (legal implication)
The phrase 'until he stoned Jamrat al-Aqaba' indicates continuation until the first throw; 'when he stoned it, he cut the talbiyah' explicitly shows the exact point of cutting.
The word 'flamma' (when) indicates immediate cessation.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) hold that talbiyah continues until the end of the stoning of all three jamarat or until sunset. The Hanafi position differs because of the explicit hadith.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; each school has its evidence.
5
Determine the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is to cut the talbiyah with the first pebble thrown at Jamrat al-Aqaba. This is the established zahir al-riwayah view.
After the first pebble, one should say takbir instead.

Source Text

ويقطع التلبية مع اول حصاة يرميها. 
ترجمه : (۱۳۵۶) اور تلبیہ کو پہلی کنکری کے ساتھ ختم کر دے۔ تشریح : تلبیہ کا مطلب ہے کہ میں حاضر ہوں۔ اب شیطان کے پاس کہے کہ میں حاضر ہوں تو یہ الٹی بات ہو جائے گی ۔ اس لئے شیطان کو مارتے وقت تلبیہ ختم کر کے اللہ کی بڑائی بیان کرے اور تکبیر کہے۔ وجه: (۱) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابن عباس ان النبي أردف الفضل فاخبر الفضل انه لم يزل يلبى حتى رمي الجمرة العقبة - ( بخاری شریف، باب التلبية والتكبير غداة الخر حتى يرمى الجمرة العقب ص ۲۲۸ نمبر ۱۶۸۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ جمرہ عقبہ تک تلبیہ پڑھا اس کے بعد نہیں۔ (۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ جمرہ عقبہ کی پہلی کنگری پر تلبیہ ختم کر دیا۔ قال الفضل بن عباس كنت ردف النبى فما زالت أسمعه يلبي حتى رمى جمرة العقبة فلما رما ها قطع التلبية . And he cuts the talbiyah with the first pebble he throws. Translation: (1356) And he ends the talbiyah with the first pebble. Explanation: Talbiyah means 'I am present.' Now saying 'I am present' at the place of the devil is contradictory. Therefore, at the time of stoning the devil, he should end the talbiyah and glorify Allah by saying takbir. Evidence: (1) Hadith: From Ibn Abbas that the Prophet made Fadl ride behind him, and Fadl informed that he continued saying talbiyah until he stoned Jamrat al-Aqaba. (Bukhari, chapter on talbiyah and takbir on the morning of sacrifice until stoning Jamrat al-Aqaba, p. 228, no. 1685) This hadith states that he said talbiyah until Jamrat al-Aqaba, not after. (2) Another hadith: Fadl ibn Abbas said: 'I was riding behind the Prophet, and I kept hearing him say talbiyah until he stoned Jamrat al-Aqaba. When he stoned it, he cut the talbiyah.' (Ibn Majah, chapter on when the pilgrim cuts talbiyah, p. 440, no. 3040) This hadith shows that he will say talbiyah until Jamrat al-Aqaba, and as soon as he throws the first pebble, he cuts the talbiyah.
Source pages p. 379

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the timing of cutting the talbiyah. The Hanafi position is that the talbiyah ends with the first pebble thrown at Jamrat al-Aqaba. The reasoning given is that it is inappropriate to say 'I am present' while stoning the devil. Instead, one should glorify Allah by saying takbir. The proofs provided are two hadiths: one from Bukhari showing the Prophet continued talbiyah until he stoned al-Aqaba, and another from Ibn Majah specifying that he cut the talbiyah precisely when he stoned it (first pebble). Thus, the reliable position is to stop talbiyah at the moment of the first throw.

Key Terms
التلبية (al-talbiyah): The phrase 'Labbayk Allahumma labbayk' recited by pilgrims, expressing readiness to serve Allah.
جمرة العقبة (jamrat al-aqabah): The large stone pillar (jamrah) at Mina, representing the devil, stoned on the 10th of Dhul-Hijjah.

Key Takeaway

Method of Rami: Holding Pebble with Thumb and Index Finger
Preferred method of gripping the pebble for stoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the preferred Hanafi method for holding the pebble during rami, cite the supporting hadith, and distinguish between the sunnah and obligatory aspects of the act.

Core Idea
The sunnah is to hold the pebble with thumb and index finger tips, not the full fist.

The method of stoning (rami) has a recommended technique that goes beyond mere validity. While any throw that hits the jamrah suffices, the Hanafi school teaches a specific grip that embodies ease and symbolic humiliation of Satan. This lesson examines that preferred method, its proof, and its status as sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its category
The passage gives the preferred method and calls it the most correct view (asahh). Determine the hukm level (sunnah muakkadah) and why it is not fard/wajib.
The ruling is about recommended practice, not validity.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith from Abu Dawud describes the Prophet (SAW) with a pebble between his fingers. Note the transmission and its zanni status.
The hadith is ahad, giving zanni thubut.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
How does 'between his fingers' specifically indicate the thumb and index finger? The commentary explains that 'fingers' here implies the tips used in gripping.
The context of throwing small pebbles favors the grip of thumb and index.
4
Understand the rationale
The method is favored because it is easier and more humiliating to the devil. This shows the legal reasoning (ta'lil) behind the sunnah.
Ease and spiritual symbolism reinforce the recommendation.

The Sunnah Method of Rami During Hajj
Sunnah method for rami: right hand, pebble on thumb nail, using index finger

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the sunnah method of throwing pebbles at the jamarat according to the Hanafi school and explain why it is considered sunnah muakkadah.

Core Idea
The sunnah method is to throw with the right hand, place pebble on the thumb nail, and flick with the index finger.

This passage explains the recommended (masnun) way to perform the stoning ritual (rami) during Hajj. While any valid method fulfills the obligation, the Hanafi school identifies a specific method that earns extra reward. The method uses the right hand, places the pebble on the back of the thumb, and employs the index finger to flick it—a practice that is more difficult but closer to the Prophet's ﷺ example.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is rami (stoning) at the jamarat. The Hanafi ruling is sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah), not fard or wajib.
This means the act is valid without following this method, but one loses the reward of the sunnah.
2
Describe the sunnah method
The method involves: (1) using the right hand, (2) placing the pebble on the back (nail side) of the thumb, (3) flicking it with the index finger.
The index finger (musabbihah) helps propel the pebble.
3
Understand the optional nature
Any method that delivers pebbles to the jamra is valid. The sunnah method is recommended but not obligatory.
Other methods (e.g., gripping with fingertips) also fulfill the stoning requirement.
4
Note the difficulty and merit
The text observes that this method is harder and the pebble does not travel far, yet it is still the sunnah—showing that following the sunnah sometimes involves extra effort.
The reward is greater even if the action is physically harder.
5
Recognize the authority level
This ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah corpus and is the mufta bihi (operative) position in the Hanafi school.
It is considered established sunnah from the Prophet's practice.

Source Text

This method complements the first method (gripping with fingertips) and is also considered recommended.

The Minimum Distance for a Valid Rami: Five Cubits
Minimum distance for valid rami

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum distance required for a valid rami and explain why a shorter distance invalidates the act.

Core Idea
Rami means throwing, not placing — five cubits ensure the action is a throw.

In this passage, the author clarifies one of the key conditions for the stoning ritual (rami) during Hajj. The text explicitly sets a minimum distance of five cubits between the worshipper and the jamrah. Why does this distance matter? Because the very meaning of rami is to throw with force; anything less would be mere placing, which does not fulfill the requirement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is rami (stoning the jamrah). The ruling is that a distance of five cubits between thrower and target is a condition for validity.
This is a shart (condition), not a rukn.
2
Understand the linguistic basis
Rami linguistically means to strike and throw. If the distance is too short, the action becomes wad' (placing) not ramy.
The author uses this linguistic distinction to justify the distance.
3
Recognize the consequence of violation
Throwing from less than five cubits invalidates the rami; it does not count as the required ritual act.
The pilgrim would need to repeat with proper distance or may incur a dam.

Source Text

ويكون بين الرامى وموضع السقوط خمسة اذرع. 
ترجمه : (۱۳۵۹) رمی کرنے والے اور گرنے کی جگہ کے درمیان پانچ ہاتھ کا فاصلہ ہو۔ تشریح : آدمی اور جمرہ کے درمیان تقریبا پانچ ہاتھ کا فاصلہ ہونا چاہئے ، پانچ ہاتھ کا فاصلہ ساڑھے سات فٹ ہوگا۔ اس سے کم فاصلہ سے کنکری مارے گا تو مارنا نہیں ہوگا وہ تو کنکری ڈالنا ہوگا ، اور رمی کا معنی مارنا اور پھینکنا ہے اس لئے ساڑھے سات فٹ کے فاصلے سے کنکری مارے۔
And there should be between the thrower and the place of falling five cubits. Translation: (1359) There should be a distance of five hand-lengths (cubits) between the thrower and the place of falling. Explanation: The distance between the person and the jamrah should be approximately five hand-lengths, which is 7.5 feet. If he throws from a shorter distance, it is not throwing but rather placing the pebble, and rami means to strike and throw, so he should throw from a distance of 7.5 feet.
Source pages p. 380

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the minimum distance for performing rami properly. The author states that there must be five cubits (approx 7.5 feet) between the thrower and the target. The reasoning is that rami (stoning) literally means hitting or throwing, not simply placing. If the distance is less, the action would be considered placing (wad') rather than throwing (ramy), and thus would not fulfill the requirement. The commentary specifies this distance as a condition for the validity of the act.

Key Terms
ذراع (dhira'): Cubit (approx 1.5 feet). Five cubits is about 7.5 feet.
الرمي (al-ramy): To throw or hit with force; distinguished from simply placing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the author give as the reason for requiring five cubits?
A) It is sunnah of the Prophet.
B) Rami means to strike and throw; a shorter distance would be placing, not throwing.
C) To avoid overcrowding.
D) It is a measure from the majority of scholars.

Key Takeaway
A valid rami requires the pebble to be thrown, not placed; therefore a minimum distance of five cubits is mandated.

Sunnah Method of Holding the Pebble for Rami
Ruling on the method of grasping the pebble for rami

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah method of holding the pebble for rami and explain the evidence from the hadith.

Core Idea
The sunnah method for rami is to hold the pebble between thumb and forefinger – easier and more humiliating for Shaytan.

In the Hajj ritual of rami (stoning the jamarat), the manner of holding the pebble is not arbitrary. The Hanafi school identifies a specific method as the sounder (asahh) based on the practice of the Prophet ﷺ. This lesson examines that method and its evidence from the hadith, clarifying its legal status as a sunnah muakkadah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
First, identify what act is being ruled upon. Here, it is the method of grasping the pebble for rami. The text explicitly states that the method is 'fi al-asahh' (the sounder view), indicating it is a recommended practice, not obligatory. Determine the hukm level: sunnah muakkadah.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a hadith from Abu Dawud. Identify the source and its chain. The hadith reports that the Prophet ﷺ had a stone between his fingers when throwing at Jamrat al-‘Aqabah.
Hadith reference: Abu Dawud, Bab fi Rami al-Jimar, no. 1967.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The operative phrase is 'between his fingers' (bayna asabi‘ihi). The Hanafi school uses this to infer that the Prophet held the stone with his fingers, specifically the thumb and forefinger, as that is the natural way to grasp a small object between two fingers. This becomes the evidence for the recommended method.
The hadith does not explicitly mention thumb and forefinger, but the method is derived from the general indication of using fingers.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
While the Hanafi school adopts this method as sunnah, other schools may not specify a particular grip or may consider any method valid. The text itself acknowledges that this is the 'asahh' (sounder) view, implying there are other views but this is preferred.
Cross-madhhab status: mukhtalaf fih.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The author explicitly marks this as the sounder view (fi al-asahh). The reasons given – ease and humiliation of Shaytan – further support its recommendation. Therefore, the mufta bihi (operative opinion) is that this is the sunnah method.
Tarjih authority: The text itself, as a reliable Hanafi source, settles on this view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۳۵۷) وكـيـفـيـة الـرمـى ان يأخذ الحصاة بطرف ابهامه وسبابته في الاصح لانه ايسر واكثر اهانة للشيطان. ترجمه : (۱۳۵۷) اور رمی کا طریقہ یہ ہے کہ کنکری کو انگوٹھے اور شہادت کی انگلی کے کنارے سے پکڑ کر پھینکے، اصح قول یہی ہے، اس لئے کہ یہ آسان ہے اور اس میں شیطان کی زیادہ اہانت ہے۔ تشـريح : رمی کرنے کے دو طریقے ہیں، [1] یہ پہلا طریقہ ہے کہ کنکری کو انگوٹھے کے کنارے سے اور شہادت کی انگلی سے پکڑے اور پھر پھینکے اس میں شیطان کی اہانت ہے اور پھینکنا آسان بھی ہے۔ وجه : (۱) عن سليمان بن عمرو بن الاحوص عن امه قالت رأيت رسول الله عليه الله عند جمرة العقبة راكبا و رأیت بین اصابعه حجرا فرمی و رمی الناس - ابوداود شریف، باب فی رمی الجمار، ص ۲۸۷، نمبر ۱۹۶۷) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ کنکری انگلیوں کے درمیان تھی ، جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ انگلیوں کے ذریعہ سے کنکری پھینکے۔
The manner of stoning is that he takes the pebble with the tip of his thumb and forefinger – this is the sounder view because it is easier and more humiliating for Satan. Translation: (1357) And the method of stoning is that he takes the pebble by the edge of the thumb and the index finger and throws it; this is the more correct statement because it is easy and contains more humiliation for Satan. Explanation: There are two methods of stoning. [1] This is the first method: he takes the pebble by the edge of the thumb and the index finger and throws it; in this there is humiliation for Satan and throwing is also easy. Proof: (1) From Sulayman ibn ‘Amr ibn al-Ahwas from his mother who said: I saw the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) at Jamrat al-‘Aqabah riding, and I saw a stone between his fingers, so he threw and the people threw. (Abu Dawud, Bab fi Rami al-Jimar, p. 287, no. 1967) This hadith indicates that the pebble was between the fingers, so it is understood that one throws the pebble by means of the fingers.
Source pages p. 380

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on the specific method of performing the stoning (rami) during Hajj. The author states the preferred (asahh) method: grasping the pebble between the tip of the thumb and the forefinger. Two reasons are given: it is easier for the thrower, and it demonstrates greater humiliation for Shaytan (Satan). The Urdu commentary elaborates that there are two methods; this first one is explained. The proof is a hadith from Abu Dawud where the Prophet ﷺ is seen with a stone between his fingers at Jamrat al-‘Aqabah, indicating that the stones are to be held and thrown using the fingers. The Hanafi position adopts this as the sunnah method.

Key Terms
حَصَاة (hasāh): A small pebble used for stoning the jamarat during Hajj.
رَمْي (ramy): The act of throwing pebbles at the jamarat pillars in the Hajj ritual.
إبهام (ibhām): The thumb, specifically the tip used to hold the pebble.
أَصَحّ (asahh): Sounder, more correct (used to indicate the preferred opinion among scholars).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the recommended (sunnah) way to hold the pebble for rami according to the Hanafi school?
A) Hold it in the palm of the hand
B) Hold it between the thumb and forefinger
C) Hold it between the index and middle fingers
D) Hold it using all five fingers

Key Takeaway
The sunnah method for rami is to hold the pebble between the thumb and forefinger, based on the Prophet's practice, and it is easier and more humiliating for Shaytan.
